Faraid — Inheritance

The Three States of the Uterine Brother's Share in Hanafi Faraid
Listing the three states of the uterine brother's share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three inheritance states of a uterine brother and identify when each applies, including the exclusions.

Core Idea
A uterine sibling inherits 1/6 if alone, 1/3 if multiple, and is excluded by a son or father.

Faraid rules for uterine siblings are distinct: they are fixed-share heirs, never residuaries. This lesson clarifies the three possible states of a uterine brother (or sister) based on the number of uterine siblings and the presence of certain closer heirs. Mastering these states is essential for correct distribution.

Guided Path
1
Classify the heir
Recognise that uterine siblings are fard (fixed-share) heirs, not asabah. They receive a Quranic share.
Uterine siblings share the mother but have different fathers.
2
Count the uterine siblings
Determine if there is one uterine sibling (brother or sister) or multiple (two or more, of any gender combination).
3
Check for exclusionary heirs
Identify if a son, son's son (grandson), father, or father's father (grandfather) exists. If any of these are present, uterine siblings are excluded (hajb hirman).
These are closer in relation to the deceased.
4
Apply the correct share
If not excluded: single uterine sibling gets 1/6; multiple uterine siblings share 1/3 equally among them.
The shares are fixed; no asabah for uterine siblings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ماں شریک بھائی کی حالتیں : تین ہیں۔
بطور عصبه
کس حالت میں کونسا حصہ ملے گا
(1) چھٹا حصہ ملے گا X 16.66 جب ایک بھائی ہو یا ایک بہن ہو
(۲) تہائی حصہ X 33.33 جب بھائی بہن دونوں ہوں یا دو بھائی یا دو بہن ہوں
(۳) ساقط ہو جائیں گے X بیٹا یا پوتا یا باپ یا دادا ہو
The states of the maternal (uterine) brother: three. As asabah? Not asabah. In which state which share will be given: (1) One-sixth will be given – X 16.66 – when there is one brother or one sister (i.e., single uterine sibling). (2) One-third – X 33.33 – when both brother and sister exist, or two brothers, or two sisters. (3) They are excluded – X – when there is a son, or grandson, or father, or grandfather.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on the uterine (maternal) brother's shares in Hanafi faraid. The uterine brother is a Quranic heir (dhū fard). Note: Unlike full or consanguine siblings, uterine siblings inherit only as fixed-share recipients, not as asabah. Three states: (1) A single uterine brother or sister receives 1/6. (2) If there are two or more uterine siblings (including one brother and one sister, or two brothers, or two sisters), they share 1/3 equally. (3) They are totally excluded if the deceased has a son, grandson, father, or grandfather. This is because these ascendants and descendants prevent uterine siblings from inheriting. The percentages 16.66 and 33.33 represent 1/6 and 1/3.

Key Terms
ماں شریک بھائی (maan shariq bhai): Uterine brother (same mother, different father).
تہائی (tehai): One-third (1/3) fixed share for multiple uterine siblings.
چھٹا حصہ (chhata hissa): One-sixth (1/6) fixed share for a single uterine sibling.
ساقط (saqit): Excluded from inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A deceased leaves a daughter and a uterine brother. What does the uterine brother receive?
A) 1/6
B) 1/3
C) Excluded
D) Residue after daughter

Key Takeaway
The uterine sibling's share depends on number: alone gets 1/6, multiple get 1/3, and they are totally excluded by a son, grandson, father, or grandfather.

The Husband's Two States in Faraid
Listing the two states of the husband's inheritance share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the husband's two possible fixed shares in faraid and identify which share applies based on the presence or absence of descendants.

Core Idea
Husband takes 1/2 without descendant, 1/4 with descendant – fixed share, never asabah.

This lesson introduces the husband's fixed shares in Islamic inheritance (faraid). The husband is a Quranic heir who always receives a predetermined fraction of the estate. His share depends solely on whether the deceased wife left any child or grandchild. Understanding these two simple conditions is essential for accurate estate division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Heir and His Category
Confirm that the deceased is a woman and the claimant is her husband. The husband is a fard (fixed-share) heir, never an asabah (residuary). This means he always takes a specified fraction, not the remainder.
The husband's share is derived from Quran 4:12.
2
Check for Descendants
Determine whether the deceased wife has any living descendants: son, daughter, grandson (son's son), or granddaughter (son's daughter). Only blood descendants in the direct line matter; grandchildren via a daughter are included? In Hanafi faraid, grandchildren through a daughter are not considered descendants for this purpose; only children and son's children count. (The source text includes 'pota' and 'poti' meaning son's children.)
Two conditions: no descendant → half; any descendant → quarter.
3
Apply the Correct Share
If no descendant exists, the husband receives half (1/2) of the entire estate. If at least one descendant exists, the husband receives one-quarter (1/4) of the estate.
The percentages 50% and 25% in the source are simplified reminders.
4
Confirm the Husband Does Not Take Residue
Even when there are no other heirs, the husband does not take the residue. Any residue after the husband's share goes to other fixed-share heirs or the public treasury (Bait-ul-Mal) if no residuaries exist.
Common mistake: assuming husband inherits everything when no child.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شوہر کی حالتیں : دو ہیں۔
حصے
بطور عصبه
کس حالت میں کونسا حصہ ملے گا
(1) آدھا ملے گا X 50 جب بیٹا، بیٹی ، ہوتا، ہوتی نہ ہوں
(۲) چوتھائی ملے گی X 25 جب بیٹا، بیٹی، یوتا، ہوتی میں سے کوئی موجود ہو
The states of the husband: two. Shares: As asabah? Not as asabah. In which state which share will be given: (1) Half will be given – X 50 – when there is no son, no daughter, no grandson, no granddaughter. (2) One-quarter will be given – X 25 – when there is a son, daughter, grandson, or granddaughter present.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on the husband's inheritance shares in Hanafi faraid. The husband is a fixed-share heir. Two states: (1) He receives half (1/2) of the estate if the deceased wife has no child or descendant (son, daughter, grandson, granddaughter). (2) He receives one-quarter (1/4) if there is any descendant. The husband does not take as asabah; he is always a fard heir. The percentages 50 and 25 represent 1/2 and 1/4.

Key Terms
آدھا (aadha): Half (1/2) – the husband's share when no descendant.
چوتھائی (chauthai): Quarter (1/4) – the husband's share when a descendant exists.
پوتا (pota): Grandson (son's son) – considered a descendant affecting husband's share.
پوتی (poti): Granddaughter (son's daughter) – considered a descendant affecting husband's share.
عصبه (asabah): Residuary heir – one who takes the remainder after fixed shares. The husband is not an asabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the husband's share if the deceased wife has a daughter?
A) 1/2
B) 1/4
C) 1/8
D) 1/6

Key Takeaway
The husband always takes a fixed share: 1/2 without any child or grandchild, 1/4 with any descendant.

The Three States of the Daughter's Inheritance Share in Hanafi Faraid
Listing the three states of the daughter's inheritance share.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three inheritance states of a biological daughter in Hanafi faraid and identify the applicable share in each scenario.

Core Idea
A daughter receives either half, two-thirds, or a variable residuary share depending on her situation.

In Hanafi inheritance law, a real daughter's share is not fixed in all cases. It changes based on the number of daughters and the presence of a son. This lesson presents the three fundamental states that every faraid practitioner must memorize.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The three scenarios are: single daughter with no son, two or more daughters with no son, and daughter(s) with son(s).
2
For each scenario, note the share
Single daughter: 1/2; two or more daughters: 2/3 equally; with son: daughter becomes asabah, taking half the son's share.
3
Understand the asabah rule
With a son, the daughter is not a fixed-share heir but a residuary heir (asabah bi-ghayriha), and her share depends on the residue.
4
Memorize the three states
Use the memorization anchor: half, two-thirds, and asabah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صلبی بیٹی کی حالتیں : تین ہیں۔
بطور عصبہ
کس حالت میں کون سا حصہ ملے گا
(1) آدھا ملے گا X 50 جب صرف ایک بیٹی ہو
(۲) دو تہائی ملے گی X 66.66 جب دو یا اس سے زیادہ بیٹیاں ہوں
(۳) اللہ کر مثل حظ الانثین X 33.33 جب بیٹے کے ساتھ ہو
The states of the daughter (real daughter): three. As asabah. In which state which share will be given: (1) Half will be given – X 50 – when there is only one daughter. (2) Two-thirds will be given – X 66.66 – when there are two or more daughters. (3) Allah... like the portion of two females – X 33.33 – when with a son.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on the daughter's inheritance shares in Hanafi faraid. Three states: (1) A single daughter receives half (1/2) of the estate. (2) Two or more daughters share two-thirds (2/3) equally. (3) When there is a son, the daughter does not take a fixed share but becomes an asabah bi-ghayriha (residuary through another), taking half of the son's share (i.e., the male gets double the female). The percentage 33.33 likely represents the daughter's share in that scenario (e.g., if residue is divided with son). The OCR phrase 'اللہ کر' is likely a misreading; it should be 'عصبہ کے طور پر' (as asabah).

Key Terms
صلبی بیٹی (sulbi bati): Real (biological) daughter.
عصبہ کے طور پر (asabah ke taur par): As a residuary heir, taking the residue after fixed shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What share do two daughters receive if there is no son?
A) 1/2
B) 2/3
C) 1/3
D) Entire residue

Key Takeaway
A daughter's share in Hanafi faraid is either 1/2 (one daughter), 2/3 (two or more), or the residuary share as asabah with a son where she takes half the son's portion.

Wife's Inheritance States
Summary of wife's fixed shares and multiple wives sharing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two inheritance shares of a widow and apply the rule of equal division among multiple wives.

Core Idea
A widow gets 1/4 with no child, 1/8 with child; multiple wives split that share equally.

In Hanafi faraid, the wife is a Quranic prescribed sharer. Her share depends solely on whether the deceased left any child or descendant. This lesson clarifies the two conditions and how to divide the share among multiple widows.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The wife's share is either 1/4 or 1/8 of the estate. The deciding condition is the presence of a child or descendant of the deceased.
The condition applies to any child (son or daughter) and also to grandchildren, though the text's mention of 'great-grandson' may be an OCR error.
2
Note the share for each scenario
When there is no child or descendant, the wife receives 1/4 (25%). When there is a child or descendant, she receives 1/8 (12.5%).
The percentages in the original text are reversed due to a typographical error; the correct percentages are as stated here.
3
Understand the inheritance of multiple wives
If the deceased had multiple wives, they collectively receive the same prescribed share (1/4 or 1/8) and then divide it equally among themselves.
The total share for all wives is fixed; it does not increase with the number of wives.
4
Apply the rule to a practical scenario
For a man with three wives and a son, each wife receives 1/24 of the estate (1/8 collective share ÷ 3 wives).
Verify that the presence of a descendant reduces the share to 1/8 before dividing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بیوی کی حالتیں : دو ہیں۔
بطور عصبہ
کس حالت میں کون سا حصہ ملے گا
(1) چوتھائی ملے گی (12.5%) جب بیٹا یا بیٹی یا پوتا، پوتی یا پر پوتا [؟] نہ ہوں
(2) آٹھواں ملے گا (25%) جب بیٹا یا بیٹی یا پوتا یا پوتی ہوں۔
ایک بیوی کو جتنا حصہ ملے گا چار ہو تب بھی اتنا ہی ملے گا۔ اور اسی میں چاروں کو تقسیم کر کے لینا ہوگا۔
States of the wife: two. As a residuary. In which state which share will be received: (1) one-fourth (12.5%) when there is no son, daughter, grandson, granddaughter, or great-grandson; (2) one-eighth (25%) when there is son, daughter, grandson, or granddaughter. Whatever share a single wife receives, if there are four, she still receives that same share, and the four must divide it among themselves.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage states the inheritance share of a widow. The author lists two states. First, if the deceased husband leaves no child or descendant (son, daughter, grandson, granddaughter, or great-grandson), the wife is entitled to one-fourth of the estate. Second, if any such descendant exists, her share is reduced to one-eighth. The note clarifies that if there are multiple wives, they collectively receive the same prescribed share (1/4 or 1/8) and then divide it equally among themselves. The heading 'بطور عصبہ' (as residuary) is again a misnomer because the wife is a Quranic prescribed sharer, not a residuary. The percentages in parentheses contain an apparent inversion: 12.5% corresponds to 1/8, and 25% corresponds to 1/4, so logically the first state (no child) should be 25%, and the second (with child) should be 12.5%. This is likely a typographical error in the OCR or original. The rule is well-established in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
بیوی (biwi): Wife of the deceased man; a Quranic prescribed sharer in inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A deceased man leaves three wives and one son. What share does each wife receive?
A) 1/24 of the estate each
B) 1/6 of the estate each
C) 1/8 of the estate each
D) 1/4 of the estate each

Key Takeaway
The wife's inheritance is a fixed Quranic right: 1/4 without child, 1/8 with child, divided equally among co-wives.

Granddaughter's Six Inheritance States
Summary of granddaughter's shares with various combinations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six inheritance states of the granddaughter (son's daughter) in Hanafi law and determine her share in each scenario.

Core Idea
The granddaughter inherits like a daughter when no daughter exists, but is excluded by a son or reduced by multiple daughters.

This passage is a concise memorization anchor summarizing all six possible inheritance states for the son's daughter (granddaughter). Understanding these states is essential for calculating shares in cases where both daughters and granddaughters survive. The rules mirror those of daughters, adjusted under Hanafi law for the presence of a grandson.

Guided Path
1
Identify the presence of daughters
Check how many daughters (if any) survive the deceased. The daughter's presence and number determine the granddaughter's base entitlement as a Quranic sharer.
Daughters' shares: one daughter gets 1/2, two or more get 2/3.
2
Identify the presence of a son or grandson
A son excludes all granddaughters entirely. A grandson (son's son) makes the granddaughter an asaba (residuary) with him, inheriting what remains after fixed shares.
Grandson's effect: with a grandson present, the granddaughter becomes asaba, not a fixed sharer.
3
Recall the six states
Memorize each state: (1) 1/2 – one granddaughter, no daughter; (2) 2/3 – two+ granddaughters, no daughter; (3) 1/6 – one daughter present; (4) 0 – two+ daughters; (5) asaba residue – with a grandson and any number of daughters; (6) 0 – son present.
State (5) is often misunderstood: with a grandson, the granddaughter takes the residue as asaba, not a fixed share.
4
Apply the rules
Given a specific scenario, identify the state by checking the presence and number of daughters, son, and grandson, then assign the granddaughter's share accordingly.
Practice with examples to solidify.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پوتی کی حالتیں : چھ ہیں۔
بطور عصبه
کس حالت میں کون سا حصہ ملے گا
(1) آدھا ملے گا (50%) جب ایک پوتی ہو اور بیٹی نہ ہو
(2) دو تہائی ملے گی (66.66%) جب دو یا اس سے زیادہ پوتیاں ہوں اور بیٹی نہ ہو
(3) چھٹا حصہ ملے گا (16.66%) جب صرف ایک بیٹی ہو اور پوتی ہو
(4) ساقط، کچھ نہیں ملے گا جب دو یا اس سے زیادہ بیٹیاں ہوں
(5) مابقی بطور عصبہ ملے گا (33.33%) جب دو بیٹیاں ہوں اور پوتی کے ساتھ پوتا ہو [؟]
(6) ساقط، کچھ نہیں ملے گا جب بیٹا موجود ہو
States of the granddaughter: six. As a residuary. In which state which share will be received: (1) half (50%) when there is one granddaughter and no daughter; (2) two-thirds (66.66%) when there are two or more granddaughters and no daughter; (3) one-sixth (16.66%) when there is only one daughter and a granddaughter; (4) excluded, nothing given when there are two or more daughters; (5) residue as residuary (33.33%) when there are two daughters and a grandson with the granddaughter [؟]; (6) excluded, nothing given when there is a son present.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage details the six possible states for a son's daughter (granddaughter) in inheritance. The first two states occur when there is no daughter: a single granddaughter gets one-half; two or more get two-thirds (the same as daughters). The third state: when there is one daughter, the granddaughter receives one-sixth to complete the two-thirds (daughters cannot exceed two-thirds; so one daughter takes 1/2, granddaughter gets 1/6). The fourth state: when there are two or more daughters, granddaughters are excluded because the daughters take the full two-thirds (the maximum fixed share for daughters). The fifth state is unclear: it mentions 'دو بیٹیاں ہوں اور پوتی کے ساتھ پوتا ہو' (two daughters and a grandson with the granddaughter). In standard Hanafi fiqh, if there is a grandson (germanus grandson), the granddaughter becomes an asaba with him, and the residue after the daughters' shares goes to them (grandson double granddaughter). However, if there are two daughters, they take 2/3, leaving 1/3 as residue for the grandson and granddaughter. The text assigns 33.33% to the granddaughter, which would be 1/3, but that seems to be the total residue, not her individual share. This may be an error in the OCR or original. The sixth state: the presence of a son excludes all granddaughters completely (the son takes precedence as a stronger residuary). This passage is a dense summary for memorization.

Key Terms
پوتی (poti): Granddaughter through son (son's daughter)
عصبہ (asabah): Residuary heir who inherits the remainder after fixed shares are distributed
ساقط (saqit): Excluded (not inheriting)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A deceased woman leaves one daughter and one granddaughter. What is the granddaughter's share?
A) 1/2
B) 1/6
C) Excluded (0)
D) 1/3

Key Takeaway
The granddaughter's share is determined by the presence and number of daughters and by the existence of a son or grandson, with six distinct states covering all possibilities.

Full Sister's Inheritance: Seven States
Summary of full sister's shares in various combinations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven inheritance states of the full sister and determine her share when given a list of surviving heirs.

Core Idea
The full sister's share depends on specific heirs: fixed sharer, residuary, or excluded.

This lesson summarises the seven possible states for a full sister in Hanafi inheritance. Understanding these rules is crucial for correct estate distribution. The full sister can inherit as a fixed sharer (1/2 or 2/3), become a residuary with a brother or with daughters/granddaughters, or be completely excluded by certain agnatic heirs.

Guided Path
1
Check for exclusion
If a son, grandson, father, or grandfather exists, the full sister is excluded (states 6 and 7).
These are agnatic heirs that block the sister entirely.
2
Check for a full brother
If a full brother is present, the sister becomes a residuary (asaba) with him, sharing the residue in a 2:1 ratio (male:female). This is state 3.
3
Check for two daughters or two granddaughters
If there are two daughters or two granddaughters (and no son/brother), the full sister becomes a residuary with them (asaba ma'a ghairiha) and takes the remaining one-third after their fixed share. This covers states 4 and 5.
This is a distinctive Hanafi position; Shafi'is do not allow this.
4
Assign fixed shares
If none of the above apply, the full sister takes a fixed share: one sister gets one-half (state 1), two or more get two-thirds (state 2).
These are Quranic shares from Surah an-Nisa 4:176.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ماں باپ شریک بہنوں کی حالتیں : سات ہیں۔
بطور عصبه
کس حالت میں کونسا حصہ ملے گا
(1) آدھا ملے گا (50%) اگر ایک بہن ہو
(2) دو تہائی ملے گی (66.66%) اگر دو یا اس سے زیادہ بہنیں ہوں
(3) للذكر مثل حظ الانثین ملے گا (33.33%) جب بہن کے ساتھ بھائی ہو
(4) مابقی تہائی بطور عصبہ ملے گا (33.33%) جب دو بیٹیاں ہوں
(5) مابقی تہائی بطور عصبہ ملے گا (33.33%) جب دو یا اس سے زیادہ پوتیاں ہوں
(6) ساقط، کچھ بھی نہیں ملے گا جب بیٹا یا پوتا ہو
(7) ساقط، کچھ بھی نہیں ملے گا جب باپ یا دادا موجود ہو
States of the mother-father sharing sisters (full sisters): seven. As a residuary. In which state which share will be received: (1) half (50%) if one sister; (2) two-thirds (66.66%) if two or more sisters; (3) for the male the equivalent of the share of two females (33.33%) when with a brother; (4) remaining one-third as residuary (33.33%) when there are two daughters; (5) remaining one-third as residuary (33.33%) when there are two or more granddaughters; (6) excluded, nothing when there is a son or grandson; (7) excluded, nothing when there is a father or grandfather present.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage enumerates the seven states for a full sister (german sister). First, if there is one full sister and no other siblings, she receives one-half. Second, if there are two or more, they collectively receive two-thirds. Third, if a full brother is present, the full sister becomes an asaba with him, taking half of what the brother takes (the residue is split 2:1, male:female). Fourth, when there are two daughters (and no son), the full sister becomes a residuary (asaba ma'a ghairiha, i.e., asaba with another female) and takes the remaining one-third after the daughters' two-thirds. Fifth, similarly with two or more granddaughters, the full sister takes the remaining one-third. Sixth, the presence of a son or grandson (agnatic descendant) excludes the full sister completely. Seventh, the presence of a father or grandfather (agnatic ascendant) also excludes the full sister. The percentages in parentheses for states (3)-(5) represent the residue portion (1/3) in those scenarios, not the sister's individual share if there are multiple sisters. This is a crucial memorization summary for Hanafi inheritance.

Key Terms
ماں باپ شریک بہن (maan baap shreeq behn): Full sister (sharing both mother and father)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A deceased woman leaves two daughters and one full sister. What is the full sister's share?
A) 1/6 of the estate
B) 1/3 of the estate
C) 1/2 of the estate
D) Excluded

Key Takeaway
The full sister's inheritance is determined by a hierarchy: exclusion by specific heirs, then asaba with brother or daughters, then fixed shares.

Uterine Sister's Shares and Exclusion
Memorization anchor for uterine sister's shares and exclusion rules.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the shares of uterine sisters in Hanafi faraid and identify the heirs who exclude them.

Core Idea
Uterine sisters are fixed sharers: 1/6 for one, 1/3 for two or more, and they are excluded only by descendants and male ascendants.

The uterine sister (maan shreeq behn) shares only the mother with the deceased. Her inheritance rights are prescribed in the Qur'an (4:12) for the kalalah case. This lesson clarifies the correct shares and the conditions of exclusion, correcting common errors found in the source text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heir category
Recognize that the uterine sister is a fixed sharer (fard) in Hanafi faraid. She does not inherit as an asabah (residuary) except in specific combinations with uterine brothers.
The source text incorrectly states she inherits as an asabah; actually, she takes a prescribed fraction.
2
State the share for one uterine sister
A single uterine sister receives 1/6 of the estate. This is the share when no other uterine siblings are present and no excluder exists.
The source correctly mentions 1/6 for one sister.
3
State the share for two or more uterine sisters
If there are two or more uterine sisters (with or without uterine brothers), they collectively receive 1/3, divided equally among them. Uterine brothers share equally with sisters in the 1/3.
The source text here is corrupt; it mentions 'one brother' getting 1/3, but a single uterine brother receives 1/6, not 1/3.
4
Identify the excluders
Uterine siblings are excluded (saqit) by the deceased's descendants (son, daughter, etc.) and by male ascendants (father, grandfather). They are NOT excluded by full siblings, consanguine siblings, or any other relatives.
The source text incorrectly lists full sister and brother as excluders. This is a common error.
5
Apply the rule to a simple case
Take an example: deceased leaves one uterine sister and one full sister. The uterine sister takes 1/6, and the full sister takes the residue (5/6) as asabah. The uterine sister is not excluded by the full sister.
This contrasts with the source's erroneous claim that a full sister excludes the uterine sister.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(1) چھٹا حصہ ملے گا (16.66%) اگر ایک بہن ہو
(2) تہائی حصہ ملے گا (33.33%) اگر ایک بھائی ہو یا ایک بہن سے زیادہ ہوں [؟]
(3) ساقط، کچھ نہیں ملے گا اگر باپ شریک بہن یا حقیقی بہن یا ایک بھائی یا ایک بہن سے زیادہ ہوں [؟]

In which state which share will be received: (1) one-sixth (16.66%) if one sister; (2) one-third (33.33%) if there is one brother or more than one sister [؟]; (3) excluded, nothing if there is a father-sharing sister (full sister) or a real sister or one brother or more than one sister [؟].

Commentary
This passage attempts to summarize the states of uterine sisters (half-sisters sharing only the mother). The author lists three states. First, a single uterine sister receives one-sixth of the estate. Second, if there are two or more uterine sisters (or possibly a mix with a uterine brother), they share one-third. The text here is confusing: it mentions 'ایک بھائی' (one brother) getting one-third, but standard Hanafi law gives one uterine brother one-sixth. This may be an error. Third, the uterine sister is excluded (saqit) if there is a full sister? Actually, in Hanafi fiqh, uterine siblings are excluded by descendants (son, daughter) and by male ascendants (father, grandfather). They are not excluded by full siblings; rather, full siblings take the residue after the uterine siblings' shares. The text's mention of 'باپ شریک بہن' (full sister) as an excluder is likely incorrect. This passage appears to be a garbled summary and should be cross-checked with reliable sources.

Key Terms

Step-Granddaughter's Inheritance States
Listing six states for step-granddaughter's share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six states of the step-granddaughter's inheritance in Hanafi law and apply the appropriate share based on the presence or absence of daughters and sons.

Core Idea
The step-granddaughter's share varies from half to exclusion depending on the presence of daughters and sons.

This lesson outlines the six possible states of the step-granddaughter (poti) in Hanafi inheritance. Understanding these states is crucial for correctly distributing the estate among female descendants. The rules are derived from the Quranic verses on inheritance and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heir
The step-granddaughter (poti) is the paternal granddaughter, i.e., the daughter of the deceased's son.
2
Check the presence of daughters
The number of daughters (0, 1, 2 or more) determines whether the step-granddaughter receives a Quranic share or is excluded.
3
Check the presence of sons or step-grandsons
If a son of the deceased exists, the step-granddaughter is excluded (state 6). In state 5, the step-granddaughter inherits as asaba when accompanied by a step-grandson of the same degree.
State 5 is unclear in the original; the standard Hanafi interpretation requires a step-grandson to convert the step-granddaughter into an asaba.
4
Apply the share rule from the six states
Match the scenario to one of the six states: (1) half if alone, no daughter; (2) two-thirds if two or more step-granddaughters, no daughter; (3) one-sixth if one daughter present; (4) excluded if two or more daughters; (5) residue as asaba if two daughters and a step-grandson present; (6) excluded if a son exists.
5
Verify the exclusion conditions
The step-granddaughter is excluded in two states: when there are two or more daughters (they fulfill the two-thirds quota) and when a son exists (the son blocks all female descendants).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پوتی کی حالتیں : چھ ہیں۔
(1) آدھا ملے گا جب ایک پوتی ہو اور بیٹی نہ ہو۔
(۲) دو تہائی ملے گی جب دو یا اس سے زیادہ پوتیاں ہوں اور بیٹی نہ ہو۔
(۳) چھٹا حصہ ملے گا جب صرف ایک بیٹی ہو اور پوتی ہو۔
(۴) ساقط ، کچھ نہیں ملے گا جب دو یا اس سے زیادہ بیٹیاں ہوں۔
(۵) مابقی بطور عصبہ ملے گا جب دو بیٹیاں ہوں اور پوتی کے ساتھ [؟] ہو۔
(۶) ساقط ، کچھ نہیں ملے گا جب بیٹا موجود ہو۔
States of the step-granddaughter: six. (1) Half will be given when there is one step-granddaughter and no daughter. (2) Two-thirds will be given when there are two or more step-granddaughters and no daughter. (3) One-sixth share will be given when there is only one daughter and a step-granddaughter. (4) Excluded, nothing will be given when there are two or more daughters. (5) The residue as an asaba will be given when there are two daughters and with the step-granddaughter a [?] is present. (6) Excluded, nothing will be given when a son is present.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage enumerates the six states of the step-granddaughter (poti) in Hanafi inheritance law. The step-granddaughter is the daughter of a son (i.e., paternal granddaughter). She can inherit as a Quranic heir (fard) or as an asaba (residuary) under certain conditions. The first two states give her half or two-thirds when there is no daughter, as she takes the place of a daughter. The third state gives her one-sixth when there is one daughter, because the daughter gets half and the step-granddaughter gets one-sixth to complete two-thirds. The fourth state excludes her when there are two or more daughters, as they fulfill the two-thirds quota. The fifth state gives her the residue as an asaba when there are two daughters and a [?] (likely a son of the deceased? or a grandson? unclear). The sixth state excludes her when a son exists, because the son blocks all female descendants. These rulings are based on the Quranic verses on inheritance and the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the consensus of the Companions.

Key Terms
پوتی (poti): A step-granddaughter; the daughter of a son (paternal granddaughter).
بطور عصبہ (batur asaba): As a residuary heir, inheriting the remaining estate after Quranic shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The step-granddaughter's inheritance depends on the presence and number of daughters and the presence of sons.

The Eleven States of the Father's Inheritance with Sisters
Tabulation of father's inheritance shares with sisters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eleven states of the father's inheritance when sisters are present and identify the conditions determining each share or exclusion.

Core Idea
The father's share with sisters ranges from half to exclusion, determined solely by the type and number of co-heirs.

The father is a key Quranic heir, but his share fluctuates dramatically depending on which sisters survive the deceased. This lesson presents the complete classification of eleven scenarios, each with a distinct rule. Mastering this table is essential for accurately calculating faraid cases involving a father and sisters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories of father's shares
Group the eleven states into: half (state 1), two-thirds (state 2), one-sixth (state 3), residuary (states 5-6), and exclusion (states 4, 7-11).
Exclusion (saqit) means the father receives nothing.
2
Associate each category with its specific condition
For each share type, memorize the condition that triggers it. For example, half is given when only one sister is present; two-thirds when two or more half-sisters and no full sisters.
Conditions are listed in order in the source.
3
Note the residuary scenarios (states 5-6)
The father takes the remainder (asabah) when there are two full sisters with a full brother, or when two or more daughters are present.
In these cases, the father is not excluded but gets whatever is left after prescribed shares.
4
Understand the exclusion conditions (states 4, 7-11)
The father is excluded when: two full sisters alone; two or more granddaughters; a son or grandson; the deceased's father or grandfather; a full brother; a full sister/daughter/granddaughter who becomes a residuary heir.
Exclusion occurs due to the presence of a nearer male heir or a female who blocks him.
5
Practice applying the rules to sample cases
Given a set of heirs (father + specific sisters), determine which state applies and calculate the father's share accordingly.
Use the condition list as a lookup table.

Mother's Inheritance: The Eight States
Enumeration of mother's share under different combinations of heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight scenarios for the mother's share in inheritance and apply the conditions to determine her share.

Core Idea
The mother's share drops from one-third to one-sixth when children or multiple siblings exist.

Faraid is a precise science. The mother's share seems simple but has subtle conditions. In this lesson, you'll learn the eight states of the mother's inheritance share from the Hanafi matn. This enumeration is a classic memorization anchor, but understanding the underlying conditions is crucial for correct application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two possible shares
The mother receives either one-sixth (1/6) or one-third (1/3) of the estate. Recognize these two numbers as the only possible shares.
The share is never more than 1/3 and never less than 1/6 in the absence of blocking.
2
Learn the conditions for one-sixth
The mother takes 1/6 if there is a child (son/daughter), a grandchild through a son (even if only one), two or more full siblings, or two or more consanguine or uterine siblings. These four conditions correspond to the first four of the eight states.
Two siblings means at least two of the same category: two full brothers or two full sisters, etc.
3
Learn the conditions for one-third
When none of the one-sixth conditions exist, the mother normally takes 1/3 of the entire estate. However, if both a spouse (husband or wife) and the father are present, she takes 1/3 of what remains after the spouse's share. If a spouse and grandfather are present (but no father), she takes 1/3 of the total. These form the remaining four states.
State 8 may cover cases with no spouse or father: pure 1/3 of total.
4
Map the eight states to the headings
Go through the matn list: States 1-4 = 1/6 under conditions 1-4; States 5-6 = 1/3 after spouse's share with father; State 7 = 1/3 with spouse and grandfather; State 8 = 1/3 without any impediments (no child, no sibling, no spouse, no father).
This step solidifies the memorization anchor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷) ماں کی حالتیں : آٹھ ہیں۔
(۱) چھٹا حصہ
(۲) چھٹا حصہ
(۳) چھٹا حصہ
(۴) چھٹا حصہ

(۷) کل مال کی تہائی

- بیٹا یا بیٹی ہو
- پوتا یا پوتی، پر پوتا یا پر پوتی ہو
- حقیقی دو بھائی یا دو بہنیں ہوں
- علاقی یا اخیافی دو بھائی یا دو بہنیں ہوں
- اگر بیٹا یا پوتا یا دو بھائی یا دو بہنیں نہ ہوں اگر بیوی ہو تو اس کے لینے کے بعد اور باپ ہو

- اگر شوہر یا بیوی ہو اور دادا ہو
(7) States of mother: eight. (1) One-sixth. (2) One-sixth. (3) One-sixth. (4) One-sixth. (5) One-third of the total estate. (6) One-third of the total estate. (7) One-third of the total estate. (8) One-third of the total estate. Conditions: - There is a son or daughter. - There is a grandson or granddaughter, and a great-grandson or great-granddaughter. - Two full brothers or two full sisters. - Two consanguine or uterine brothers or two sisters. - If there is no son, grandson, two brothers, or two sisters, and there is a wife, then after her share, and there is a father. - If there is a husband, after his share, and there is a father. - If there is a husband or wife and a grandfather.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage lists eight scenarios for the mother's share as an heir. Generally, if the deceased has children (or grandchildren through a son), the mother receives one-sixth. If there are two or more siblings (full, consanguine, or uterine), she also gets one-sixth. When there are no children and fewer than two siblings, she receives one-third of the total estate. However, if the deceased also leaves a spouse (husband or wife) and a father, the mother's share is one-third of what remains after the spouse's share, not of the whole.

Key Terms
چھٹا حصہ (chhata hissa): One-sixth.
کل مال کی تہائی (kull maal ki thai): One-third of the entire estate.
حقیقی (haqiqi): Full sibling (same mother and father).
علاقی (ilaqi): Consanguine sibling (same father, different mother).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) When there is a husband and father.

Key Takeaway
The mother's share in Hanafi faraid is either one-sixth or one-third, determined by the presence of children, grandchildren, multiple siblings, and the combination of spouse and father/grandfather.

Paternal Grandmother's Three States in Faraid
List of paternal grandmother's inheritance conditions

By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three inheritance states of the paternal grandmother in Hanafi faraid and apply the conditions to determine her share or exclusion.

Core Idea
Paternal grandmother inherits one-sixth unless the mother is present, which excludes her.

In Hanafi inheritance law, the paternal grandmother has a fixed share but is subject to exclusion under specific conditions. This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri encapsulates her three states: receiving one-sixth, being excluded, or receiving one-sixth again. Understanding these states is essential for correct estate distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three states
List the three outcomes: (1) one-sixth, (2) excluded, (3) one-sixth. Each corresponds to a distinct condition.

2
Note the condition for each state
State 1: no mother present. State 2: mother present. State 3: grandfather present. Understand that state 3 occurs even if mother is absent? Actually text says when grandfather is present, she also gets one-sixth. Clarify that state 3 is an alternative scenario involving grandfather.
State 3: grandfather present (and mother absent? The text implies distinct condition).
3
Apply to a scenario
Given a deceased's heirs, check if mother is alive. If yes, paternal grandmother is excluded. If no, check if grandfather is alive. If no, she gets 1/6; if yes, she still gets 1/6 (per Hanafi ruling).
The grandfather does not exclude her.

Maternal Grandmother's Inheritance: Two States
Tabulation of maternal grandmother's inheritance rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the inheritance share of the maternal grandmother and identify the condition that excludes her.

Core Idea
A maternal grandmother inherits one-sixth unless the mother is alive, in which case she is excluded.

In this lesson, we examine the inheritance of the maternal grandmother (nani). The Hanafi school assigns her a share of one-sixth under specific conditions. However, she is completely excluded when the mother of the deceased is present. Understanding these two states is essential for correct faraid calculations.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the two states
The maternal grandmother has only two states: she either inherits one-sixth or is excluded entirely. There is no intermediate share.
2
Learn the condition for inheritance
She inherits one-sixth when the deceased's mother is not alive. This holds whether there is one maternal grandmother or multiple.
3
Learn the condition for exclusion
If the mother of the deceased is alive, the maternal grandmother is excluded and receives nothing.
Note: The mother excludes both paternal and maternal grandmothers.

Source Text

This passage covers the maternal grandmother's inheritance. She inherits one-sixth if she is alone or if there are multiple maternal grandmothers, provided the mother of the deceased is not alive. If the mother is present, the maternal grandmother is excluded and receives nothing.

The Rule: Male Takes Double the Share of Female
Statement of the rule that brother gets twice the sister's share when inheriting together.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a male heir inherits twice the share of a female when they are in the same category, and identify which categories this rule applies to.

Core Idea
In Hanafi faraid, when a male and female inherit together in the same degree, the male receives double the female's share.

This lesson introduces a fundamental principle of Hanafi inheritance law derived from the Quranic verse (4:11): 'to the male the equivalent of the portion of two females.' The rule applies specifically when a male and female heir belong to the same category—such as children, grandchildren, or siblings. Understanding this rule is essential for correct inheritance distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
State the principle: 'for the male is the share of two females.' This means the male gets twice what the female gets when they inherit together.
The rule is a general principle, not a specific share.
2
Recognize the applicable categories
The rule applies when the male and female are in the same category: sons and daughters, grandsons and granddaughters (from a son), or full/half-brothers and sisters (from the father's side).
It does not apply to uterine siblings or cross-category pairs like father and daughter.
3
Understand the condition of 'brother and sister'
The text specifies that the male and female must be 'real brother and sister to each other'—meaning they share the same father or both parents. Uterine siblings (same mother only) are not covered by this rule.
Uterine siblings inherit differently (each gets one-sixth if alone).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاعدہ : جب کبھی بھائی بہن دونوں حصے لینے والے ہوں تو للذ کر مثل حظ الانثین ہو جاتا ہے۔ یعنی بھائی کو دوگنا اور بہن کو ایک گنا۔ چاہے وہ دونوں میت کے لئے بیٹا اور بیٹی ہو یا پوتا اور پوتی ہو یا بھائی اور بہن ہو۔ البتہ یہ دونوں آپس میں بھائی اور بہن ہوں گے۔
Rule: Whenever a brother and sister both are taking shares, then for the male is the share of two females, i.e., the brother gets double and the sister gets single. Whether both are son and daughter of the deceased, or grandson and granddaughter, or brother and sister. However, they must be real brother and sister to each other.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This is a general rule of inheritance in the Hanafi school: when a male and female heir inherit together and are from the same category (e.g., children, grandchildren, siblings), the male receives twice the share of the female. This is derived from the Quranic verse 'to the male the equivalent of the portion of two females' (4:11). The rule applies specifically to cases where they are full siblings or half-siblings from the same father, but not to uterine siblings.

Key Terms
للذکر مثل حظ الانثیین (lil-dhakari mithlu hazzi al-unthayayn): For the male is the share of two females.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Any male and female heirs.
B) Only full siblings.
C) Sons and daughters, grandchildren, and siblings.
D) Only parents.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi faraid, when a male and female inherit together in the same category (children, grandchildren, or full/consanguine siblings), the male receives twice the female's share.

Shares of Paternal and Maternal Grandmothers
Table summarizing inheritance shares for dadi and nani under different conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which the paternal and maternal grandmothers inherit 1/6 in Hanafi faraid and identify the cases where they are excluded.

Core Idea
Both grandmothers inherit 1/6 when the mother is absent; the paternal grandmother is not excluded by the paternal grandfather.

This lesson summarizes the Hanafi rulings on the shares of paternal (dadi) and maternal (nani) grandmothers. Understanding these rules is essential for correctly distributing an estate when the deceased leaves a mother, father, or grandfather. The rules are derived from the Quran and hadith and are part of the fixed shares (fard) in inheritance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two grandmothers
Differentiate between the paternal grandmother (mother of the father, dadi) and the maternal grandmother (mother of the mother, nani). Their rulings differ slightly in certain conditions.
2
List the cases for the paternal grandmother
There are three cases: (1) When no mother exists, she receives 1/6. (2) When the mother exists, she is excluded (nothing). (3) When the paternal grandfather exists (and no mother), she still receives 1/6.
The presence of the paternal grandfather does not exclude her.
3
List the cases for the maternal grandmother
There are two cases: (1) When no mother exists, she receives 1/6. (2) When the mother exists, she is excluded (nothing).
The maternal grandmother is not affected by the presence of the maternal grandfather.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may exclude the paternal grandmother when the paternal grandfather is present, but the Hanafi school maintains she inherits 1/6 even with the grandfather.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Commentary
This passage presents the rulings for the shares of paternal and maternal grandmothers in inheritance. Actually, the table shows she gets 1/6 in two cases: when there is no mother (regardless of multiple grandmothers) and when there is a paternal grandfather (dada). She is excluded when the mother exists. For the maternal grandmother (nani), there are two cases: she receives 1/6 when there is no mother, and she is excluded when the mother exists. The ruling reflects the Hanafi position that grandmothers inherit only in the absence of the mother, and the paternal grandmother is not excluded by the paternal grandfather.

Key Terms
دادی (dādī): Paternal grandmother (mother of the father).
نانی (nānī): Maternal grandmother (mother of the mother).

C) When there is no mother, regardless of the paternal grandfather
D) When the maternal grandmother is also present

Key Takeaway
The paternal grandmother inherits 1/6 even with the paternal grandfather present, but both grandmothers are excluded when the mother is present.

Asabah: Definition, Proof, and Four Types
Definition, proof, and classification of asabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-asabah, cite its proofs from hadith and Quran, and classify any heir as one of the four types of asabah in Hanafi faraid.

Core Idea
The residue after fixed shares belongs to the nearest male relative, yielding four categories of residuary heirs.

This lesson opens the chapter on residuary heirs (asabah) in Hanafi inheritance law. We will define asabah, establish its proofs from the Sunnah and Quran, and then learn the four-fold classification that determines who inherits the residual estate. Understanding these categories is essential for computing shares correctly.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of asabah
Identify the key elements: asabah are paternal relatives who inherit the residue after fixed shares are distributed. The term 'asabah' is derived from 'asab' meaning to bind or surround, indicating their agnatic connection.
Asabah excludes uterine relatives and non-agnatic heirs.
2
Analyze the primary proofs (hadith and Quran)
Examine the hadith of Ibn Abbas commanding to give residue to the nearest male relative, and the Quranic verse in Surah Nisa (4:11) that implies the male gets double the female's share, indicating asabah inheritance.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Abu Dawood; the verse is the key textual basis for asabah bi-ghayrihi.
3
Identify and distinguish the four types of asabah
List the four types: bi-nafsihi (males inherently asabah), bi-ghayrihi (females with male counterparts), ma'a ghayrihi (females with female descendants when no male asabah), and bi al-sabab (emancipators). For each, note the conditions and examples.
Pay special attention to the examples given: daughter+son (bi-ghayrihi), sister+daughter (ma'a ghayrihi).

Source Text

باب العصبات .
باب العصبات
[٣٢١٦ ] (١) واقرب العصبات البنون ثم بنوهم ثم الاب ثم الجد ثم بنو الاب وهم باب العصبات کا
ضروریات عصبات عصبہ کی جمع ہے۔ اس کا ترجمہ ہے والد کے رشتہ دار، چونکہ یہ حصے لینے والے سب باپ کے رشتہ دار ہیں اس لئے ان کو عصبات کہتے ہیں۔ اس کا ثبوت اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال الحقوا الفرائض باهلها، فما تركت الفرائض فلا ولی رجل ذكر (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب اپنی عم احدهما اخ للام والآخر زوج بی، نمبر ۶۷۴۶ رابوداؤد شریف، باب فی میراث العصبة ص ۴۵، نمبر ۲۸۹۸) اس حدیث میں ہے حصے داروں کو حصے دید و پھر جو باقی بچے وہ مذکر عصبہ کو دیدو (۲) آیت میں بھی اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ يوصيكم الله في اولادكم للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين (ب) (آیت اا، سورۃ النساء ) اس آیت میں بیٹے کے لئے دو گنا اور بیٹی کے لئے ایک گنا بطور عصبہ ہے۔ اس لئے اس آیت میں عصبہ کو دینے کا اشارہ ہے۔
اقسام عصبات که
عصبات کی چار قسمیں ہیں (۱) عصبہ بنفسہ (۲) عصبہ بغیره (۳) عصبه مع غیره (۴) عصبہ بالسبب ۔ (۱) عصبه بنفسہ : جو لوگ خود بخود عصبہ ہوں کسی دوسرے کے بنانے کی وجہ سے نہ ہوں اس کو عصبہ بنفسہ، کہتے ہیں، ان میں بیٹا، پوتا، باپ دادا، بھائی، بھتیجا، چا، چازاد بھائی عصبہ ہیں۔
(۲) عصبه بغیره : خود تو عصبہ نہیں تھا لیکن بھائیوں نے اس کو عصبہ بنادیا اس لئے غیر کی وجہ سے عصبہ بن گئے ۔ اس لئے ان کو عصبہ بغیرہ کہتے ہیں۔ ان میں بیٹی بیٹے کے ساتھ ، پوتی پوتے کے ساتھ حقیقی بہن حقیقی بھائی کے ساتھ ، علاتی بہن علاتی بھائی کے ساتھ عصبہ ہیں ۔ ان لوگوں کو للذكر مثل حظ الانثیین ملے گا۔ یعنی مرد کو دو گنا اور عورت کو ایک گنا۔
(۳) مع غیرہ : یہ عورتیں خود تو عصبہ نہیں تھیں اور نہ کسی نے اس کو عصبہ بنایا۔ البتہ بیٹی نے یا پوتی نے اپنا اپنا حصہ لیا اور عصبہ مرد کوئی نہیں تھا تو حقیقی بہن نے یا علاتی بہن نے باقی مال آدھا یا ایک تہائی لیا۔ تو چونکہ بیٹی یا پوتی کے ساتھ عصبہ بنی ہے اس لئے ان کو عصبہ مع غیرہ کہتے ہیں۔ مثلا ایک بیٹی تھی اور ایک پوتی تھی۔ بیٹی نے آدھا لیا اور دو ثلث پورا کرنے کے لئے پوتی کو چھٹا دیا۔ باقی ایک تہائی بچی وہ بہن کو بطور عصبہ دیا۔ اس لئے بہن عصبہ مع غیرہ ہوئی۔
(۴) عصبه بالسبب : آزاد کرنے کے سبب سے آقا یا سیدہ غلام کے مال کا بطور عصبہ وارث بنے اس کو عصبہ بالسبب، کہتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ یہ نسب کی وجہ سے عصبہ نہیں بنے بلکہ آزادگی کے سبب سے عصبہ بنے۔ یہ دو قسم کے لوگ ہیں (۱) آزاد کرنے والا آقا (۲) آزاد کرنے والی سیدہ۔
Chapter on Asabah. (1) And the closest asabah are the sons, then their sons, then the father, then the grandfather, then sons of the father... Necessities: 'Asabat' is the plural of 'asabah'. Its translation is paternal relatives. Because these sharers are all paternal relatives, they are called asabah. Its proof is in this hadith: from Ibn Abbas, he said: 'Give the fixed shares to their owners, and what remains from the fixed shares belongs to the nearest male relative' (Bukhari, chapter...; Abu Dawood, chapter on inheritance of asabah). In this hadith: give the sharers their shares, then whatever remains, give it to the male asabah. (2) There is also an indication in the verse: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children: for the male, the share of two females' (Surah Nisa). In this verse, the son gets double and daughter gets one share by way of asabah. So this verse indicates giving to asabah. Types of asabah: There are four types: (1) Asabah bi-nafsihi (2) Asabah bi-ghayrihi (3) Asabah ma'a ghayrihi (4) Asabah bi al-sabab. (1) Asabah bi-nafsihi: Those who are asabah by themselves, not because of someone else, are called asabah bi-nafsihi. Among them are son, grandson, father, grandfather, brother, nephew, paternal uncle, cousin brother. (2) Asabah bi-ghayrihi: They are not asabah by themselves, but brothers made them asabah, so they become asabah because of others. So they are called asabah bi-ghayrihi. Among them are: daughter with son, granddaughter with grandson, full sister with full brother, consanguine sister with consanguine brother. These people will receive 'for the male, the share of two females', i.e., male gets double and female gets one. (3) Asabah ma'a ghayrihi: These women are not asabah by themselves, nor did anyone make them asabah. But when the daughter or granddaughter took their share and there is no male asabah, then the full sister or consanguine sister took the remaining property, half or one-third. Since they become asabah with the daughter or granddaughter, they are called asabah ma'a ghayrihi. For example, there was one daughter and one granddaughter. The daughter took half, and to complete two-thirds, the granddaughter was given one-sixth. The remaining one-third was given to the sister as asabah. So the sister became asabah ma'a ghayrihi. (4) Asabah bi al-sabab: By the reason of emancipation, the master or mistress inherits the property of the slave as asabah. This is called asabah bi al-sabab, because they do not become asabah due to lineage but due to the cause of emancipation. There are two types of people: (1) The male emancipator (master) (2) The female emancipator (mistress).
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on Asabah (residuary heirs). It begins with the definition: Asabah are paternal relatives who inherit the residue after the fixed (Quranic) shares have been distributed. The proof is from a hadith of Ibn Abbas (narrated by Bukhari and Abu Dawood) commanding to give fixed shares to their owners and the leftover to the nearest male relative, and from the Quranic verse in Surah Nisa (4:11) which prescribes for the male double the female's share, indicating that sons take as asabah. The passage then categorizes asabah into four types: (1) By themselves (bi-nafsihi): males like sons, fathers, brothers, etc., who are asabah inherently. (2) By another (bi-ghayrihi): females who become asabah when accompanied by a male counterpart, e.g., daughter with son, full sister with full brother; they inherit according to the 'for male double female' rule. (3) With another (ma'a ghayrihi): females who inherit as asabah in the presence of a female descendant like a daughter or granddaughter, when there is no male asabah; e.g., a full sister inherits the residue after the daughter and granddaughter take their shares. (4) By cause (bi al-sabab): the emancipator inherits as asabah from the freed slave due to the relationship of wala. This classification is fundamental to Hanafi inheritance law.

Key Terms
العصبات (al-ʿaṣabāt): Plural of asabah; paternal relatives who inherit the residue after fixed shares.
عصبه بنفسه (ʿaṣabah bi-nafsihi): A male relative who is inherently a residuary heir without needing another person, such as son, father, brother.
عصبه بغیره (ʿaṣabah bi-ghayrihi): A female relative who becomes asabah when accompanied by a male counterpart of the same degree, inheriting per the rule 'male gets double female's share'.
عصبه مع غیره (ʿaṣabah maʿa ghayrihi): A female relative who inherits as asabah in the presence of a female descendant (daughter or granddaughter) when there is no male asabah, e.g., sister inherits residue with daughter.
عصبه بالسبب (ʿaṣabah bi al-sabab): Residuary heir by cause of emancipation (wala), either the former master (male or female) inheriting from the freed slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of asabah applies when a full sister inherits the residue alongside a daughter of the deceased?
A) Asabah bi-nafsihi
B) Asabah bi-ghayrihi
C) Asabah ma'a ghayrihi
D) Asabah bi al-sabab

Key Takeaway
The residue after fixed shares goes to the nearest male relative; this principle yields four types of asabah: by self, by another, with another, and by cause.

Hierarchy of Residuary Heirs (Asabah) in Hanafi Faraid
States the hierarchical order of residuary heirs and the exclusion principle with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the order of the seven categories of asabah and apply the rule that a nearer residuary excludes all more distant ones.

Core Idea
A nearer asabah blocks all farther ones: son excludes grandson, father, brother, and beyond.

In this lesson, we examine the detailed ranking of residuary heirs in Hanafi inheritance law. The text enumerates seven categories in descending order, from the son down to the great-grandfather's brother. The key principle is that the nearest surviving residuary takes the entire residue; all others are excluded. This principle is derived from the Quranic verse on kalalah and from prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Enumerate the seven categories
List the seven residuaries mentioned: son, grandson, father, grandfather, brother, paternal uncle, father's paternal uncle.
Memorise this order as it is foundational.
2
Apply the exclusion principle
Understand that if a nearer residuary exists, the farther one inherits nothing from the residue. For example, a son excludes a grandson.
This is the central rule of asabah inheritance.
3
Trace the proof from the Quran
Analyse how Quran 4:176 conditions the sister's inheritance on the absence of a child, implying that a child (a nearer residuary) excludes more distant residuaries.
The verse uses 'in lam yakun lahu walad' (if he has no child).
4
Trace the proof from the hadith
The hadith 'Give the fixed shares to their recipients; what remains is for the nearest male relative' establishes that the residue goes to the nearest male relative in proximity.
This hadith is from Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
5
Recognise the structural relationships
Note the part/root connections: son is a part (juz') of the deceased, father is the root (asl), brother is part of the root, etc. This clarifies why proximity matters.
Understanding these relationships helps in remembering the order.

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الرابع
۴۱۵
باب العصبات
الاخوة ثم بنو الجد وهم الاعمام ثم بنو اب الجد ۳۲ (۲) واذا استوى بنو اب في
[۳۲۱۶] (۱) عصبوں میں سے قریب (۱) بیٹے ہیں (۲) پھر پوتے ہیں (۳) پھر باپ (۴) پھر دادا (۵) پھر باپ کے بیٹے وہ بھائی ہیں (۶) پھر دادا کے بیٹے وہ چاہیں (۷) پھر دادا کے باپ کے بیٹے جس کو دادا کے بھائی کہتے ہیں۔
اس عبارت میں سات قسم کے عصبات کو ذکر کیا ہے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ قریب والا عصبہ موجود ہو تو اس سے بعد والے کو کچھ نہیں ملے گا۔ مثلا بیٹا موجود ہو تو پوتا کونہیں ملے گا۔ اور پوتا موجود ہو تو باپ کو نہیں ملے گا۔ اور باپ موجود ہو تو دادا کونہیں ملے گا۔ اور دادا ہو تو بھائی کو نہیں ملے گا۔ اور بھائی ہو تو چچا کو نہیں ملے گا۔ اور چچا ہو تو دادا کے بھائی کو نہیں ملے گا۔
آیت میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ يستفتونك قل الله يفتيكم في الكلالة ان امرؤهلك ليس له ولد وله اخت فلها نصف ماترك وهو يرثها ان لم يكن لها ولد (الف) ( آیت ۱۷۶ سورۃ النسام ) اس آیت میں ہے کہ اولاد نہ ہو تب بہن کو ملے گا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اولاد جو قریب کا عصبہ ہو تو اس سے دور کے عصبہ کو نہیں ملے گا (۲) اور مذکر عصبہ کو دینے دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس عن النبي قال الحقوا الفرائض باهلها، فما تركت الفرائض فلا ولى رجل ذكر (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب اپنی عم احدهما اخ للام والآخر زوج ہیں، نمبر ۶۷۴۵ / ابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی میراث العصبة، ص ۴۵، نمبر ۲۸۹۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اصحاب فرائض کے دینے کے بعد جو بچے وہ مذکر عصبات کو دیئے جائیں گے۔
ان عصبات میں (۱) بیٹا جزومیت ہے اور فروع ہے (۲) پوتا جزو کا جزو ہے (۳) باپ اصل میت ہے (۴) دادا اصل کا اصل ہے (۵) بھائی اصل یعنی باپ کا جز ہے (۶) چچا اصل کے اصل کا جزو ہے یعنی باپ کے باپ کا بیٹا ہے (۷) اور دادا کا بھائی اصل کے اصل کے اصل کا جزو
ہے۔
ابي الزناد على معانی زید بن ثابت قال الاخ للام والاب اولى بالميراث من الاخ للاب ، والاخ للاب اولى بالميراث من ابن الاخ للاب والام و ابن الاخ للام والاب اولى من ابن الاخ للاب ، وابن الاخ للاب اولى من ابن ابن الاخ للاب والام الخ (سنن للمیتی باب ترتیب العصبات، ج سادس ہیں ۱۳۹۱ نمبر ۱۲۳۷۳) اس اثر میں عصبہ کی ترتیب بیان کی
گئی ہے۔
[۳۲۱۷] (۲) جب باپ کے بیٹے درجے میں برابر ہوں تو زیادہ مستحق وہ ہے جو ماں اور باپ دونوں کی طرف سے ہو۔
بھائی بہنوں کی تین قسمیں ہوتی ہیں (۱) بھائی اور بہن ماں میں بھی شریک ہوں اور باپ میں بھی شریک ہوں ان کو اعیان بنی الام کہتے ہیں ۔ اردو میں حقیقی بھائی حقیقی بہن کہتے ہیں۔ یہ دوسرے بھائی بہنوں سے زیادہ حقدار ہیں (۲) صرف باپ دونوں کے ایک ہو۔ اور ماں الگ الگ ہو جس کو علاتی بھائی یا علاتی بہن کہتے ہیں۔ اردو میں سوتیلا بھائی یا سوتیلی بہن کہتے ہیں (۳) صرف ماں دونوں کی ایک ہو جس کو
حاشیہ : (الف) لوگ آپ سے فتوی پوچھتے ہیں۔ اللہ تم کو کلالہ کے بارے میں فتوی دیتے ہیں کہ اگر آدمی ہلاک ہو جائے۔ اس کی اولاد نہ ہوا اور اس کی بہن ہو تو اس کے لئے ترکہ کا آدھا ہو گا۔ اور بھائی بھی بہن کا وارث ہو گا اگر اس کی اولاد نہ ہو (ب) آپ نے فرمایا حصے والوں کو حصے دو اور جو چھوڑ دے تو مذکر کے لئے ہے۔
Chapter of Asabah: brothers, then descendants of grandfather (uncles), then descendants of great-grandfather. (2) And when the sons of a father are equal in rank, the one from both mother and father is more entitled. [3216] (1) Among residuaries, the nearest are: (1) sons, (2) then grandsons, (3) then father, (4) then grandfather, (5) then sons of father (brothers), (6) then sons of grandfather (paternal uncles), (7) then sons of great-grandfather (father's paternal uncles). The meaning of this statement is that when a nearer residuary exists, the more distant does not receive anything. For example, if a son exists, the grandson gets nothing; if grandson exists, father gets nothing; if father exists, grandfather gets nothing; if grandfather exists, brother gets nothing; if brother exists, paternal uncle gets nothing; if paternal uncle exists, great-grandfather's brother gets nothing. There is an indication in the verse: 'They ask you for a ruling; say: Allah gives you a ruling concerning kalalah: if a man dies, childless, and he has a sister, then she gets half of what he leaves, and he inherits from her if she has no child' (Quran 4:176). This shows that when there is a child (a nearer residuary), the more distant residuary does not get anything. (2) The proof for giving to male residuaries is the hadith: from Ibn Abbas from the Prophet: 'Give the fixed shares to their recipients; what remains after the fixed shares is for the nearest male relative.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawud). This hadith shows that after giving the fixed shares, what remains is given to male residuaries. Among these residuaries: (1) son is part of the deceased and is a descendant; (2) grandson is part of a part; (3) father is the root of the deceased; (4) grandfather is the root of the root; (5) brother is part of the root (i.e., part of father); (6) paternal uncle is part of the root of the root (i.e., son of father's father); (7) great-grandfather's brother is part of the root of the root of the root. Abu al-Zinad on the meaning of Zaid ibn Thabit: 'The brother from mother and father has more right to inheritance than the brother from father only; and the brother from father has more right to inheritance than the son of the brother from father and mother; and the son of the brother from father and mother has more right than the son of the brother from father only; and the son of the brother from father only has more right than the son of the son of the brother from father and mother, etc.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Bab Tartib al-Asabat). This athar explains the order of residuaries. [3217] (2) When the sons of a father are equal in rank, the one from both mother and father is more entitled. Brothers and sisters are of three types: (1) brothers and sisters who share both mother and father; they are called a'yan bani al-umm; in Urdu, they are called real brother and real sister. They are more entitled than other brothers and sisters. (2) Those who share only the same father but different mothers; they are called 'allati brother or 'allati sister; in Urdu, step-brother or step-sister. (3) Those who share only the same mother but different fathers; they are called... (the text cuts off). Footnote: (a) People ask you for a ruling; Allah gives you a ruling concerning kalalah: if a man dies, childless, and he has a sister, then she gets half of what he leaves, and he inherits from her if she has no child. (b) He said: give the fixed shares to their recipients, and what remains is for the male.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on Asabah by detailing the order of priority among residuaries. The author enumerates seven categories in descending order of proximity: (1) son, (2) grandson (son's son), (3) father, (4) grandfather (paternal), (5) full brother (or half-brother from father), (6) paternal uncle (father's brother), (7) father's paternal uncle (grandfather's brother). The key principle is that a nearer residuary excludes all more distant ones; for example, if a son exists, no grandson or father inherits as residuary. This is supported by the Quranic verse on kalalah (4:176), which conditions the sister's inheritance on the absence of a child. Two hadiths are cited: the general command to give residue to the nearest male relative, and the specific order derived from the practice of Zaid ibn Thabit (recorded by Abu al-Zinad). The passage then introduces a second ruling (numbered [3217]) on equal rank: when two brothers are both eligible as residuaries (e.g., full brother and consanguine brother), the full brother (from both parents) takes precedence over the consanguine brother (from father only). The author elaborates on the three categories of siblings: full (ayn), consanguine (allati), and uterine (only through mother), though the third category is cut off. The footnote clarifies the Quranic verse used as proof.

Key Terms
حقیقی بھائی/بہن (ḥaqīqī bhā'ī/bahan): Full sibling sharing both parents; also called 'ayn (عین) in inheritance law.
علاتی بھائی/بہن (ʿallātī bhā'ī/bahan): Consanguine sibling sharing only the father; in Urdu 'step-brother/sister' from father's side.
اعیان بنی الام (aʿyān banī al-umm): Full siblings (literally 'the specific ones of the mother's children'), referring to those who share both parents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a deceased leaves a grandson (son's son) and a paternal uncle, who inherits as residuary according to the Hanafi order?
A) The grandson
B) The paternal uncle
C) Both share equally
D) Neither, the residue goes to the state

Key Takeaway
The order of residuaries is: son, grandson, father, grandfather, brother, uncle, great-uncle; a nearer one excludes all farther ones.

Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate
7 min
Priority of Full Siblings over Consanguine Siblings Among Asabah
Explains the priority of full siblings over consanguine siblings among residuary heirs of equal rank.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that among brothers of equal rank, the full brother takes precedence over the consanguine brother, and explain the proof from the practice of Zaid ibn Thabit.

Core Idea
Full blood is stronger: a full brother excludes a consanguine brother from the residue.

In the previous lesson, we learned the general hierarchy of residuaries. Now we examine a specific case: when two brothers are both residuaries at the same level, the one who shares both parents is preferred over the one who shares only the father. This ruling is based on the established practice of the Companion Zaid ibn Thabit and is unanimously upheld in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of siblings
Recognise that siblings are classified into full (ayn), consanguine (allati), and uterine (only through mother). Only full and consanguine siblings are residuaries; uterine siblings are dhawi al-arham.
Memorise the Arabic terms: a'yan bani al-umm, 'allati, and uterine.
2
State the rule of priority
When two brothers are both sons of the same father (equal rank), the full brother (sharing both parents) is more entitled to the residue than the consanguine brother (sharing only the father).
This applies even if both are equally distant from the deceased.
3
Trace the dalil
The primary proof is the athar (tradition) of Zaid ibn Thabit: 'The brother from mother and father is more entitled to inheritance than the brother from father.' This is recorded in Sunan al-Daraqutni.
Zaid ibn Thabit was the leading Companion in inheritance law.
4
Analyse the Hanafi reasoning
Full blood establishes a stronger connection to the deceased. The mother's side adds an additional link, making the full sibling a 'closer' relative in terms of lineage.
This reasoning is consistent with the principle of proximity.
5
Compare with other schools
The Shafi'i school generally agrees on the priority of full siblings over consanguine siblings, but classifies uterine siblings differently (as fixed-share heirs). The practical consequence is minimal for the rule itself.
The ikhtilaf here is about the classification of uterine siblings, not the priority between full and consanguine.

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on Asabah by detailing the order of priority among residuaries. The author enumerates seven categories in descending order of proximity: (1) son, (2) grandson (son's son), (3) father, (4) grandfather (paternal), (5) full brother (or half-brother from father), (6) paternal uncle (father's brother), (7) father's paternal uncle (grandfather's brother). The key principle is that a nearer residuary excludes all more distant ones; for example, if a son exists, no grandson or father inherits as residuary. This is supported by the Quranic verse on kalalah (4:176), which conditions the sister's inheritance on the absence of a child. Two hadiths are cited: the general command to give residue to the nearest male relative, and the specific order derived from the practice of Zaid ibn Thabit (recorded by Abu al-Zinad). The passage then introduces a second ruling (numbered [3217]) on equal rank: when two brothers are both eligible as residuaries (e.g., full brother and consanguine brother), the full brother (from both parents) takes precedence over the consanguine brother (from father only). The author elaborates on the three categories of siblings: full (ayn), consanguine (allati), and uterine (only through mother), though the third category is cut off. The footnote clarifies the Quranic verse used as proof.

Key Terms
حقیقی بھائی/بہن (ḥaqīqī bhā'ī/bahan): Full sibling sharing both parents; also called 'ayn (عین) in inheritance law.
علاتی بھائی/بہن (ʿallātī bhā'ī/bahan): Consanguine sibling sharing only the father; in Urdu 'step-brother/sister' from father's side.
اعیان بنی الام (aʿyān banī al-umm): Full siblings (literally 'the specific ones of the mother's children'), referring to those who share both parents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a deceased leaves a full brother and a consanguine brother, who inherits the residue according to Hanafi law?
A) The full brother
B) The consanguine brother
C) Both share equally
D) The residue is divided 2:1 in favour of the full brother

Key Takeaway
Among brothers of the same rank, the full brother (sharing both parents) is more entitled to the residue than the consanguine brother (sharing only the father).

Preference of Full Siblings over Paternal Half-Siblings in Inheritance
Explains the priority of full siblings over paternal half-siblings with a hadith and analogical extension.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that full siblings exclude paternal half-siblings from inheritance and extend this rule analogically to other agnatic relations.

Core Idea
Full siblings block paternal half-siblings from inheritance regardless of degree equality.

In Islamic inheritance, not all brothers are equal. When a deceased leaves both a full brother (same mother and father) and a paternal half-brother (same father, different mother), the full brother takes priority and excludes the half-brother. This lesson unpacks the hadith proof from ʿAlī and shows how the rule extends to uncles, nephews, and cousins.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario and ruling
The passage addresses a situation where two siblings are equal in degree (both are brothers from the same father), but one is a full brother and the other a paternal half-brother. The ruling: the full brother is more entitled and excludes the half-brother.
Equality in degree means both are ‘asabat (agnatic heirs) but with different strengths.
2
Understand the three sibling categories
The text defines three types: full siblings (aʿyān banī al-umm), paternal half-siblings (banī al-ʿallāt), and maternal half-siblings (akhyāfī). Memorize the Arabic terms and their Urdu equivalents.
Maternal half-siblings are dhū arḥām (uterine) in Hanafi and inherit only if no agnates exist.
3
Locate the dalīl (proof)
The hadith from ʿAlī: the Prophet decreed that full siblings inherit to the exclusion of paternal half-siblings. The key phrase is 'اعيان بنى الام يرثون دون بنى العلات'.
This is a hadith ahad (single narration), but accepted by Hanafi scholars as evidence.
4
Apply analogical extension (qiyas)
The author extends the rule: a full nephew excludes a paternal half-nephew, a full uncle excludes a paternal half-uncle, and so on. The underlying reason is the strength of blood tie through both parents.
This reflects the Hanafi principle that agnates are ranked by the closeness of their connection to the deceased.
5
Note the practical effect and cross-madhhab variation
The ruling affects who inherits when multiple siblings exist. Although other schools generally agree, the exact order may differ (e.g., Shafi’i also prioritizes full siblings).
In Hanafi, full siblings are treated as primary agnates; paternal half-siblings are secondary.

(2) When the sons (brothers) of the father are equal in degree, the one who is from both mother and father is more entitled. There are three types of brothers and sisters: (1) Those who share both the mother and the father; they are called aʿyān banī al-umm (full siblings); in Urdu, they are called ḥaqīqī brother and ḥaqīqī sister. They are more deserving than the other siblings. (2) Those who share only the father, and the mothers are different; they are called ʿallātī brother or sister; in Urdu, they are called sūtelā (step) brother or sister. (3) Those who share only the mother; they are called akhyāfī brother or sister, or mothersharing sibling. Full siblings (from both parents) are more entitled than step-siblings (paternal half). That is, if there is a full brother or sister, the step-brother or step-sister gets nothing. The proof is this hadith: ʿAlī said that the Messenger of Allah decreed that debts are paid before bequests, and that full siblings inherit to the exclusion of paternal half-siblings: a man inherits from his full brother, not from his paternal half-brother (Tirmidhi, chapter on inheritance of brothers from father and mother, p. 29, #2094). This hadith states that full siblings precede paternal half-siblings. This rule applies also to nephews, uncles, and cousins: a full nephew precedes a paternal half-nephew; a full uncle precedes a paternal half-uncle; a full uncle's son precedes a paternal half-uncle's son. Similarly, a paternal half-brother or sister precedes a maternal half-brother or sister; and a paternal half-uncle precedes a maternal half-uncle. (Explanation of terms: at istawā: equal in degree; awlā: more entitled.) Footnote: (a) ʿAlī said: He (the Prophet) decreed that debts are before bequests, and that full siblings inherit before paternal half-siblings; a man inherits from his full brother before his paternal half-brother.

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario: when two brothers from the same father but different mothers (paternal half-brothers) are equal in degree to full brothers, the full brother (from both parents) is preferred. The author categorizes siblings into three types: (1) full siblings (aʿyān banī al-umm) – having the same father and mother; (2) paternal half-siblings (ʿallātī) – same father, different mothers; and (3) maternal half-siblings (akhyāfī) – same mother, different fathers. The ruling is that full siblings exclude paternal half-siblings from inheritance; paternal half-siblings in turn exclude maternal half-siblings. The proof is a hadith from ʿAlī ibn Abī Ṭālib, which includes the general principle that full siblings inherit to the exclusion of paternal half-siblings. The author extends this rule analogically to other relations: a full nephew excludes a paternal half-nephew, a full uncle excludes a paternal half-uncle, and so on. The footnote reiterates the hadith's content. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that agnatic relations are prioritized by the strength of blood ties (through both parents). The terminology 'at istawā' (equal in degree) and 'awlā' (more entitled) are defined at the end.

Key Terms
اعيان بنى الام (aʿyān banī al-umm): Full siblings who share the same mother and father.
بنى العلات (banī al-ʿallāt): Paternal half-siblings who share the same father but have different mothers.
اخيافى (akhyāfī): Maternal half-siblings who share the same mother but have different fathers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Full siblings (aʿyān banī al-umm) always exclude paternal half-siblings (banī al-ʿallāt) from inheritance, and this priority extends to all agnatic relations by analogy.
