Male-Female Ratio Among 'Asabat: 2:1 Distribution
Ruling with proof: establishes the 2:1 ratio for male-female 'asabat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the shares of male and female 'asabat (son, daughter, grandson, granddaughter, brother, sister) using the 2:1 ratio derived from Quran 4:11 and apply it to a simple estate with a spouse.

Core Idea
When male and female 'asabat inherit together, the male takes twice the share of the female.

This passage from a Hanafi faraid text establishes the foundational rule for distributing the residue among male and female 'asabat. The author cites Quran 4:11 and provides a worked example involving a wife, son, and daughter. Understanding this ratio is essential for correct inheritance calculations whenever children or siblings survive as 'asabat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
Determine which heirs are 'asabat (male and female). Note that the female must become 'asabah bil-ghayr through a male of the same degree.
Example: son and daughter, brother and sister, grandson and granddaughter.
2
Locate the primary proof
Read the Quranic verse (4:11) cited in the text. Understand the explicit phrase 'للذكر مثل حظ الانثيين' that commands the 2:1 ratio for children.
The Hanafi school extends this to all 'asabat via qiyas.
3
Apply the rule to an example
Take the given estate: deceased leaves a wife (gets 1/8 fixed share), a son, and a daughter. Calculate the residue and divide it in a 2:1 ratio between son and daughter.
Residue = 1 - 1/8 = 7/8 of estate.
4
Perform the calculation
Convert the fractions to a common denominator (e.g., 24) and distribute. Verify that the son gets 2/3 of residue and daughter gets 1/3.
Use the method of tashih if needed.
5
Generalize the principle
Understand that this ratio applies only when both male and female are 'asabat. If the female is not 'asabah (e.g., only daughter without son), she takes a fixed share and the residue goes to the male 'asabah alone.
The common misunderstanding is to apply the 2:1 ratio in all mixed-gender scenarios.

Source Text

(3) The son, grandson, and brother distribute to their sisters: for the male the share of two females. These four types of people are such that when a male and female inherit as 'asabah, the male gets double and the female gets one portion. (1) If a son and daughter of the deceased inherit, after the fixed-share recipients take their shares, the son gets double and the daughter gets one portion; these two are brother and sister to each other. (2) If a grandson and granddaughter inherit, after fixed shares, the grandson gets double and the granddaughter gets one portion; they are brother and sister to each other. The proof is in this verse: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children: for the male the share of two females' (Quran 4:11). In this verse, 'children' includes son, daughter, grandson, granddaughter, great-grandson, great-granddaughter. Therefore, whenever a male and female inherit as 'asabah, the male gets double and the female gets one portion. The calculation is as follows: Deceased has 100. Wife gets 12.5 (1/8). Residue is 87.5. Daughter gets 29.16 (one third of residue? Actually the calculation shows daughter 29.16 and son 58.33, so the ratio is 1:2). In this problem, one-eighth is given to the wife, which becomes 12.5. The remaining 87.5, from that one-third goes to the daughter? [The numbers indicate the correct division: daughter 29.16, son 58.33, which is a 1:2 split.]
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage addresses the distribution of inheritance among male and female 'asabat who are siblings or similar relations (son/daughter, grandson/granddaughter, brother/sister). The rule is that the male takes twice the share of the female, based on the Quranic verse 4:11. The author specifies four categories: (1) son and daughter, (2) grandson and granddaughter, (3) brother and sister? Actually the text mentions son, grandson, and brother as males who distribute with their female counterparts. It says 'son, grandson, and brother distribute to their sisters,' implying that these males, when inheriting as 'asabat alongside their female counterpart (sister, or for the son, the daughter, etc.), follow the 2:1 ratio. The verse from Surah Nisa is cited as the primary dalil, and the author explains that it encompasses all descendants (children, grandchildren, etc.). An example calculation is provided: a deceased leaves a wife (1/8), a son, and a daughter. After giving the wife her share, the residue is divided between the son and daughter in a 2:1 ratio. The numbers confirm: 87.5 residue, son gets 58.33 (2/3 of residue) and daughter gets 29.16 (1/3). The author's comment at the end clarifies the ratio. This is a straightforward application of the Quranic principle.

Key Terms
عصبة بالغير (ʿaṣabah bil-ghayr): A female who becomes an 'asabah through the presence of a male 'asabah of the same degree, e.g., daughter with son.

Key Takeaway
The male 'asabah inherits twice the share of the female 'asabah when they inherit together, as per Quran 4:11.

Priority of Full Siblings over Consanguine Siblings in 'Asaba
States the rule and hadith proof for full siblings precedence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that full siblings exclude consanguine siblings from 'asaba inheritance, identify the supporting hadith proof, and apply the same precedence to other 'asaba categories (nephew, uncle, uncle's son).

Core Idea
Full siblings exclude consanguine siblings from 'asaba inheritance.

This passage establishes a fundamental rule in Hanafi inheritance law: among agnatic heirs ('asaba), those who share both parents with the deceased (full siblings) take precedence over those who share only the father (consanguine siblings). The ruling is not a mere preference; it is an exclusion – the consanguine heir receives nothing when a full heir of the same category exists. The author supports this with a hadith from Tirmidhi and extends the rule analogically to other 'asaba like nephews and uncles. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly distributing the residue of an estate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs and their relationship
List all potential 'asaba heirs from the sibling category. Determine whether they are full (both parents) or consanguine (father only).
Uterine siblings (mother only) are not 'asaba; they are Quranic heirs in specific cases.
2
Apply the precedence rule among 'asaba
If a full sibling exists, the consanguine sibling is completely excluded from the 'asaba share. The full sibling takes the entire residue.
This is based on the hadith: 'A man inherits from his full brother more than from his half-brother (father only).'
3
Extend the rule to other 'asaba of the same degree
The same precedence applies between full and consanguine nephews, full and consanguine uncles, and full and consanguine uncle's sons. The full relative always excludes the consanguine relative of the same category.
The rule does not cross categories (e.g., a full nephew does not exclude a consanguine brother; degree matters).
4
Distinguish from uterine siblings
Uterine siblings (only mother shared) are not 'asaba and are governed by Quranic shares. Consanguine siblings, though 'asaba, are still preferred over uterine siblings if no full sibling exists.
The passage notes: 'Consanguine brother or sister takes precedence only over a half-brother or half-sister from mother's side.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب العصبات درجة فاولهم من كان من اب وام والابن وابن الابن والاخوة يقاسمون اخیافی بھائی یا اخیافی بہن کہتے ہیں ۔ یا ماں شریک بھائی بہن کہتے ہیں۔ ماں باپ شریک بھائی ، یا ماں باپ شریک بہن سوتیلے بھائی بہن سے زیادہ مستحق ہیں۔ یعنی اگر ماں باپ شریک بھائی یا بہن ہوتو سوتیلے بھائی یا سوتیلی بہن کو نہیں ملے گا اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن علی انه قال ... وان رسول الله الله قضى بالدين قبل الوصية وان اعیان بنی الام يرثون دون بنى العلات الرجل يرث اخاه لابيه وامه دون اخيه لابيه ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی میراث الاخوة من الاب والام ص ۲۹، نمبر ۲۰۹۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حقیقی بہن بھائی سوتیلے بہن بھائی سے مقدم ہوں گے ۔ یہ قاعدہ بھتیجا، چچا اور چچا کے بیٹے میں بھی چلے گا۔ یعنی حقیقی بھتیجا مقدم ہوگا سوتیلے بھتیجا ہے۔ اسی طرح حقیقی چا مقدم ہوگا سوتیلے چاہے۔ اور حقیقی چچا کے بیٹے مقدم ہوں گے سوتیلے چچا کے بیٹے سے۔ اسی طرح سوتیلے بھائی یا بہن مقدم ہونگے صرف ماں شریک بھائی یا ماں شریک بہن سے۔ اور سوتیلے چچا مقدم ہونگے صرف ماں شریک چچا ہے۔
Chapter of 'Asaba. Degree: The first among them is the one from father and mother. The son, son's son, and brothers divide. They are called paternal half-brother or paternal half-sister, or mother-sharing brother or sister. A full (father and mother) brother or full sister is more entitled than a consanguine (paternal half) brother or sister. That is, if there is a full brother or full sister, then the consanguine brother or consanguine sister will not get anything. Its proof is this hadith: 'From Ali that he said... the Messenger of Allah judged debts before the will, and that the sons of the mother inherit more than the sons of the paternal uncle; a man inherits from his full brother (father and mother) more than from his half-brother (father only).' (Tirmidhi, chapter on inheritance of brothers from father and mother, p. 29, no. 2094). In this hadith, full siblings take precedence over half-siblings. This rule also applies to nephew, uncle, and uncle's son: full nephew takes precedence over consanguine nephew, full uncle over consanguine uncle, full uncle's son over consanguine uncle's son. Similarly, a consanguine brother or sister takes precedence only over a half-brother or half-sister from mother's side, and a consanguine uncle takes precedence only over a half-uncle from mother's side.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the priority of 'asaba. It explains that among agnatic heirs, those who share both parents (full siblings) take precedence over those who share only the father (consanguine siblings). The commentary cites a hadith from Tirmidhi transmitted by 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) to establish this priority. The rule is extended analogically to other 'asaba: the same precedence applies between full and consanguine nephews, uncles, and uncle's sons. A consanguine heir is still preferred over a half-brother from the mother only (uterine sibling), but such uterine siblings are not 'asaba; they are Quranic heirs in specific cases. Thus, the Hanafi ruling is clear: full 'asaba exclude consanguine 'asaba of the same category.

Key Terms
عصبة (asaba): Agnatic heir who inherits via males; residuary after Quranic shares.
حقیقی (haqiqi): Full sibling: shares both father and mother with the deceased.
سوتیلا (sotala): Consanguine sibling: shares only father with the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a deceased leaves a full brother and a consanguine brother, who inherits as 'asaba?
A) The full brother inherits and the consanguine brother is excluded.
B) The consanguine brother inherits and the full brother is excluded.
C) Both inherit equally.
D) Both inherit but the full brother gets double the consanguine brother.

Key Takeaway
Full siblings (haqiqi) exclude consanguine siblings (sotala) from 'asaba inheritance, as proven by hadith and adopted by the Hanafi school.

Asaba bil-Ghayr: Male Takes Double Female's Share
Explains rule and Quranic proof for sons, grandsons, brothers sharing with sisters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of 'asaba bil-ghayr to distribute the residuary estate between male and female heirs in a 2:1 ratio, and cite the Quranic verses that establish this rule.

Core Idea
In 'asaba bil-ghayr, the male inherits double the female's share – a fixed ratio from the Quran.

When a male and female of the same category (e.g., son and daughter, brother and sister) inherit together as residuaries, their shares are not equal. The Quran explicitly commands that the male takes twice the share of the female. This lesson unpacks that rule from the two key Quranic verses and shows you how to apply it in real inheritance calculations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of 'asaba bil-ghayr
Recognize the four pairs where a female becomes a residuary through a male of the same degree: (1) son & daughter, (2) grandson & granddaughter, (3) full brother & full sister, (4) consanguine brother & consanguine sister.
Other combinations, e.g., paternal uncle with niece, do not create 'asaba bil-ghayr.
2
State the 2:1 rule
The underlying legal principle is 'lil-dhakari mithlu hazzi al-unthayayn' – the male receives double the share of the female when inheriting as 'asaba together.
This ratio applies only to the residuary portion after fixed shares are given.
3
Locate the Quranic proofs
Quran 4:11 (children) and Quran 4:176 (siblings) both contain the imperative 'للذكر مثل حظ الانثيين', which is the primary textual evidence. Confirm that these verses are qat'i in transmission and meaning (thubut and dalala both qat'i).
The Hanafi school applies these verses literally without exception to all 'asaba bil-ghayr situations.
4
Work through the numerical examples
Follow the two examples provided: (a) wife + son + daughter, and (b) wife + consanguine brother + consanguine sister. Trace how the fixed shares are first deducted, then the remainder is split 2:1 between the male and female 'asaba.
In example (a), wife gets 1/8; remainder 7/8 divided in ratio 2:1. In example (b), wife gets 1/4; remainder 3/4 divided 2:1.
5
Identify common pitfalls
Note that the rule applies to siblings (both full and consanguine), not just children. Also note that the sister does NOT have a fixed share in these cases; she is an 'asaba bil-ghayr.
A common mistake is to give the sister a fixed Quranic share (e.g., 1/2) when with a brother; that is incorrect.

Equal: of equal degree, higher: takes precedence. The son, grandson, and brother will divide by giving their sisters for the male the share of two females. These four types of people are such that when a male and female inherit as 'asaba, the male gets double and the female gets single share. (1) If the deceased's son and daughter inherit, after the shares of other fixed-share heirs, the son gets double and the daughter gets its single. And these two are brother and sister. (2) If the deceased's grandson and granddaughter inherit, after the shares of other fixed-share heirs, whatever remains, the grandson gets double and the granddaughter gets single. And these two are brother and sister. The proof is in this verse: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children: for the male, the share of two females.' (Quran 4:11). In this verse, 'children' includes sons, daughters, grandsons, granddaughters. So whenever a male and female inherit, the male gets double and the female gets single. The case works out as: Deceased: 100; Wife: 12.5; Daughter: 87.50; 29.16; 58.33. In this case, from 100, one-eighth is given to the wife which is 12.5, remainder 87.5; out of that, one-third to the daughter: 29.16, and two-thirds to the son: 58.33. The calculation for grandson and granddaughter is similar. If the deceased's full brother and full sister inherit, after the shares of fixed-share heirs, whatever remains, the brother gets double and the sister gets single. These two are brother and sister. If the deceased's consanguine brother and consanguine sister inherit, the brother gets double and the sister gets single. And these two are brother and sister. The proof for these two problems is in this verse: 'And if they are brothers and sisters, male and female, then for the male the share of two females.' (Quran 4:176). This verse says that when there are brothers and sisters, the male gets double and the female gets single. The case will be as: Deceased: 100; Wife: 25; Consanguine brother: 75; 50; +; Consanguine sister: 25. In this case, there are no children, so the wife gets one-fourth of 100, i.e., 25; the remainder is 75. Out of that, the brother gets double, i.e., 50; and the sister gets single, i.e., 25. The principle: when the inheritors are siblings (brothers and sisters), the rule of 'for the male the share of two females' applies. So the male gets double and the female gets single. These women are 'asaba bil-ghayr (residuaries through others).
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining the rule of 'asaba bil-ghayr (residuaries through another). It covers four categories: son and daughter, grandson and granddaughter, full brother and sister, and consanguine brother and sister. In each case, when a male and female inherit together as residuaries after the fixed shares, the male takes double the female's share. The proof is from two Quranic verses: 4:11 for children (including grandchildren) and 4:176 for siblings. The passage includes two worked examples. The first: a deceased leaves a wife, son, and daughter. The wife gets 1/8 (12.5), the remaining 87.5 is divided between son and daughter in a 2:1 ratio (son: 58.33, daughter: 29.16). The second: a deceased leaves a wife, and consanguine brother and sister (no children). The wife gets 1/4 (25), the remaining 75 is divided between brother (50) and sister (25) in a 2:1 ratio. Note that the brother and sister here are 'asaba bil-ghayr: the sister becomes a residuary through her brother. This is a distinctive feature of Hanafi inheritance law: sisters can become 'asaba when accompanied by a brother of the same degree.

Key Terms
عصبة بالغير (asaba bil-ghayr): A female who becomes an 'asaba (residuary) through the presence of a male of the same category (e.g., daughter with son).
للذكر مثل حظ الانثيين (lil-dhakari mithlu hazzi al-unthayayn): Legal principle: male gets double the female's share in specified inheritances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The 2:1 ratio for male to female 'asaba bil-ghayr is a fixed Quranic ruling applied to children, grandchildren, full siblings, and consanguine siblings.

Male 'Asaba Who Inherit Alone
States that male 'asaba (father, grandfather, etc.) inherit alone without female counterparts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the male 'asaba who inherit alone and apply the rule to determine which females do not become 'asaba bil-ghayr.

Core Idea
Only four male 'asaba make their female counterparts residuary; all others inherit alone.

In Hanafi inheritance law, 'asaba (agnatic heirs) are divided into two categories: those whose female counterparts become 'asaba bil-ghayr when inheriting together, and those who inherit alone. This passage clarifies the latter group—men like father, grandfather, nephew, uncle, and great-uncle who take the residue without any female sharing it. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly allocating shares in complex estates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exception
First, recall that only four male 'asaba cause their female counterparts to become 'asaba bil-ghayr: son, grandson, full brother, and consanguine brother. All other male 'asaba fall outside this exception.
This is the key distinction.
2
List the exclusive male 'asaba
From the passage, list the five categories that inherit alone: father, grandfather, nephew (brother's son), uncle (father's brother), and grandfather's brother (paternal great-uncle).
These are all 'asaba bi-nafsihi.
3
Apply the rule to examples
Work through each example: e.g., father inherits as 'asaba from son, but mother and father's sister do not. Verify that no female counterpart shares the residue.
The mother gets a fixed share (1/6) if a child exists; she never takes as 'asaba.
4
Understand the legal consequence
The practical effect: in distributions involving these male 'asaba, the residue after Quranic shares goes solely to the male. Females like mother, grandmother, niece, paternal aunt, or great-aunt never become residuaries.
Contrast with cases where a daughter inherits with a son (she becomes 'asaba bil-ghayr).

Other than these, from among the 'asaba, the men are alone in taking inheritance, not their women. Except for the son, grandson, full brother, and consanguine brother, all other 'asaba are such that the male takes as 'asaba. The women who are with them will not get anything. For example: the father takes as 'asaba from the son's property, but the mother does not take as 'asaba, nor does the father's sister (paternal aunt) take as 'asaba. (2) The grandfather takes as 'asaba from the grandson's property, but the grandmother or the grandfather's sister does not take as 'asaba. (3) The nephew takes as 'asaba from the uncle's property, but his sister (the niece) does not take as 'asaba from the uncle's property. (4) The uncle takes as 'asaba from the nephew's property, but his wife or his sister (the deceased's paternal aunt) does not take as 'asaba. (5) The grandfather's brother takes as 'asaba, but his sister (as if the grandmother) does not take as 'asaba. The conclusion is that when the father, grandfather, nephew, uncle, and grandfather's brother take as 'asaba, the women (their sisters) do not take as 'asaba along with them.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that identifies which 'asaba are 'asaba bi-nafsihi (residuaries by themselves) and that they inherit alone without female counterparts. It lists five categories: father, grandfather, nephew (brother's son), uncle (father's brother), and grandfather's brother (paternal great-uncle). These male 'asaba inherit the residue alone; their female counterparts (e.g., mother, grandmother, niece, paternal aunt, grandaunt) do not become 'asaba bil-ghayr. This contrasts with the four categories mentioned earlier (son, grandson, full brother, consanguine brother) whose sisters become 'asaba bil-ghayr. The passage serves to clarify the distinction: only specific male 'asaba cause their female counterparts to become residuaries; the rest are purely male 'asaba. This is important for calculating inheritance: when a father inherits as 'asaba, the mother does not share that residue; her share is fixed (1/6) if there is a child.

Key Terms
عصبة بالنفس (asaba bi-nafsihi): A male agnatic heir who inherits as 'asaba by virtue of his own relation, without needing another to make him residuary.
عصبة بالغير (asaba bil-ghayr): A female who becomes 'asaba because she inherits with a male of the same category (e.g., daughter with son).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Niece with nephew
C) Sister with full brother
D) Paternal aunt with uncle

Key Takeaway
Only four male 'asaba (son, grandson, full brother, consanguine brother) make their female counterparts residuary; all other male 'asaba inherit alone.

Sibling Inheritance: Brother Gets Double Sister's Share
States ruling and provides Quranic proof for sibling inheritance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares of siblings when they inherit as asaba, applying the Quranic 2:1 ratio.

Core Idea
Brother inherits double the sister's share when both are residuary heirs (asaba).

This passage presents the explicit Quranic ruling for sibling inheritance from Surah An-Nisa 4:176. When a brother and sister inherit together as residuary heirs (asaba), the brother takes twice the sister's share. This lesson examines the ruling, the proof, and a worked example. Understanding this principle is essential for accurate distribution of estates involving siblings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states: 'للذكر مثل حظ الانثيين' – for the male the like of the share of two females. This applies when siblings inherit as asaba, after the shares of fixed heirs (Quranic sharers) are distributed. Both full and half-siblings are included.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
The proof is from Surah An-Nisa 4:176: 'وان كانوا اخوة رجالا ونساء فللذكر مثل حظ الانثيين'. This verse explicitly prescribes the 2:1 ratio.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut (certain transmission) and qat'i al-dalalah (clear meaning).
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase 'فللذكر مثل حظ الانثيين' directly establishes that the male sibling receives double the share of a female sibling when they inherit together. This is a categorical command.
No need for further interpretation; the ruling is taken as is.
4
Work through the numerical example
The passage gives a case: deceased leaves wife (takes 1/4 = 25), remaining 75 is residue. The brother gets double the sister: brother 50, sister 25. This demonstrates the 2:1 ratio on the residue after fixed shares are deducted.
The example includes both full and half-siblings; the same ratio applies.
5
Note the classification of females
The passage states: 'These women are asaba bi-ghayrihim' – they become residuary heirs through the presence of a male sibling. Without a brother, the sister would not be asaba; here the male makes her a residuary heir.
This is a key principle: females become asaba bi-ghayrihim when a male sibling is present.

اخواتهم للذكر مثل حظ الانثيين [۳۲۱۹) دیا۔ اور اس کی دو تہائی یعنی 58.33 اٹھاون پوائنٹ تینتیس بیٹے کو دیا۔ اور پوتے اور پوتی کا حساب بھی اسی طرح بنے گا۔ [۳] میت کے حقیقی بھائی اور بہن وارث بنے تو حصے داروں کے حصے لینے کے بعد جو بچے اس میں سے بھائی کو دو گنا اور بہن کو ایک گنا ملے گا۔ میت دونوں آپس میں بھائی بہن ہوئے۔ [۴] میت کے سوتیلے بھائی اور سوتیلی بہن وارث بنے تو بھائی کو دو گنا اور بہن کو ایک گنا ملے گا۔ اور یہ دونوں آپس میں بھائی بہن ہیں۔ ان دونوں مسئلوں کی دلیل اس آیت میں ہے۔ وان كانوا اخوة رجالا ونساء فللذكر مثل حظ الانثيين (ب) (آیت ۱۷۶، سورۃ النساء ۴ ) اس آیت میں ہے کہ بھائی بہن دونوں ہوں تو بھائی کو دو گنا اور بہن کو ایک گنا ملے گا۔ مسئلہ اس طرح ہوگا۔ میت 100 بیوی حقیقی بھائی 25 سوتیلا بھائی 75 50 + حقیقی بہن سوتیلی بہن 25 اس مسئلے میں اولاد نہیں ہے اس لئے بیوی کو سو میں سے چوتھائی یعنی 25 دیا باقی 75 بچا۔ ان میں سے بھائی کو دو گنا یعنی 50 دیا اور بہن کو ایک گنا یعنی 25 دیا۔ اصول حصے لینے والے آپس میں بھائی بہن ہوں تو لاذ [؟] کر مثل حظ الانثمین ہو جاتا ہے۔ یعنی بھائی کو دو گنا اور بہن کو ایک گنا ملے گا (۲) یہ عورتیں عصبہ بغیرہ ہوئے۔
Their sisters: for the male the like of the share of the two females. [3219] Given. And its two-thirds i.e. 58.33 fifty-eight point thirty-three was given to the son. And the calculation of grandson and granddaughter will also be in the same way. [3] If the deceased's real brother and sister become heirs, then after the shares of the entitled ones take, from what remains, the brother will take two portions and the sister one portion. [4] If the deceased's half-brother and half-sister become heirs, then the brother will take two portions and the sister one portion. And both are brother and sister together. The proof of both these issues is in this verse: 'And if they are brothers, men and women, then for the male the like of the share of the two females' (Surah An-Nisa 4:176). In this verse it is that when both brother and sister are present, the brother gets double and the sister one portion. The case will be like this: deceased 100, wife 25, real brother 75, half-brother 50+, real sister, half-sister 25. In this case there is no child, so the wife is given one-fourth of the hundred i.e. 25, the remaining 75 remains. Out of that, the brother is given double i.e. 50 and the sister is given one portion i.e. 25. The principle: when the ones taking shares are brother and sister among themselves, then لاذ [؟] like the share of the two females applies, meaning the brother gets double and the sister one portion. (2) These women are 'asaba bi-ghayrihim.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran on the inheritance of siblings. It begins by stating the ruling: 'For the male the like of the share of the two females' – meaning when a brother and sister inherit together as residuary heirs (asaba), the brother receives double the sister's share. The commentary then gives a numerical example: a deceased leaves a wife, a full brother, a half-brother, a full sister, and a half-sister. The wife takes her fixed share (1/4), and the remaining 3/4 is divided among the siblings according to the 2:1 ratio. The proof is from Quran 4:176 which explicitly states this rule. This applies to both real (full) siblings and half-siblings. Note that these females become 'asaba bi-ghayrihim (residuary through male relative). The passage also hints that this principle applies similarly to other relationships like sons and daughters.

Key Terms
عصبہ (asabah): A category of heirs who inherit the residue after the Quranic sharers; male agnatic relatives such as father, brother, son, etc.
حظ الانثيين (hazz al-unthayayn): The share of two females; used to indicate the ratio where the male takes double the female's share.
عصبہ بغیرہ (asaba bi-ghayrihi): A female who becomes a residuary heir due to the presence of a male relative of the same category (e.g., sister becomes asaba with brother).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 1/4
B) 1/2
C) 2/3
D) 3/4

Key Takeaway
When a brother and sister inherit together as asaba, the brother receives double the sister's share, as prescribed by Quran 4:176.

Manumitter as 'Asaba When No Agnatic Relative
States the rule with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that the manumitter inherits as 'asaba in the absence of agnatic relatives and identify the supporting hadith (wala' belongs to the manumitter).

Core Idea
The manumitter inherits as 'asaba when the freed slave has no blood agnates.

In Hanafi faraid, the bond of clientage (wala') creates an inheritance right for the manumitter. This lesson explains that when a freed slave dies without any agnatic relatives, the manumitter – whether male or female – becomes the residuary heir and takes the entire estate. The ruling is based on a clear prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal rule
State the ruling: if the deceased (freed slave) has no agnatic relative by blood, the manumitter inherits as 'asaba (residuary heir). This is called 'asaba bi'l-sabab (by cause).
The rule applies only when there is no nasabi 'asaba.
2
Identify the proof (dalil)
Locate the hadith quoted: the Prophet (ﷺ) said, 'Indeed wala' belongs to the one who manumitted.' This is from Sahih al-Bukhari.
The hadith is ahad but accepted in fiqh.
3
Explain the inference (wajh al-dalalah)
Understand how the hadith proves the ruling: the phrase 'al-wala' liman a'taq' grants the manumitter the right of wala', which includes inheritance as 'asaba when the slave dies without agnates.
Wala' is a cause of inheritance, not a fixed share.
4
Distinguish 'asaba by cause from 'asaba by blood
Recognize that 'asaba nasabi (blood agnates) take priority. Only when none exist does the manumitter step in as 'asaba sababi.
If any agnatic relative exists, the manumitter does not inherit.
5
Apply to male and female manumitter
Note the rule applies equally whether the manumitter is a man or a woman; both become 'asaba through wala'.
This is a specific Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۲۲۰] (۵) اگر میت کا نسبی عصبہ نہ ہو تو آزاد کرنے والا آقا عصبہ ہوتا ہے۔ اس عبارت میں عصبہ بالسبب کا تذکرہ ہے۔ یعنی اگر نسبی عصبہ موجود نہ ہو۔ اور میت آزاد کردہ غلام تھا تو اس کا آقا جس نے آزاد کیا تھا وہ آزاد کرنے کے سبب سے عصبہ بنے گا۔ اور سارا مال وہ والد کے طور پر لے جائے گا۔ چاہے آزاد کرنے والا مرد یعنی آقا ہو یا آزاد کرنے والے عورت یعنی سیدہ ہو۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت اشتريت بريرة فقال النبى الله الله اشتريها فان الولاء لمن اعتق(الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الولاء لمن اعتق و میراث اللقیط ،ص ۹۹۹ نمبر (۶۷۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جس نے آزاد کیا اس کو غلام کا مال بطور عصبہ ملیگا۔
[3220] (5) If the deceased has no agnatic 'asaba, then the manumitting master is the 'asaba. This phrase mentions 'asaba by cause. That is, if an agnatic 'asaba is not present, and the deceased was a freed slave, then his master who freed him becomes 'asaba by reason of the manumission. And he takes all the property like a parent/descendant. Whether the manumitter is a man (master) or a woman (mistress). In a hadith: from 'Aisha (ra) who said: I bought Barirah, so the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Buy her, for indeed wala' belongs to the one who manumitted.' (Bukhari, Book of Wala', no. 675) In this hadith is that the one who manumitted receives the slave's property as 'asaba.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding wala' (clientage) as a cause of inheritance. It states that when a deceased has no agnatic (nasabi) 'asaba, then his former master who manumitted him becomes his 'asaba, inheriting all the property. This is called 'asaba by cause (asaba bi'l-sabab). The ruling applies whether the manumitter is male or female. The proof is the hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) told 'Aisha to buy Barirah because 'wala' belongs to the one who manumits.' The commentary clarifies that the master does not inherit as a fixed sharer but as an 'asaba, taking the entire residue.

Key Terms
ولاء (wala'): The bond of clientage between a freed slave and his manumitter, which gives the manumitter the right to inherit the freed slave's estate in certain circumstances.
عصبہ بالسبب (asaba bi'l-sabab): A residuary heir due to a legal cause (like wala') rather than blood relationship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The manumitter inherits as 'asaba when the freed slave has no agnatic relatives, by virtue of the bond of wala' established by the Prophet's hadith.

Nearest Male Relative of Manumitter Inherits Wala'
States rule for inheritance of wala' by nearest male 'asaba of the manumitter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who inherits wala' (clientage) from a freed slave and apply it to scenarios involving male and female manumitters.

Core Idea
Wala' inheritance follows the nearest male 'asaba of the manumitter; women only inherit if they personally manumitted.

This passage clarifies the inheritance of wala' after a slave is freed. The Hanafi school, relying on the practice of Companions, holds that the right of wala' passes to the nearest male agnatic relative of the manumitter, not to women unless they themselves are the manumitter. We will explore the ruling, the supporting evidence, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the inheritance of wala' after the manumitter's death. The ruling: the nearest male 'asaba inherits first, then the next nearest. Women do not inherit except as manumitters.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is an athar from Ali, Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, and Zayd ibn Thabit that they assigned wala' to the eldest/closest male 'asaba and did not give women inheritance unless they manumitted themselves.
The athar is from Sunan al-Baihaqi and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit practice of the Companions establishes that wala' belongs to the male 'asaba, and women are excluded. The wording 'الاكبر من العصبة' indicates proximity/order.
Hanafis interpret 'akbar' as 'closest' in order of inheritance, not age.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Maliki, Shafi'i) allow women to inherit wala' as 'asaba in some situations. The Hanafi position is stricter based on this athar.
The difference arises from differing interpretations of the same athar and other evidence.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: if a man frees a slave and dies, his daughter does not inherit wala'; his son does. In other schools, the daughter might qualify as 'asaba.
This impacts the distribution of the right of wala'.

Source Text

[3221] (6) Then the closest, then the closer from the manumitter's 'asaba. Women do not get a share from the 'asaba of the freed slave. Yes, if a woman manumitted, then the wala' goes to that woman. But for example, if the father manumitted a slave, then the wala' of the slave goes to the manumitter's son, not to a woman. And also, the male who is closest to the deceased among the 'asaba gets it first. If none, then the next. However, if wala' came through inheritance, then a woman can get it by inheritance. There is an athar from 'Ali, 'Abdullah, and Zayd ibn Thabit that they used to assign wala' to the eldest of the 'asaba and did not give inheritance to women unless they themselves had manumitted or the one they manumitted had manumitted. Another narration: 'Umar, 'Ali, and Zayd ibn Thabit did not give women inheritance from wala' except from what they themselves manumitted. (Baihaqi, Sunan) From this athar it is understood that a woman will not be an 'asaba inheritor of a slave manumitted by someone else. And from the previous athar it is also understood that the 'asaba will be in order, because the wording 'جعولون الولاء للكبر من العصبة' meaning the one who is foremost gets it first; if none, then the next. (2) The master himself inherits not by fixed share but as 'asaba by cause, so subsequent males also inherit as 'asaba.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (athar) detailing the inheritance of wala' after the manumitter's death. It states that the nearest male agnatic relative of the manumitter inherits the wala' as 'asaba, following the principle of proximity. Women generally do not inherit wala' from others, except when they themselves are the manumitter. The proof is from the practice of 'Ali, 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, and Zayd ibn Thabit, who assigned wala' to the eldest (or closest) male 'asaba and excluded women from inheriting wala' unless they had personally manumitted. This establishes that wala' inheritance follows the same order as agnatic 'asaba (nearest first), and that women are not 'asaba by wala' for slaves manumitted by others. The commentary also notes that if wala' becomes part of an inheritance (e.g., the manumitter dies and his heirs inherit his rights), a woman could potentially inherit wala' as part of general inheritance, but not as 'asaba directly.

Key Terms
الاكبر من العصبة (al-akbar min al-'asaba): The eldest or nearest male agnatic relative among the 'asaba; used here to determine who inherits wala'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The slave's own relatives

Key Takeaway
Wala' follows the nearest male 'asaba of the manumitter; women only inherit wala' if they personally manumitted.

Asabah through Wala': Manumitter Inheritance and Gender Rules
Explanation of asabah from wala' with hadith and athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on inheritance through wala', identify the primary dalil from hadith, and explain why women do not inherit wala' from relatives' freed slaves.

Core Idea
Wala' belongs to the manumitter, who inherits as 'asabah; women only inherit wala' they personally created.

In this lesson, we explore how a master who frees a slave becomes an agnatic heir ('asabah) when the freed slave dies without blood relatives. We will examine the hadith of 'Aisha and the Prophet ﷺ, as well as the athar from the Companions that restrict women's inheritance of wala'. Understanding this ruling is crucial for correctly applying the Hanafi law of inheritance in cases involving freed slaves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the opening sentence: if there is no agnatic relative by lineage, the manumitter becomes 'asabah. Note that this is inheritance 'by cause' (sabab), not by blood.
The ruling applies regardless of the manumitter's gender, but with important restrictions for women.
2
Locate the Primary Proof
Find the hadith from 'Aisha about Barirah. The Prophet ﷺ said: 'al-wala' liman a'taqa' (wala' belongs to the one who frees). Identify how this establishes the manumitter as heir.
The hadith is in Sahih al-Bukhari; it is an ahad hadith but with clear meaning.
3
Analyze the Proof's Scope
Understand that the hadith is general: the manumitter inherits as 'asabah. However, the Hanafi school restricts women's inheritance based on companion practice (athar). Consider the athar from 'Ali, 'Abdullah, Zayd, and 'Umar.
This step highlights the role of companion consensus (athar) in refining the general ruling.
4
Apply the Gender Restriction
From the athar, derive that a woman only inherits wala' if she herself freed the slave or if the slave was freed by someone she freed. She does not inherit wala' from her father's or brother's freed slave.
This is a distinctive Hanafi position; Shafi'is allow women to inherit wala' from any relative.
5
Synthesize the Complete Hanafi Position
Combine the ruling and restrictions: the manumitter or his male agnates inherit as 'asabah in order of proximity. Women inherit wala' only from their own manumitted slaves (or chain). Support with the hadith and the athar.
The mufta bihi position is clear: women do not inherit wala' from others.

آزاد کردہ غلام کے عصبات میں عورت کو حصہ نہیں ملتا ہے۔ ہاں ! عورت نے آزاد کیا تو وہ ولاء عورت کو ملے گا۔ لیکن مثلا باپ نے غلام آزاد کیا تو غلام کا ولاء آقا کے بیٹے کو ملے گا عورت کو نہیں ملے گا۔ اور یہ بھی ہے کہ جو مردمیت کے قریب کے عصبات ہیں اس کو سب سے پہلے ملے گا۔ وہ نہ ہو تو اس کے بعد والے کو ملے گا۔ البتہ اگر ولاء وراثت میں آ گیا تو وراثت کے اعتبار سے عورت کو مل سکتا ہے۔
اثر میں ہے۔ عن علی وعبد الله وزيد بن ثابت انهم كانوا يجعلون الولاء للكبر من العصبة ولا يرثون النساء الا ما اعتقن او اعتق من اعتقن (ب) دوسری روایت میں ہے۔ کان عمر وعلى وزيد بن ثابت لا يورثون النساء من الولاء الا ما اعتقن ( ج ) ( سنن بیہقی ، باب لا ترث النساء الولاء الا من اعتقن او احق من اعتقن ، ج عاشر ص ۵۱۵، نمبر ۲۱۵۱۲/۲۱۵۱۱ / مصنف ابن ابی هيبة ، ۹۷ فیمن ترث النساء من الولاء و ما هو؟ ، ج سادس، ص ۲۹۲، نمبر ۳۱۴۹۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت دوسرے کے آزاد کردہ غلام کی وارث بطور عصبہ نہیں ہوگی۔ اور اوپر کے اثر سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ عصبہ بھی ترتیب کے ساتھ ہوں گے ۔ کیونکہ اثر میں يجعلون الولاء للكبر من العصبة کا لفظ ہے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ جو مقدم ہو اس کو پہلے ملے گا۔ وہ نہ ہو تو اس کے بعد والے کو ملے گا (۲) خود آقا بطور فرض کے وارث نہیں ہوا ہے بلکہ سبب کے طور پر عصبہ ہو کر وارث ہوا ہے اس لئے بعد کے مرد بھی بطور عصبہ ہی وارث ہوں گے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا باندی کو خرید لولاء آزاد کرنے والے کے لئے ہوگا (ب) حضرت علی، حضرت عبداللہ اور زید بن ثابت ولاء عصبہ میں سے بڑے کے لئے کرتے تھے ۔ اور عورتیں ولاء کا وارث نہیں ہوگی مگر جس غلام کو خود آزاد کی ہو یا اس کے آزاد کردہ غلام نے آزاد کیا ہو اس ولاء کا وارث ہوگی ( ج ) حضرت عمر حضرت علی ، اور زید بن ثابت عورتوں کو ولاء کا وارث نہیں بناتے تھے مگر خود آزاد کی ہو تو اس ولاء کی وارث ہوگی۔
Chapter of Asabah. Males only, not their females. [3220] (5) And if there is no agnatic relative by lineage, then the asabah is the manumitting master. [3221] (6) Then the closest, then the closest from the asabah of the master. [Urdu: He will not get asabah. Minhum: besides them. [3220] (5) If the deceased has no agnatic relative by lineage, then the manumitting master is the asabah. This phrase mentions asabah by cause. That is, if no agnatic relative exists and the deceased was a freed slave, then his master who freed him becomes asabah due to the act of manumission and takes all the property as a father would, whether the manumitter is a male master or a female mistress. There is a hadith: 'Aisha said: I bought Barirah. The Prophet ﷺ said: Buy her, for wala belongs to the one who manumits.' (Bukhari, Chapter on Wala' to the Manumitter, p. 999 no. 675). This hadith indicates that the one who frees receives the slave's property as asabah. [3221] (6) Then the closest among the master's asabah. In the asabah of a freed slave, a woman does not get a share. Yes, if a woman freed, then wala belongs to her. But for example, if the father freed a slave, then the wala of the slave goes to the master's son, not to the woman. And also, whoever among the male agnates is nearest gets it first; if he is not there, then the next one gets it. However, if wala enters into inheritance, then women can inherit it by way of inheritance. There is an athar: from 'Ali, 'Abdullah, and Zayd ibn Thabit that they used to assign wala to the eldest of the asabah and did not let women inherit wala except what they themselves manumitted or what the one they manumitted manumitted. Another narration: 'Umar, 'Ali, and Zayd ibn Thabit did not make women inherit from wala except what they themselves manumitted. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter: Women do not inherit wala except from those they manumit or from the one they manumitted, vol. 10 p. 515 nos. 21512/21511; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 97, section on what women inherit from wala, vol. 6 p. 292 no. 31495). From this athar, it is understood that a woman will not be an heir as asabah of another's freed slave. And from the previous athar, it is also understood that asabah also have an order, because the athar uses the phrase 'they used to assign wala to the eldest of the asabah,' meaning that the one who is foremost gets it first; if he is not there, then the next one gets it. (2) The master himself does not inherit by prescribed share but inherits as asabah by cause; therefore, the subsequent males also inherit as asabah. Footnote: (a) He said: Buy the slave girl, for wala belongs to the one who frees. (b) 'Ali, 'Abdullah, and Zayd ibn Thabit used to give wala to the eldest among the asabah, and women do not inherit wala except from a slave they themselves freed or from a slave freed by the one they freed. (c) 'Umar, 'Ali, and Zayd ibn Thabit did not make women inherit wala except from those they themselves freed.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on asabah (agnatic heirs) discusses inheritance through wala' (clientage by manumission). The author first states the ruling: if the deceased has no agnatic relative by lineage (nasab), then the manumitter (mu'tiq) becomes the 'asabah and inherits all property. This is known as 'asabah bil-sabab (asabah by cause). The author then quotes a hadith from 'Aisha (ra) where the Prophet (saw) declared that wala' belongs to the manumitter. This is the primary proof. Next, the author clarifies that the order among the master's own asabah applies: the closest male agnate of the master inherits the wala' after the master. The commentary includes an important Hanafi ruling: women do not inherit wala' from others; they only inherit wala' from slaves they personally freed or from the chain of manumission starting from them. This is supported by athar from 'Ali, 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, Zayd ibn Thabit, and 'Umar. The passage also highlights that the asabah from wala' follows the same order of proximity as nasab asabah: the closest male takes precedence. This ruling is based on the principle that wala' is a right transferred by cause, not a fixed share (fard), and thus women cannot inherit it unless they are the cause themselves.

Key Terms
ولاء (wala'): The right of inheritance that a manumitter has over the estate of a freed slave who dies without agnatic heirs.
عصبة ('asabah): Agnatic heirs who inherit the residue of the estate after the Qur'anic sharers take their portions.
مولى المعتق (mawla al-mu'tiq): The manumitter (master) who frees a slave; becomes a mawla with the right of wala'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The manumitter inherits as 'asabah through wala'; women only inherit wala' they personally created, based on the hadith and companion athar.

Categories and Order of 'Asabah Heirs in Hanafi Faraid
Summary chart of asabah order and categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three categories of 'asabah and list the order of 'asabah bi-nafsihi heirs in Hanafi inheritance law.

Core Idea
The correct distribution of residue depends on knowing the precise hierarchical order of 'asabah.

In Hanafi inheritance law, after the Quranic sharers take their fixed portions, the residue (the remaining estate) goes to the nearest 'asabah (agnatic heir). This lesson unpacks a summary chart that classifies 'asabah into three categories: by themselves ('asabah bi-nafsihi), through another ('asabah bi-ghayrihi), and with another ('asabah ma'a ghayrihi). Mastering this hierarchy is essential for accurately distributing an estate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three main categories of 'asabah
Look at the chart and note the headings: 'asabah bi-nafsihi (عصبة بنفسه), 'asabah bi-ghayrihi (عصبة بغيره), and 'asabah ma'a ghayrihi (عصبة مع غيره). Understand the distinguishing feature of each: bi-nafsihi = male agnates inheriting solely by their own lineage; bi-ghayrihi = females who become 'asabah when accompanied by a corresponding male; ma'a ghayrihi = females who inherit as 'asabah in the presence of another female (e.g., daughter) without a male counterpart.
The chart also lists 'asabah through manumission (due to wala) separately.
2
Memorize the order of 'asabah bi-nafsihi
The chart provides a numbered list starting from son (1), grandson (2), great-grandson (3), father (4), grandfather (5), full brother (6), consanguine brother (7), full nephew (8), consanguine nephew (9), then uncles and their descendants. Learn the sequence: it follows the principle of proximity in lineage – closer in degree (e.g., son before father) and stronger in blood (e.g., full brother before consanguine brother).
Note: The chart includes numbering; some numbers repeated due to formatting, but the order is clear.
3
Understand 'asabah bi-ghayrihi conditions
These heirs (daughter, granddaughter, full sister, consanguine sister, niece) inherit as 'asabah only when a specific male counterpart is present. For example, daughter becomes 'asabah with son, granddaughter with grandson, sister with brother, etc. The chart lists these pairs. Without the male, these females are not 'asabah and may instead be Quranic sharers or excluded.
The chart lists 'niece (بھتیجی) with nephew? – this entry may require verification, but the principle is consistent.
4
Differentiate 'asabah ma'a ghayrihi
This category applies to full and consanguine sisters when there is a daughter or granddaughter. They inherit the residue after the daughter/granddaughter takes her fixed share. The chart lists four scenarios: after daughter, full sister; after daughter, consanguine sister; after granddaughter, full sister; after granddaughter, consanguine sister.
Note that 'asabah ma'a ghayrihi does not require a male counterpart; the presence of a female heir (daughter/granddaughter) elevates the sister to 'asabah status.
5
Recognize 'asabah through wala'
The chart ends with 'asabah through manumission: the manumitting master (or mistress) inherits as 'asabah if there are no blood agnates. This is a separate category based on patronage (wala) rather than lineage.
In practice, wala' is rare today but remains part of classical faraid.

In this chart, the order of asabah is explained. Asabah through another: (1) Daughter (when with a son). (2) Granddaughter (when with a grandson). (3) Sister (when with a brother). (4) Consanguine sister (when with a brother). (5) Niece (when with a nephew?). Asabah with another (these are sisters): (1) After taking the daughter, the full sister gets (the residue). (2) After the daughter takes, the consanguine sister gets. (3) After the granddaughter takes, the full sister gets. (4) After the granddaughter takes, the consanguine sister gets. Asabah through manumission: (1) The manumitting master. (2) The manumitting mistress.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This is a summary chart of the categories of asabah (agnatic heirs) in Hanafi inheritance law. It lists the heirs in order of priority. First, 'asabah bi-nafsihi (by themselves): they are male agnates who inherit without any intermediary. The order is: son, grandson (son's son), great-grandson, father, grandfather (paternal), full brother, consanguine brother, full nephew (brother's son), consanguine nephew, then uncles and their sons. Next, 'asabah bi-ghayrihi (through another): these are females who become 'asabah when accompanied by a corresponding male. Examples: daughter becomes 'asabah with son; granddaughter with grandson; full sister with full brother; consanguine sister with consanguine brother; niece with nephew? (the niece is listed but may require the presence of the nephew). Then 'asabah ma'a ghayrihi (with another): these are sisters who inherit as 'asabah when there is a daughter or granddaughter. For example, a full sister inherits the residue after the daughter takes her share. Lastly, 'asabah through manumission: the manumitter (master or mistress) inherits as 'asabah in the absence of agnatic relatives by lineage. The chart serves as a mnemonic for the complex order of 'asabah.

Key Terms
عصبة بنفسه ('asabah bi-nafsihi): A male agnatic heir who inherits the residue by virtue of his own male lineage, without needing any female to qualify him.
عصبة بغيره ('asabah bi-ghayrihi): A female who becomes an 'asabah due to the presence of a male counterpart (e.g., daughter with son).
عصبة مع غيره ('asabah ma'a ghayrihi): A female who inherits as 'asabah when there is another female (e.g., full sister with daughter) but no corresponding male.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi asabah order determines who inherits the residue; the chart organizes this hierarchy into three categories based on lineage and gender.

Faraid — Inheritance

Three Categories of Asabah in Hanafi Inheritance
Chart defining three categories of residuary heirs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three categories of asabah (bin-nafs, bi-ghayri, ma'a ghayr) and list the order of priority within bin-nafs.

Core Idea
Asabah are residuary heirs; their priority order is bin-nafs, then bi-ghayri, then ma'a ghayr.

In Hanafi inheritance, after the Quranic sharers take their fixed shares, the remainder goes to residuary heirs (asabah). These are divided into three categories: those who inherit by their own right, those who become residuary due to a male relative, and those who inherit as residuary alongside another female. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correct distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Recognize that asabah are classified into bin-nafs (by self), bi-ghayri (by another), and ma'a ghayr (with another). Each has distinct conditions.
Asabah bin-nafs includes all male relatives who inherit without needing another heir.
2
Define each category
Asabah bin-nafs: a residuary by virtue of own relation (e.g., son, brother). Asabah bi-ghayri: a female who becomes residuary due to a male of same degree (e.g., daughter with son). Asabah ma'a ghayr: a sister who inherits as residuary when a daughter or granddaughter takes her share.
Asabah bi-ghayri only applies to specified females: daughter, granddaughter, sister, consanguine sister.
3
List examples for each category
Bin-nafs: son, grandson, father, grandfather, full brother, consanguine brother, full nephew, consanguine nephew, etc. Bi-ghayri: daughter with son, granddaughter with grandson, sister with brother, consanguine sister with her brother. Ma'a ghayr: full sister with daughter, consanguine sister with daughter, full sister with granddaughter, consanguine sister with granddaughter.
The order within bin-nafs is based on closeness of lineage.
4
Memorize the priority order
The order of asabah bin-nafs from highest to lowest: son → son's son → father → grandfather → full brother → consanguine brother → full nephew → consanguine nephew → full paternal uncle → consanguine paternal uncle → etc.
This order is foundational for solving inheritance problems.

(1)
Chapter of Asabah. Asabah bin-Nafs: Shares. [List of entries with numbers]... Asabah bi-Ghayri: (18) Then paternal uncle? Asabah bin-Nafs: [more entries]... In this chart the order of asabah is explained. Asabah bi-Ghayri: (1) Daughter when son is present; (2) Granddaughter when grandson is present; (3) Sister when brother is present; (4) Consanguine sister when brother is present; (5) Niece? Asabah Ma'a Ghayr (these are sisters): (1) After daughter takes, full sister will get; (2) After daughter takes, consanguine sister will get. Asabah Ma'a Ghayr: (3) After granddaughter takes, full sister will get; (4) After granddaughter takes, consanguine sister will get. Asabah due to freeing: The master who freed; (2) The mistress who freed.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage presents a chart summarizing the order of residuary heirs (asabah) in Hanafi inheritance law. It is divided into three categories: Asabah bin-Nafs (heirs who inherit as residuaries by their own right), Asabah bi-Ghayri (heirs who become residuaries due to a male relative of the same degree), and Asabah Ma'a Ghayr (female heirs who inherit as residuaries in the presence of another female). The list under Asabah bin-Nafs includes the son, then grandson, then father, then grandfather, then full brother, then consanguine brother, then full nephew, then consanguine nephew, and so on. Under Asabah bi-Ghayri, a daughter becomes residuary when there is a son, a granddaughter with a grandson, a sister with a brother, and a consanguine sister with a consanguine brother. Under Asabah Ma'a Ghayr, a full sister inherits alongside a daughter, and a consanguine sister inherits alongside a daughter or granddaughter. The final section mentions asabah due to freeing (wala), where the master or mistress inherits from the freed slave.

Key Terms
عصبه بنفسه (asabah bin-nafs): A residuary heir who inherits by virtue of their own relation to the deceased, without needing another heir to make them residuary.
عصبه بغیره (asabah bi-ghayri): A female heir who becomes a residuary because she is accompanied by a male heir of the same degree (e.g., daughter with son).
عصبه مع غیرہ (asabah ma'a ghayr): A female heir who inherits as a residuary in the company of another female heir (e.g., full sister with daughter).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi inheritance, which of the following is an example of asabah ma'a ghayr?
A) A son inheriting as a residuary.
B) A daughter inheriting as a residuary when a son is present.
C) A full sister inheriting as a residuary after a daughter takes her share.
D) A grandfather inheriting as a residuary.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi asabah are classified into three types: bin-nafs, bi-ghayri, and ma'a ghayr, with a fixed order of priority that determines inheritance distribution.

Hajb in Hanafi Faraid: Types, Proofs, and the Mother's Reduction
Defines hajb, its types, and proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define hajb, distinguish between hajb nuqsan and hajb hirman, and apply the Hanafi rule for the mother's share reduction with its proofs.

Core Idea
Hajb prevents an heir from receiving a share or a larger share due to a closer heir.

This lesson explores the key inheritance principle of hajb (exclusion) from a classical Hanafi matn. You will learn the two types of hajb: nuqsan (reduction) and hirman (total exclusion), supported by clear Quranic and hadith evidence. The passage then applies these rules to the specific case of the mother's share, showing how her one-third is reduced to one-sixth by certain heirs.

Guided Path
1
Define Hajb and its Two Categories
Understand that hajb literally means prevention. In faraid, it is the prevention of an heir from receiving a share (hirman) or from receiving a larger share (nuqsan). The passage gives examples: the mother's reduction from 1/3 to 1/6 is hajb nuqsan; the exclusion of the granddaughter by two daughters is hajb hirman.
2
Identify the Proof for Hajb Nuqsan
The Quranic verse (Surah an-Nisa 4:12) on the husband's share is cited: his share is halved in the presence of a child, demonstrating reduction due to another heir. This is the evidence for the principle of hajb nuqsan.
The same principle is applied to the mother in verse 4:11.
3
Identify the Proof for Hajb Hirman
The hadith from Ibn Buraidah states the grandmother gets one-sixth only if there is no mother. If the mother exists, the grandmother is totally excluded. This is hajb hirman.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (dalala qati).
4
Apply the Rule to the Mother's Share
According to the matn, the mother is reduced from one-third to one-sixth by a child (son or daughter), a grandson (through a son), or two brothers. This is hajb nuqsan. The Quranic verse 4:11 is the evidence.
Only two brothers or more cause reduction; one brother does not.
5
Work Through a Sample Calculation
If the deceased leaves 100 units, a mother, and two brothers: the mother gets 1/6 (16.66), the two brothers divide the residue (83.33) equally. This illustrates the reduced share of the mother.
This example matches the footnote calculation in the passage.

ضروری نوٹ حجب کے معنی روکنا، اس باب میں یہ بیان کیا جائے گا کہ مثلا ماں کو اولاد نہ ہونے پر تہائی ملتی تھی لیکن اولاد نے ماں کو تہائی سے روک دیا اور چھٹا دلوایا۔ تو گویا کہ اولاد کی وجہ سے ماں محجوب ہو گئی ۔ یہ حجب نقصان ہوا۔ کیونکہ اولاد کی وجہ سے تہائی سے چھٹا ملا۔ اور اگر ایک بیٹی ہوتی تو پوتی کو چھٹا ملتا۔ لیکن دو بیٹیاں ہوں تو پوتی کو کچھ نہیں ملے گا تو دو بیٹیوں کی وجہ سے ہوتی محروم اور مجوب ہوگئی تو یہ حجب حرمان

حجب نقصان کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ ولکم نصف ماترك ازواجكم ان لم يكن لهن ولد فان كان لهن ولد فلكم الربع مماترکن (الف) (آیت ۱۲ سورۃ النساء۴) اس آیت میں اولاد نہ ہو تو شوہر کو آدھا دیا گیا۔ اور اولاد ہو تو انہوں نے شوہر کو نقصان دے کر آدھا سے چوتھائی پر لے آیا۔ تو اس میں حجب نقصان ہوا (۲) اور حجب حرمان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن بريدة عن ابيه ان النبي الله جعل للجدة السدس اذالم تكن دونها ام (ب) ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الجدة ، ص ۴۵، نمبر ۲۸۹۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ
ماں نہیں ہوگی تو دادی کو چھٹا ملے گا۔ مطلب یہ ہوا کہ مان ہو تو دادی محروم اور محجوب ہو جائے گی ۔ اس میں حجب حرمان ہے۔

Chapter of Hajb. [3222 (1)] And the mother is excluded from one-third to one-sixth by a child, or a child's child, or two brothers. Chapter of Hajb. Essential note: The meaning of hajb is prevention. In this chapter it will be explained that, for example, the mother used to get one-third when there was no child, but the child prevented the mother from one-third and caused her to get one-sixth. So the mother became mahjub (prevented) due to the child. This is hajb nuqsan (reduction). Because due to the child, she got one-sixth instead of one-third. And if there was one daughter, the granddaughter would get one-sixth. But if there are two daughters, the granddaughter gets nothing; so due to two daughters, the granddaughter becomes deprived and mahjub. This is hajb hirman (exclusion). The proof of hajb nuqsan is this verse: 'And for you is half of what your wives leave if they have no child; but if they have a child, then for you is a quarter of what they leave' (Surah an-Nisa 4:12). In this verse, when there is no child, the husband is given half, and when there is a child, it brings the husband down from half to quarter. So in this there is hajb nuqsan. (2) And the proof of hajb hirman is this hadith: From Ibn Buraidah from his father that the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordained one-sixth for the grandmother if there is no mother present (Abu Dawud). In this hadith it is that if the mother is not there, the grandmother gets one-sixth. The meaning is that if the mother is present, the grandmother is deprived and mahjub. In this there is hajb hirman. [3222] (1) The mother is excluded from one-third to one-sixth due to the presence of a son, or a grandson, or two brothers. If there is no son, grandson, or two brothers, the mother gets one-third. And if any of these is present, she gets a reduced one-sixth share. This is hajb nuqsan. Proof of this is in the verse: 'And for his parents, each of them has one-sixth of what he leaves if he has a child; but if he has no child and his parents inherit from him, then his mother gets one-third; but if he has brothers, then his mother gets one-sixth' (Surah an-Nisa 4:11). In this verse, if there is no child – and grandson is included in this – she gets one-third. And if there is a child, she gets reduced to one-sixth. Similarly, if there are no two brothers, she gets one-third; and if there are two brothers, she gets reduced to one-sixth. 'Ikhwah' is the plural of 'akh' meaning two brothers. The case will be like this: deceased 100, mother 16.66, two brothers 83.33. Footnote: (a) 'Whatever your wives leave, half is yours if they have no child; but if they have a child, then for you is a quarter.' (b) The Prophet said: 'For the grandmother is one-sixth if there is no mother.' (c) 'For each of the parents is one-sixth if the deceased has a child; then if he has no child, his parents inherit; then for his mother is one-third; and if he has brothers, then for his mother is one-sixth.'
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Hajb explains the concept of exclusion in Hanafi inheritance law. Hajb literally means prevention, and it operates in two ways: hajb nuqsan (reduction of share) and hajb hirman (total exclusion). The author first gives an example of hajb nuqsan: a mother normally gets one-third when there are no children, but if the deceased has a child, she is 'prevented' from the one-third and receives only one-sixth. This reduction is proven by the Quranic verse in Surah an-Nisa (4:12) regarding the husband's share, where the presence of children reduces his share from half to a quarter. Then the author gives an example of hajb hirman: a granddaughter would get one-sixth if there is only one daughter, but if there are two daughters, she gets nothing because the two daughters exclude her entirely. The proof for hajb hirman is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that a grandmother gets one-sixth only if there is no mother; if the mother is present, the grandmother is totally excluded. The author then presents the specific ruling about the mother's share from the matn: the mother is excluded from one-third to one-sixth by the presence of a child (son or daughter), a grandson (through a son), or two brothers. The Quranic verse at the beginning of Surah an-Nisa (4:11) is cited as evidence. The passage ends with a sample calculation where the deceased leaves 100, the mother gets 16.66 (one-sixth), and two brothers get 83.33 (the residue). The footnotes provide the full text of the cited verses and hadith.

Key Terms
حجب (hajb): Prevention of an heir from receiving a share or from receiving a larger share due to the presence of another heir.
حجب نقصان (hajb nuqsan): When an heir's share is reduced from a larger prescribed share to a smaller one due to the presence of another heir.
حجب حرمان (hajb hirman): When an heir is completely excluded from inheritance due to the presence of a closer heir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the cause for the mother's share to be reduced from one-third to one-sixth?
A) The presence of a brother
B) The presence of a child or a grandchild (through a son) or two brothers
C) The presence of the father
D) The presence of a sister

Key Takeaway
Hajb nuqsan reduces a share (e.g., mother from 1/3 to 1/6 by child or two brothers), while hajb hirman totally excludes an heir (e.g., grandmother by mother).

Hajb: Definition and Two Types
Defines hajb and its two types with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define hajb and distinguish between hajb nuqsan and hajb hirmān with textual evidence.

Core Idea
Hajb prevents heirs: reduction (nuqsan) or total exclusion (hirmān).

In this lesson we explore the concept of hajb (prevention) in Hanafi inheritance law. You will learn the two categories—hajb nuqsan and hajb hirmān—through clear examples and the Quranic and hadith proofs that establish them. Understanding hajb is essential for correctly calculating inheritance shares.

Guided Path
1
Understand the literal meaning
Hajb means prevention. In inheritance, an heir's presence prevents another from receiving their full entitlement.
2
Distinguish the two types
Hajb nuqsan reduces the share (e.g., mother from 1/3 to 1/6). Hajb hirmān excludes entirely (e.g., grandmother excluded by mother).
These are the two categories in Hanafi law.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence for nuqsan
Surah an-Nisa 4:12 shows the husband's share reduces from half to quarter when children exist.
This is the primary proof for reduction.
4
Examine the hadith evidence for hirmān
The hadith from Abu Dawud shows that the mother prevents the grandmother entirely.
This is the proof for total exclusion.
5
Apply the concepts to simple cases
Practice identifying which type of hajb occurs in given heir scenarios, such as mother with child (nuqsan) or grandmother with mother (hirmān).

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الححب
باب الحجب
ضروری نوٹ حجب کے معنی روکنا، اس باب میں یہ بیان کیا جائے گا کہ مثلا ماں کو اولاد نہ ہونے پر تہائی ملتی تھی لیکن اولاد نے ماں کو تہائی سے روک دیا اور چھٹا دلوایا۔ تو گویا کہ اولاد کی وجہ سے ماں محجوب ہو گئی ۔ یہ حجب نقصان ہوا۔ کیونکہ اولاد کی وجہ سے تہائی سے چھٹا ملا۔ اور اگر ایک بیٹی ہوتی تو پوتی کو چھٹا ملتا۔ لیکن دو بیٹیاں ہوں تو پوتی کو کچھ نہیں ملے گا تو دو بیٹیوں کی وجہ سے ہوتی محروم اور مجوب ہوگئی تو یہ حجب حرمان ہے۔
حجب نقصان کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ ولکم نصف ماترك ازواجكم ان لم يكن لهن ولد فان كان لهن ولد فلكم الربع مماترکن (الف) (آیت ۱۲ سورۃ النساء۴) اس آیت میں اولاد نہ ہو تو شوہر کو آدھا دیا گیا۔ اور اولاد ہو تو انہوں نے شوہر کو نقصان دے کر آدھا سے چوتھائی پر لے آیا۔ تو اس میں حجب نقصان ہوا (۲) اور حجب حرمان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن بريدة عن ابيه ان النبي الله جعل للجدة السدس اذالم تكن دونها ام (ب) ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الجدة ، ص ۴۵، نمبر ۲۸۹۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ماں نہیں ہوگی تو دادی کو چھٹا ملے گا۔ مطلب یہ ہوا کہ مان ہو تو دادی محروم اور محجوب ہو جائے گی ۔ اس میں حجب حرمان ہے۔
Chapter of al-Hajb. Necessary note: The meaning of hajb is to prevent. In this chapter it will be explained that, for example, the mother used to get one-third when there was no child, but the child prevented the mother from the one-third and caused her to get one-sixth. So it is as if the mother became mahjub (prevented) because of the child. This is hajb nuqsan (reduction), because due to the child she got one-sixth instead of one-third. And if there were one daughter, the granddaughter would get one-sixth. But if there are two daughters, the granddaughter gets nothing, so the granddaughter is deprived and mahjub because of the two daughters. This is hajb hirmān (total exclusion). The proof of hajb nuqsan is this verse: 'And for you is half of what your wives leave if they have no child; but if they have a child, then for you is a quarter of what they leave' (Surah an-Nisa 4:12). In this verse, if there is no child, the husband is given half; but if there is a child, it (the child) brings the husband down from half to a quarter. So in this is hajb nuqsan. And the proof of hajb hirmān is this hadith: From Ibn Buraidah from his father that the Prophet (peace be upon him) appointed for the grandmother one-sixth if there is no mother in her way (Abu Dawud, Book of al-Jaddah, p. 45, no. 2895). In this hadith, if there is no mother, the grandmother gets one-sixth; meaning that if there is a mother, the grandmother is deprived and mahjub. In this is hajb hirmān.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on hajb, a key concept in Hanafi inheritance law. The author first explains that hajb literally means 'prevention'. In inheritance, it refers to the effect of one heir preventing another from receiving their full share. The mother is the primary example: without children she receives one-third, but with a child she is reduced to one-sixth (hajb nuqsan). Similarly, a granddaughter is entirely excluded if there are two daughters (hajb hirmān). The author then provides textual evidence: for hajb nuqsan, Quran 4:12 shows how the husband's share reduces from half to a quarter when there are children; for hajb hirmān, a hadith from Abu Dawud shows that a mother prevents a grandmother from inheriting entirely. This establishes the two categories within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
حجب (hajb): Prevention: in inheritance, the effect of an heir's presence on another heir's entitlement, either reducing their share (nuqsan) or excluding them entirely (hirmān).
حجب نقصان (hajb nuqsān): Reduction: when an heir's presence causes another heir's share to decrease from a larger fixed share to a smaller fixed share (e.g., mother from 1/3 to 1/6).
حجب حرمان (hajb ḥirmān): Total exclusion: when an heir's presence causes another heir to be completely deprived of inheritance (e.g., mother excludes grandmother).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the difference between hajb nuqsan and hajb hirmān?
A) Hajb nuqsan reduces the share; hajb hirmān totally excludes.
B) Hajb nuqsan excludes; hajb hirmān reduces.
C) Both are the same.
D) Hajb nuqsan applies only to males; hajb hirmān to females.

Key Takeaway
Hajb in Hanafi inheritance law comprises two types: nuqsan (reduction) and hirmān (total exclusion), each supported by revealed evidence.

Mother's Hajb Nuqsan: When Her Share Reduces from 1/3 to 1/6
States the ruling that mother's share reduces from 1/3 to 1/6 due to son, grandson, or two brothers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a mother's inheritance share reduces from 1/3 to 1/6 in Hanafi faraid, apply hajb nuqsan, and calculate the resulting shares.

Core Idea
Mother's share drops to 1/6 if deceased leaves a child, grandson, or two brothers.

In Hanafi inheritance law, the mother generally receives one-third of the estate when there are no descendants and no multiple siblings. However, certain heirs 'block' her from that higher share, reducing it to one-sixth. This lesson examines the specific heirs that trigger this reduction, known as hajb nuqsan, and walks through the Quranic proof from Surah an-Nisa 4:11.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heir and the potential hajb
The mother is the primary heir. Determine if any of the three categories (child, grandson, two brothers) exist.
2
Locate the Quranic dalil
Surah an-Nisa 4:11 explicitly states the mother's shares: 1/3 if no child and no brothers, 1/6 if child or brothers exist.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalala.
3
Define key terms
Understand that 'walad' includes son, daughter, and son's child; 'ikhwah' means two or more brothers.
Hanafi interpretation extends walad to grandchildren via son.
4
Apply the rule
If any of these exist, mother gets 1/6; else she gets 1/3.
5
Calculate an example
Given estate value, compute mother's share and the residuary heirs' shares.
Example: estate 100, mother 1/6 = 16.67, two brothers get 83.33 as asabah.

[۳۲۲۲] (۱) وتحجب الام من الثلث إلى السدس بالولد او ولد الابن او اخوين.

[3222] (1) And the mother is prevented from one-third to one-sixth by a child, or a son's child, or two brothers. [3222] (1) The mother is mahjub (prevented) from one-third to one-sixth because of the existence of a son, or a grandson, or two brothers. If there were no son and no two brothers, the mother would get one-third. If any of these exist, she gets one-sixth instead of one-third. This is hajb nuqsan. The proof of this is in this verse: 'And for his parents, each of them gets one-sixth of what he leaves if he has a child; if he has no child and his parents inherit him, then his mother gets one-third; if he has brothers, then his mother gets one-sixth' (Surah an-Nisa 4:11). In this verse, if there is no child (and grandson is included in this), then she gets one-third; if there is a child, she gets one-sixth instead of one-third. Similarly, if there are no two brothers, she gets one-third; if there are two brothers, she gets one-sixth instead of one-third. 'Ikhwa' is the plural of 'akh' meaning two brothers. The case is as follows: Deceased 100, mother 16.66, two brothers 83.33. Footnote: 'What your wives leave...' etc.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage states a clear ruling from the chapter on hajb: the mother's share is reduced from one-third to one-sixth when there is a child (son or daughter), a son's child (grandson/granddaughter), or two or more brothers of the deceased. The author cites Quran 4:11 as proof, noting that 'walad' (child) includes grandchildren via the son. The term 'ikhwa' (brothers) in the verse means two or more brothers. An example calculation is given: with 100 units, the mother gets 16.67 (1/6) and the two brothers receive the remaining 83.33. This is a classic example of hajb nuqsan.

Key Terms
ولد (walad): Child: includes son or daughter, and also includes son's child (grandson) by extension in Hanafi interpretation.
اخوة (ikhwah): Brothers: in this context means two or more brothers (full or consanguine) who reduce the mother's share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following does NOT cause the mother's share to reduce from 1/3 to 1/6?
A) A son of the deceased
B) A grandson (son's son)
C) One brother of the deceased
D) Two brothers of the deceased

Key Takeaway
The mother's inheritance share is reduced from 1/3 to 1/6 by the presence of any child, a son's child, or two or more brothers of the deceased.

Grandchildren Inheriting Surplus After Daughters
States surplus after daughters goes to grandchildren as asabah with male double female

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares of grandchildren when they inherit as asabah after daughters, applying the rule that male takes double female.

Core Idea
When two or more daughters take two-thirds, grandchildren inherit the surplus as asabah, with males receiving twice females.

The distribution of an estate when both daughters and grandchildren survive can cause confusion. This passage clarifies that daughters receive their fixed two-thirds, and grandchildren only take the remaining one-third as residuary heirs. The rule is anchored in an athar from Zaid bin Thabit, a companion of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Guided Path
1
Identify the fixed shares
Recognize that two or more daughters receive two-thirds of the estate as their fixed share (fard). The remainder is one-third.
If there is only one daughter, her share is one-half, not two-thirds.
2
Determine the residuary heirs
After the fixed shares, the remaining property goes to the residuary heirs (asabah). In this case, grandchildren (sons of the son and their sisters) are the asabah.
If there is no male grandchild, granddaughters alone do not inherit as asabah; they would be blocked.
3
Apply the asabah rule
Among the grandchildren, males take double the share of females (asabah bi-ghayrihi). Divide the surplus according to this ratio.
For example, if surplus is 1/3 and there are one grandson and one granddaughter, grandson gets 2/3 of surplus, granddaughter 1/3.
4
Examine the supporting evidence
The author cites the athar of Zaid bin Thabit: when there is no surviving son and two or more daughters, grandchildren inherit the surplus only if a male grandchild exists, with male taking double.
This athar is the basis for the Hanafi ruling and illustrates the application of hajb nuqsan (reduction) rather than complete exclusion.
5
Practice the calculation
Work through the example: estate 100, two daughters get 66.66 (2/3), grandson gets 22.22, granddaughter gets 11.11. Verify the male to female ratio.
Note that the grandchildren's share is reduced from a potential full inheritance to only one-third due to the daughters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
