[۳۲۲۳) (۲) اور جو باقی بچ جائے بیٹیوں کے لینے سے وہ پوتے اور ان کی بہنوں کے لئے ہے مرد کو عورت سے دو گنا۔ دو یا اس سے زیادہ بیٹیاں ہوں تو ان کو دو تہائی ملے گی ، باقی ایک تہائی پوتے اور پوتیوں کو بطور عصبہ ملے گی۔ اس ایک تہائی میں مرد کو عورت کا دو گنا ملے گا۔ اگر بیٹیاں نہ ہوتی تو سب مال ہوتے اور پوتیون کو ملتا لیکن بیٹیوں کی وجہ سے پوتے اور پوتیوں کو حجب نقصان ہوا کہ صرف ایک تہائی میں ان کو تقسیم کرنا پڑا۔

[3223] (2) And the surplus over the fixed share of the daughters is for the sons of the son and their sisters, for the male the share of two females. (2) And whatever remains after the daughters' share, that is for the grandson and his sisters; the male gets twice the female. If there are two or more daughters, they get two-thirds; the remaining one-third is given to the grandson and granddaughters as asabah (residuary). In this one-third, the male gets twice the female. If there were no daughters, all the property would go to the grandchildren, but because of the daughters, the grandchildren suffer hajb nuqsan (reduction) and only one-third is divided among them. In the athar (narration) it is mentioned: From Kharija bin Zaid from his father Zaid bin Thabit: 'If there is no male child and there are two or more daughters, then the daughters' sons do not inherit with them, unless there is with the daughters' sons a male who is of the same degree or higher from the deceased. Then whatever surplus remains, they divide it with the male getting twice the share of the female. If no surplus remains, they get nothing.' (Sunan Sa'id, Bab al-Mirath, vol. 6, p. 1377, no. 12313). The case is: Deceased 100, two daughters 66.66, grandson 22.22, granddaughter 11.11.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage explains the inheritance of grandchildren when there are daughters. If two or more daughters exist, they receive two-thirds as their fixed share. The remaining one-third goes to the grandchildren (sons of the son) as residuary heirs (asabah). Among the grandchildren, males take double the share of females. The author cites an athar from Zaid bin Thabit to support this ruling. The example calculation shows 66.66 for the two daughters, and 33.33 split between grandson (22.22) and granddaughter (11.11). This is another case of hajb nuqsan: the grandchildren are reduced from a potential full inheritance to only one-third due to the presence of daughters.

Key Terms
عصبة (asabah): Residuary heir: those who inherit the remainder after the fixed shares are distributed; in this context, grandchildren are asabah after daughters.

Surplus after Full Sisters Goes to Consanguine Siblings
States that surplus after two full sisters goes to consanguine siblings with male taking double female

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares when the deceased leaves two full sisters and consanguine siblings, applying the asabah rule that consanguine siblings receive the surplus with male taking twice the female's share.

Core Idea
After full sisters take two-thirds, the remaining third goes to consanguine siblings, male twice female.

This lesson addresses a specific faraid scenario: two full sisters and consanguine siblings. The full sisters take their fixed share of two-thirds. The surplus (one-third) is inherited by consanguine brother(s) and sister(s) as asabah, with the brother taking twice the sister's share. This ruling is supported by the athar of Zaid bin Thabit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs
The deceased leaves two full sisters and at least one consanguine sibling (brother or sister).
2
Assign the fixed share to full sisters
Two full sisters receive two-thirds of the estate as their Quranic share.
Based on Quran 4:176.
3
Calculate the surplus
The remaining one-third is the surplus that goes to the consanguine siblings.
Surplus = 1 - 2/3 = 1/3.
4
Distribute the surplus to consanguine siblings as asabah
Consanguine siblings take the surplus as residuary heirs, with the male taking twice the share of the female.
If one brother and one sister, brother gets 2/3 of surplus, sister gets 1/3.
5
Consider the evidence
The athar of Zaid bin Thabit, transmitted by Abu al-Zinad, supports this allocation.
The source text includes a fragmented quote from that athar.

Source Text

[3224] (3) And the surplus over the fixed share of the two full sisters (from both father and mother) is for the brothers and sisters (from father). (3) And whatever remains from the share of full sisters, that is for consanguine (father's side) brothers and sisters. The male gets twice the female. If there are two full sisters (from both parents), they get two-thirds, and one-third remains for the consanguine brother and sister. For the brother two shares and for the sister one share. Commentary
This passage addresses the inheritance of consanguine siblings (by the same father but different mother) when there are two or more full sisters. The full sisters take two-thirds as their fixed share, and the remaining one-third goes to the consanguine siblings. Among them, males (consanguine brother) take twice the share of females (consanguine sister). The author refers to the athar of Zaid bin Thabit, though the quoted text appears to be a repetition from earlier. This is another illustration of hajb nuqsan: the consanguine siblings are reduced to only the surplus after the full sisters' share.

Key Terms
اخوة من اب (ikhwah min ab): Consanguine siblings: brothers and sisters sharing the same father but not the same mother.
حقیقی بہن (haqiqi bahan): Full sister: sister sharing both parents with the deceased.

Distribution of Residue to Grandchildren After Daughters' Shares
Ruling with proof from Zaid ibn Thabit on inheritance by grandchildren.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the share of grandsons and granddaughters as residuaries after daughters take their fixed shares, applying the rule 'للذكر مثل حظ الانثيين'.

Core Idea
After daughters take their fixed shares, the residue goes to grandchildren as asabah, with sons getting twice the daughters' portion.

In Hanafi inheritance law, when a deceased leaves daughters and grandchildren from a predeceased son, the daughters receive their prescribed shares (e.g., two-thirds for two or more daughters). The remaining estate is not wasted but passes to the grandchildren as residuaries (asabah), with the male inheriting twice the female. This ruling is based on an athar from Zaid ibn Thabit and exemplifies the concept of hajb nuqsan (partial exclusion). This lesson walks through the rule, its proof, and a numerical example.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs and fixed shares
List the surviving heirs: daughters (fixed-share heirs) and grandchildren through a predeceased son (residuaries). Determine the daughters' share: one daughter gets half; two or more get two-thirds.
Remember: daughters are 'ashab al-furud' (fixed-share heirs).
2
Calculate the residue after fixed shares
Subtract the daughters' share from the total estate. This remainder is the residue (fadil).
If no residue remains, grandchildren receive nothing.
3
Distribute the residue to grandchildren as asabah
The residue is divided among grandsons and granddaughters, with the male receiving double the female's portion. This is the rule 'للذكر مثل حظ الانثيين'.
Grandsons and granddaughters are asabah bi-ghayriha (by reason of the male).
4
Note the effect of hajb nuqsan
The grandchildren are partially excluded (hajb nuqsan) because the daughters consume part of the estate. Without daughters, they would take the entire estate.
This is not total exclusion (hajb hirman).
5
Verify with the athar from Zaid ibn Thabit
The ruling is supported by the athar transmitted by Kharijah ibn Zaid from his father, specifying that residue after two or more daughters goes to grandsons/granddaughters with male double.
The athar is found in Sunan al-Bayhaqi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[۳۲۲۳) (۲) اور جو باقی بچ جائے بیٹیوں کے لینے سے وہ پوتے اور ان کی بہنوں کے لئے ہے مرد کو عورت سے دو گنا۔ دو یا اس سے زیادہ بیٹیاں ہوں تو ان کو دو تہائی ملے گی ، باقی ایک تہائی پوتے اور پوتیوں کو بطور عصبہ ملے گی۔ اس ایک تہائی میں مرد کو عورت کا دو گنا ملے گا۔ اگر بیٹیاں نہ ہوتی تو سب مال ہوتے اور پوتیون کو ملتا لیکن بیٹیوں کی وجہ سے پوتے اور پوتیوں کو حجب نقصان ہوا کہ صرف ایک تہائی میں ان کو تقسیم کرنا پڑا۔

[3223 (2)] And what remains after the prescribed share of the daughters is for the sons' sons and their sisters, the male gets double the female. In this case, the mother gets one-sixth, i.e., 16.66 out of 100, and the remaining 83.33 goes to the two brothers. [3223 (2)] And what is left over after the daughters take their share, it is for the grandsons and their sisters, the male gets double the female. If there are two or more daughters, they get two-thirds, the remaining one-third goes to the grandsons and granddaughters as asabah. In that one-third, the male gets double the female. If there were no daughters, they would get all the property, but due to the daughters, the grandsons and granddaughters suffer hajb nuqsan (reduction in share), being confined to only one-third. An athar has passed: from Kharijah ibn Zaid from his father Zaid ibn Thabit: 'If the deceased has no male child, and there are two or more daughters, then the daughters' sons' daughters have no inheritance with them unless there is a male descendant of the son who is of equal rank or lower. Then the surplus is given to those of equal rank and above among the daughters' sons, and they divide it with the male getting double the female. If nothing remains, they get nothing.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Kitab al-Mawaris, vol. 6, p. 1377, no. 12313). In this athar, whatever remains after the two daughters is for the grandson and granddaughter, with the male getting double the female. The calculation is as follows: Estate 100; two daughters get 66.66; remaining 33.33 is divided between a grandson and granddaughter, with the grandson getting 22.22 and the granddaughter 11.11.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling on the distribution of inheritance when there are daughters and grandchildren through a son (sons' sons and daughters). The ruling is that after the daughters take their fixed share (two-thirds for two or more daughters, one-half for one daughter), the residue goes to the sons' sons and their sisters as residuaries (asabah) with the male receiving twice the female's share. This is supported by an athar (tradition) from Zaid ibn Thabit transmitted by his son Kharijah. The text also provides a numerical example: if the estate is 100 and there are two daughters, they take 66.66, and the remaining 33.33 is divided among the grandson and granddaughter, with the grandson taking 22.22 and the granddaughter 11.11. The passage notes that the grandchildren suffer 'hajb nuqsan' (partial exclusion) because the daughters reduce their share; otherwise, they would have taken the entire estate.

Key Terms
عصبہ (asabah): Residuary heirs who take the remainder after fixed shares; here grandsons and granddaughters through a son.
حجب نقصان (hajb nuqsan): Partial exclusion that reduces the share of an heir without entirely excluding them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a case where the deceased leaves two daughters and a grandson and granddaughter from a predeceased son, how is the estate divided?
A) Daughters get all; grandchildren get nothing.
B) Daughters get two-thirds; grandson and granddaughter share the remaining one-third with male getting double.
C) Daughters get half; grandson and granddaughter share the other half equally.
D) All heirs share equally.

Key Takeaway
The residue after daughters' fixed shares goes to grandchildren as asabah, with the male inheriting twice the female.

Residue After Full Sisters Goes to Consanguine Siblings
Ruling on distribution of residue after full sisters' shares to half-siblings from father

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the shares of full sisters and consanguine siblings when both are present, applying the Hanafi ruling that consanguine siblings inherit residue as asabah.

Core Idea
When full sisters take two-thirds, the residue passes to consanguine siblings as residuaries with the male taking double the female's share.

In Hanafi faraid, full sisters are entitled to a fixed share (2/3 if two or more). However, when there are also consanguine siblings (half-siblings from the father's side), they do not receive a fixed share but inherit the residue as residuaries—but only if a consanguine brother is present. This ruling is established by the practice of Zaid ibn Thabit and supported by the Quranic verse on inheritance. In this lesson, we will work through the calculation and the underlying evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs
List all surviving heirs: full sisters (from same parents) and consanguine siblings (from father only). Note that full sisters are 'fard' heirs, while consanguine siblings are 'asabah' (residuaries) only if a male consanguine is present.
If no consanguine brother, consanguine sisters do not inherit.
2
Assign fixed shares
Full sisters receive their prescribed Quranic share: if two or more, they get two-thirds of the estate equally. If only one full sister, she gets half.
This lesson covers two or more full sisters.
3
Calculate the residue
Subtract the total fixed shares from the estate. The remainder is the residue available for consanguine siblings as residuaries.
If no residue, consanguine siblings get nothing.
4
Distribute the residue
Divide the residue among the consanguine siblings according to the principle: male gets twice the share of a female (for the male like the portion of two females). This is a fixed ratio.
If there are multiple consanguine siblings, the ratio holds across them.
5
Check for exclusion and final shares
Ensure no consanguine sister inherits without a consanguine brother. Then compute each heir's share as a fraction of the estate.
Use tashih if needed to obtain whole numbers.

[3224 (3)] And what remains after the shares of the full sisters (from the same father and mother) is for the consanguine brothers and sisters (from the father only), the male gets double the female. If there are two full sisters, they get two-thirds. The remaining one-third is for the consanguine brother and sister, the male gets double and the female one. It is in an athar: Tafsir Abi al-Zinad on the meanings of Zaid ibn Thabit: 'If there are two or more full sisters, they have two-thirds prescribed. And the consanguine sister has no inheritance with them unless there is a consanguine brother with them. Then those with fixed shares take first, and if anything remains, it is for the consanguine siblings, with the male getting double. If nothing remains, they get nothing.' (Footnote) Hadrat Zaid ibn Thabit said: If there are two or more full sisters, they get two-thirds. And the consanguine sister does not inherit with them unless there is a consanguine brother with them. Then those with fixed shares are given first. If something remains, it is for the consanguine siblings on the principle of male getting double female. And if nothing remains, they get nothing. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Mirath al-Ikhwah wa al-Akhawat li Ab wa Umm aw li Ab, vol. 6, p. 381, no. 12326). From this athar, it is learned that after the two full sisters take, what remains is divided between the consanguine brother and sister, with the male getting double the female. There is also an indication in the Quran: 'But if there are two (sisters), they get two-thirds of what he leaves. And if there are brothers and sisters, then for the male is the share of two females.' (Surah an-Nisa', 176). The calculation: Estate 100; two full sisters get 66.66; remaining 33.33 goes to one consanguine brother (22.22) and one consanguine sister (11.11).
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on exclusion (hajb) and presents the ruling when there are full sisters and half-siblings from the father's side. The ruling: two or more full sisters take two-thirds as their fixed share. The residue (if any) goes to the consanguine siblings (from father only) as residuaries, with the male taking twice the female's share. This is supported by an athar from Zaid ibn Thabit and a Quranic verse (an-Nisa' 4:176). The text provides a numerical example: estate 100, two full sisters take 66.66, remaining 33.33 is divided between one consanguine brother (22.22) and one consanguine sister (11.11). The footnote clarifies that consanguine sisters do not inherit with full sisters unless there is a consanguine brother present, and even then they only get residue after fixed shares.

Key Terms
حقیقی بہن (haqiqi bahan): Full sister sharing both father and mother with the deceased.
سوتیلا بھائی/بہن (sotela bhai/bahan): Consanguine half-sibling sharing only the father with the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

In Hanafi faraid, full sisters take two-thirds; the residue passes to consanguine siblings as residuaries, but only if a consanguine brother is present, with the male taking double the female's share.

One Daughter with Grandsons and Granddaughters
Ruling for estate with one daughter and grandchildren through son

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares when a daughter and grandchildren through a son survive, applying hajb nuqsan rules correctly.

Core Idea
A daughter's half share reduces the grandchildren's portion — this is hajb nuqsan, not total exclusion.

This lesson covers a common faraid scenario: a deceased leaves one daughter and grandchildren through a son (grandsons and granddaughters). The Quran gives the daughter half. The remaining half goes to the grandchildren as residuaries, with the male taking twice the female's share. This is an example of hajb nuqsan (partial exclusion) because the daughter's presence reduces the grandchildren's potential share from the entire estate to only half.

Guided Path
1
List all surviving heirs
Identify: daughter, grandson, granddaughter. No other relatives are mentioned. Note that grandchildren through a son inherit in the absence of parents and siblings.
2
Apply hajb hirman (total exclusion)
In this scenario, no one is totally excluded. The daughter does not exclude the grandchildren; they are asabah.
3
Apply hajb nuqsan (partial reduction)
The daughter's fixed share of half reduces the grandchildren's share from the whole estate to the remaining half. This is a reduction, not exclusion.
Compare: if the daughter were absent, the grandchildren would take the entire estate as asabah.
4
Assign Quranic shares (fard)
Daughter gets 1/2 (half) as per Quran 4:11. This is her fixed share.
5
Distribute residue to asabah
The remaining half goes to the grandchildren as asabah bi-ghayrihi: grandson takes double the granddaughter's share. The residue is divided into three parts: grandson gets two, granddaughter gets one.
The ratio is 2:1 male to female.

[3225 (4)] If the deceased leaves one daughter and several sons' daughters and several sons' sons, then the daughter gets half. The remainder is for the sons' sons and their sisters, the male gets double the female. It has passed earlier that if there is one daughter, she gets half. The remaining half is for the grandson and granddaughter as asabah. In this, the grandson gets double the granddaughter. If there was no daughter, they would take all the property, but due to the daughter, they only get half, which is hajb nuqsan (partial exclusion). The Quran says: 'If there are two or more daughters, they get two-thirds; if one, she gets half.' (Surah an-Nisa', verse 11). So the half that remains goes to grandson and granddaughter as asabah. Footnote: Hadrat Zaid ibn Thabit said: If there are two or more full sisters, they get two-thirds. And with them, the consanguine sister does not inherit unless there is a consanguine brother. Then those with fixed shares are given first. If something remains, it is for the consanguine siblings on the principle of male double female. If nothing remains, they get nothing. (b) If there are more than two women, they get two-thirds; if one, she gets half.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This lesson covers the case of a deceased who leaves one daughter and grandchildren through a son. The ruling: the daughter takes half (1/2) as her fixed share. The remaining half goes to the sons' sons and daughters (grandchildren) as residuaries (asabah), with the male taking twice the female's share. The text notes that this is an example of hajb nuqsan (partial exclusion) because the daughter reduces the grandchildren's share from the entire estate to just half. The Quranic basis is cited: 'if one daughter, half.' The footnote reiterates the previous ruling on full sisters and consanguine siblings, which is slightly out of context here.

Key Terms
حجب نقصان (hajb nuqsan): Reduction of share for some heirs due to the presence of others; here grandchildren get only half instead of all.
عصبہ (asabah): Residuary heirs who take the remainder after fixed shares; here grandsons and granddaughters through a son.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Daughter gets 133.33, grandson gets 44.44, granddaughter gets 22.22.
D) Daughter gets 50, grandson gets 100, granddaughter gets 50.

Key Takeaway
When a daughter inherits alongside grandchildren through a son, she takes half, and the grandchildren share the residue with the male receiving twice the female's share.

Inheritance of Half-Siblings with Full Sisters
Explains the rule for half-siblings inheriting alongside two or more full sisters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares when two full sisters and half-siblings are present, applying hajb rules and the asabah principle.

Core Idea
Half-siblings inherit as asabah only if a half-brother is present; otherwise, half-sisters are excluded by two full sisters.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri explains a classic faraid scenario: a deceased person leaves two full sisters and half-siblings (from the father's side). The full sisters receive their fixed Quranic share of two-thirds. The half-siblings' entitlement depends on the presence of a half-brother, who transforms them into residuary heirs. We will walk through the rule, the evidence from the Quran and the practice of Zayd ibn Thabit, and a sample calculation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs
List all surviving heirs: two full sisters, one half-brother, one half-sister.
Ignore any other potential heirs (e.g., spouse, parents) as they are absent in this case.
2
Apply hajb (exclusion)
Determine if any half-sibling is excluded. The half-sister alone would be excluded by the two full sisters (hajb hirman). However, because a half-brother is present, all half-siblings become residuary heirs and are not excluded.
Presence of a half-brother lifts the exclusion of half-sisters.
3
Assign fixed shares
The two full sisters are entitled to the Quranically prescribed share of two-thirds (2/3) of the estate.
This is based on Quran 4:176 and consensus.
4
Distribute the residue as asabah
The remaining one-third (1/3) of the estate goes to the half-siblings as residuary heirs. They divide the residue with the male (half-brother) taking twice the share of the female (half-sister).
The division ratio is 2:1, as established by Quran 4:176 and the athar of Zayd ibn Thabit.

حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت زید بن ثابت نے فرمایا اگر حقیقی بہنیں دو یا ان سے زیادہ ہوں تو ان کے دو تہائی متعین ہوگی۔ اور ان کے ساتھ سوتیلی بہن کو میراث نہیں ملے گی مگر یہ کہ ان کے ساتھ سوتیلا بھائی ہو تو حصے والوں کو پہلے حصے دیئے جائیں گے۔ پس اگر ان سے کچھ بچ گیا تو یہ بچا ہوا سوتیلے بھائی بہنوں میں ہوگا ۔ مرد کو عورت کے دو گنے کے اصول پر۔ اور اگر نہیں بچا تو ان کو کچھ نہیں ملے گا (ب) اگر عورتیں دو سے زیادہ ہوں تو ان کے لئے ترکہ کی دو تہائی ہوگی اور ایک ہو تو اس کے لئے آدھا ہوگا۔
Chapter of Exclusion. Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Volume 4. The father: for the male the share of two females. [3225] (4) And if he leaves a daughter, and daughters of a son, and sons of a son, then for the daughter and the females? prescribe for them two-thirds, and no inheritance with them for daughters of the father except if there is with them a male from the father. So if there is with them a male, begin with the fixed shares of those who have a fixed share and give them. Then if there remains after that a surplus, it is among the children of the father: for the male the share of two females. And if nothing remains, nothing for them. (a) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on Inheritance of Brothers and Sisters from Father and Mother or Father, Volume 6, p. 381, no. 12326) From this athar it became known that after the two full sisters take, what remains will be divided between the half-brother and half-sisters, such that the male gets twice the female. (2) The verse indicates this: 'But if there are two, they share two-thirds of what he left. And if there are brothers and sisters, males and females, then for the male the share of two females.' (Surah an-Nisa 4:176) This verse states that if there are brothers and sisters, the male gets twice the female. The case will be as such: Deceased: 100. Two full sisters: 66.66. One half-brother: 22.22. One half-sister: 11.11. In this case, the two full sisters got two-thirds of 100 (66.66). The remaining one-third (33.33) was divided between the half-brother and half-sister, with the brother getting double (22.22) and the sister getting one share (11.11). Footnote (a): Sayyiduna Zayd ibn Thabit said: If there are two or more full sisters, their fixed share is two-thirds. And with them, the half-sister does not inherit unless there is a half-brother with them. Then the fixed-share holders are given their shares. If anything remains after that, it goes to the half siblings, with the male getting twice the female. If nothing remains, they get nothing. (b) If females are more than two, they get two-thirds of the estate; if one, she gets half.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is a faraid case ruling with proof and example. It explains the inheritance of half-siblings (from the father) when there are two or more full sisters. The key principle: full sisters get their fixed share of two-thirds. Half-sisters are normally excluded by full sisters unless accompanied by a half-brother. The presence of a half-brother transforms the half-siblings into 'asabah (residuary heirs). They inherit the residue after full sisters' shares, with the male taking twice the female's share. The proof is from the athar of Zayd ibn Thabit and the Quranic verse (4:176) which establishes the general principle for siblings of the father. The example illustrates: estate 100, two full sisters get 66.66 (2/3), the remaining 33.33 goes to half-brother (22.22) and half-sister (11.11) in 2:1 ratio.

Key Terms
حجب (hajb): Exclusion or reduction of inheritance share due to presence of another heir.
عصبة (asabah): Residuary heir who takes the remainder after fixed shares.
فرض (fard): Fixed Quranic share in inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the deceased leaves two full sisters and one half-brother (with no half-sister), what is the half-brother's share?
A) 1/3 of the estate
B) 1/6 of the estate
C) Nothing, he is excluded
D) The residue after full sisters' 2/3

Key Takeaway
Half-siblings inherit the residue after full sisters' two-thirds only if a half-brother is present, with the male taking twice the female's share.

Inheritance of Daughter with Grandchildren
Explains the inheritance of one daughter with grandsons and granddaughters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the shares when a daughter and grandchildren survive, applying hajb nuqsan and the 'asabah principle correctly.

Core Idea
A daughter's half share reduces grandchildren's inheritance from whole estate to the residue, illustrating hajb nuqsan.

This passage presents a classic faraid scenario: a deceased leaves one daughter and several grandchildren (sons and daughters of a predeceased son). The daughter takes her fixed half, and the grandchildren share the remaining half as residuary heirs ('asabah), with the male taking twice the female. This case demonstrates the concept of hajb nuqsan (partial exclusion) and the rule that grandchildren inherit as 'asabah only when a male of equal rank is present.

Guided Path
1
Identify all surviving heirs
List the heirs from the case: one daughter, one grandson, one granddaughter. Note that the grandchildren are children of a predeceased son; they are called 'banu al-ibn'.
No other heirs are present in this case.
2
Apply hajb nuqsan
Determine which heirs are affected by partial exclusion. The daughter's presence reduces the grandchildren's share from the whole estate to the residue (half). This is hajb nuqsan, not total exclusion.
If the daughter were absent, grandchildren would take the entire estate as 'asabah.
3
Assign fixed shares (fard)
Allocate the daughter's fixed share: 1/2 of the estate, based on Quran 4:11.
Daughter's share is fard (fixed) and takes priority over residuary heirs.
4
Distribute the residue as 'asabah
The remaining half (residue) goes to the grandchildren as residuary heirs. Among them, the grandson takes twice the granddaughter's share (ratio 2:1). This follows the general rule for 'asabah when males and females are present.
If only granddaughters were present (no grandson), they would receive a fixed 2/3 or half, but with a male they become 'asabah.
5
Calculate the base number and final shares
Set the base number to express shares as integers. Since daughter's share is 1/2 (3/6), the residue is 1/2 (3/6). The residue is divided in a 2:1 ratio, giving grandson 2/6 and granddaughter 1/6. Convert to actual amounts using the estate value.
Example with $100: daughter $50, grandson $33.33, granddaughter $16.66.

[3225] (4) If he leaves one daughter and several granddaughters and several grandsons, then the daughter gets half. The remainder is for the grandsons and their sisters: for the male the share of two females. It has already passed that if there is one daughter, she gets half. The remaining half is for the grandson and granddaughter as 'asabah. In this, the grandson gets double the granddaughter. If there were no daughter, all the property would be for the grandson and granddaughter, but because of the daughter, they only got half, which is hajb nuqsan (reduction). The verse states that for one daughter is half, so the remaining half goes to the grandson and granddaughter as 'asabah. The verse is: 'But if there are women more than two, then for them two-thirds of what he left; and if there is one, then for her half.' (Surah an-Nisa 4:11) (b) Footnote (a): So if with the granddaughters there is a male of the same rank, they get no sixth and no fixed share, but if after the fixed-share holders there is a surplus, that surplus is for that male and for the females of the same rank, with the male getting the share of two females. (b) If women are more than two, they get two-thirds; if one, she gets half. [PAGE_430] Chapter of Exclusion. Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Volume 4. The half, and the remainder for the sons of the son and their sisters: for the male the share of two females. [3226] (5) And similarly, the surplus over the fixed share of the sister from father and mother is for the children of the father and daughters of the father, for the male the share of two females. If there is one daughter, she gets half. And since with the granddaughter there is a grandson, they both take the remaining half as 'asabah. There is an athar: 'If with the daughters of the son there is a male of their rank, they get no sixth and no fixed share, but if there is a surplus after the fixed shares of the fixed-share holders, that surplus is for that male and for the females of his rank: for the male the share of two females.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on Inheritance of Children and Grandchildren, Vol. 6, p. 377, no. 12313 / Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, on a man leaving two daughters and a granddaughter and a grandson lower than her, Vol. 6, p. 246, no. 31075) From this athar it became known that after the daughter takes half, the remaining half is divided between the grandson and granddaughter. The case will be as such: Deceased: 100. One daughter: 50. Grandson: 33.33. Granddaughter: 16.66. In this case, the daughter gets half, i.e., 50 out of 100. The remaining half, i.e., 50, is divided: one-third (16.66) to the granddaughter, and double that (33.33) to the grandson.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is a faraid case ruling with proof and example. It covers the inheritance of one daughter together with grandchildren (children of a predeceased son). The daughter takes her fixed half. The remaining half goes to the grandchildren as residuary heirs ('asabah), with the grandson taking twice the granddaughter's share. This is an example of hajb nuqsan (reduction): without the daughter, the grandchildren would take the whole estate, but the daughter's presence reduces their share to half. The proof is from the Quran (4:11) for the daughter's half and from the athar of the Prophet (via Bayhaqi and Ibn Abi Shaybah) stating that grandchildren do not get a fixed share but take as 'asabah when a male of equal rank is present. The example: 100 estate, daughter 50, granddaughter 16.66, grandson 33.33 (ratio 2:1).

Key Terms
حجب نقصان (hajb nuqsan): Reduction of an heir's share due to presence of another heir, not total exclusion.
بنو الابن (banu al-ibn): Grandchildren (children of the son), who inherit as 'asabah in absence of son.

Inheritance of Half-Siblings After Full Sister
Explains the inheritance of half-siblings from the residue after a full sister's half

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance distribution when a full sister and consanguine half-siblings survive, identifying the condition that half-siblings inherit only as residue when a male half-brother is present.

Core Idea
Half-siblings inherit only as residue (asabah) and only when a male half-brother is present.

In faraid, the full sister's fixed share is clear from the Quran. But what about half-siblings from the father? This passage clarifies that they are not fixed-share holders; they take the residue only if a male half-brother is present. The rule ensures that the inheritance is distributed fairly, with the male receiving twice the female's share.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs and their relationships
List all surviving heirs: one full sister (germane), one half-brother (consanguine), one half-sister (consanguine). Understand that half-siblings share only the father.
Full sister shares both parents; half-siblings share only father.
2
Determine the full sister's fixed share
From Quran 4:176, a single full sister inherits half (1/2) when there are no children.
The verse is clear: '...if a man dies leaving no child, and he has a sister, she gets half...'
3
Assess the condition for half-siblings to inherit
Half-siblings have no fixed share. They inherit as 'asabah (residuary heirs) only if there is a male half-brother. Without a male, half-sisters are excluded by the full sister.
The athar states: 'If with the daughters of the father there is a male brother, they have no fixed share...'
4
Apply the 'asabah division rule
The residue after the full sister's half is divided among half-siblings in a 2:1 ratio (male:female). Half-brother gets double the half-sister.
This follows the general Quranic principle for male and female shares when inheriting together.
5
Calculate using a common denominator
Use base 2 for the half, then adjust to 6 for integer shares: full sister 3/6, half-brother 2/6, half-sister 1/6. Verify total equals 1.
If the estate is 120, full sister gets 60, half-brother 40, half-sister 20.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۲۲۶] (۵) ایسے ہی جو باقی بچے ایک حقیقی بہن کے حصے سے وہ سوتیلے بہن بھائی کے لئے ہے، مرد کے لئے عورت کا دو گناہ ایک ماں باپ شریک بہن ہو تو اس کو آدھا ملے گا اور باقی جو آدھار ہا وہ باپ شریک یعنی سوتیلے بھائی اور بہن کو لے گا ۔ مرد کو دو گنا اور عورت کو ایک گنا۔ ایک حقیقی بہن ہو تو اس کے لئے آدھا ہے اس کی دلیل کے لئے آیت گزر چکی ہے۔ یستفتونك قل الله يفتيكم في الكلالة ان امرؤ هلك ليس له ولد وله اخت فلها نصف ماترک (ب) ( آیت ۱۷۶، سورۃ النساء ۴ ) اس میں ہے کہ ایک حقیقی بہن ہو تو اس کو آدھا ملے گا ۔ اور باقی آدھا سوتیلے بھائی بہن کو ملے گا اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ فان كان مع بنات الاب اخ ذكر فلا فريضة لهم ويبدأ باهل الفرائض فيعطون فرائضهم فان فضل بعد ذلك فضل كان بين بنى الاب للذكر مثل حظ الانثيين حاشیہ : (الف) پس اگر پوتی کے ساتھ ہوتا ہو اسی درجے میں تو پوتی کو چھٹا نہیں ملے گا اور نہ اس کا کوئی با ضابطہ حصہ ہوگا۔ لیکن اگر حصے داروں کے لینے بعد کچھ باقی رہ گیا تو یہ بقیہ پوتے کے لئے ہوگا۔ اور اس کے درجے میں جو ہوتی ہے اس کے لئے بھی ہو گا۔ مرد کے لئے عورت کے دو گنا کے اصول پر (ب) آپ سے فتوی مانگتے ہیں تو فرمادیجئے کہ اللہ کلالہ کے بارے میں فتوی دیتے ہیں کہ آدمی مرجائے اور اس کی بہن ہو تو اس کے لئے ترکے کا آدھا ہوگا۔
[3226] (5) Similarly, what remains from the share of a full sister is for the half-brother and half-sister: for the male the share of two females. If there is a full sister (from both mother and father), she gets half, and the remaining half is taken by the half-brother and half-sister from the father. The male gets double, the female single. For one full sister, she gets half; the proof of this has already passed with the verse: 'They ask you for a ruling. Say: Allah gives you a ruling concerning the person who has neither parents nor offspring: if a man dies leaving no child, and he has a sister, she gets half of what he leaves.' (Surah an-Nisa 4:176) This verse states that if there is one full sister, she gets half. The remaining half goes to the half-brother and half-sister; the proof is this athar: 'If with the daughters of the father there is a male brother, they have no fixed share. Start with the fixed-share holders and give them their fixed shares. Then if there remains after that a surplus, it is among the children of the father, for the male the share of two females.' Footnote (a): So if with the granddaughters there is a male of the same rank, they get no sixth and no fixed share. But if after the fixed-share holders there remains something, that remainder is for that male and for the females of his rank, with the male getting the share of two females. (b) 'They ask you for a ruling. Say: Allah gives you a ruling concerning the person who has neither parents nor offspring: if a man dies leaving no child, and he has a sister, she gets half of what he leaves.'
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is a faraid case ruling with proof and example. It explains the inheritance of half-siblings (consanguine brothers and sisters) when there is one full sister (germane sister). The full sister takes her fixed half (Quran 4:176). The residue goes to half-siblings, but only if a half-brother is present (as per the athar). The half-siblings take as 'asabah, with the male getting twice the female's share. The proof is from the Quran (4:176) for the full sister's share and from the athar (similar to the one used in lesson 2) showing that half-siblings have no fixed share but take the residue after fixed shares are given. This is analogous to the rule for grandchildren: half-siblings inherit only when there is a male among them.

Key Terms
كلالة (kalalah): A deceased who leaves neither parents nor children; siblings inherit in this case.
أخت لأب وأم (ukhtun li-abi wa-umm): Full sister (germane) – shares same parents.
أخت لأب (ukhtun li-abi): Consanguine half-sister (same father, different mother).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The full sister takes her fixed half; half-siblings inherit the residue only when a male half-brother is present, with the male receiving twice the female's share.

Inheritance of Daughter and Grandchildren
Ruling with proof and example for daughter's half and grandson's share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares when a daughter and grandchildren from a predeceased son survive, applying the residuary (asabah) rule correctly.

Core Idea
Daughter's half is fixed; the remaining half goes to son's children as asabah, male double female.

In this lesson, we examine a specific inheritance scenario: the deceased leaves a daughter and grandchildren from a predeceased son (both a grandson and a granddaughter). You will learn how to apply the Quranic share of the daughter and the residuary rule for the son's children, supported by a prophetic athar. Understanding this distribution is essential for accurate faraid calculations.

Guided Path
1
Identify all surviving heirs
List the heirs: daughter, grandson (son's son), granddaughter (son's daughter).
No spouse or parents in this scenario.
2
Determine fixed shares
The daughter is entitled to half (1/2) as a Quranic share. The grandchildren do not have a fixed share; they inherit as residuary heirs because a male is present.
If there were only granddaughters, they would get 1/6 each collectively, but here a grandson elevates them to asabah.
3
Apply the residuary (asabah) rule
After the daughter takes her half, the remaining half is distributed among the son's children as asabah. The grandson takes twice the share of the granddaughter (male:female = 2:1).
The athar confirms this: 'for the male the share of two females'.
4
Calculate the shares
Estate = 100. Daughter: 1/2 = 50. Remaining = 50. Divide 50 into three parts (2 for grandson, 1 for granddaughter): each part = 16.66. Granddaughter: 16.66, Grandson: 33.33.
Check: total = 50+16.66+33.33 = 100.
5
Note the exception
If the granddaughter were not accompanied by a grandson (only granddaughters), they would receive 1/6 collectively, and the daughter would get 1/2, the rest would go to other asabah.
The footnote clarifies: if a male of equal degree is present, the female gets no sixth; they share the surplus as asabah.

Source Text

النصف والباقى لبنى الابن واخواتهم للذكر مثل حظ الانثيين [۳۲۲۲ (۵) بیٹی ہو تو اس کو آدھا ملے گا۔ اور چونکہ پوتی کے ساتھ پوتا بھی ہے اس لئے باقی آدھا عصبہ کے طور پر دونوں لے لیں گے۔ اثر ہے۔ فان كان مع بنات الابن ذكر هو بمنزلتهن فلا سدس لهن ولا فريضة ولكن ان فضل فضل بعد فريضة اهل الفرائض كان ذلك الفضل لذلك الذكر ولمن بمنزلته من الاناث للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين (الف)(سنن للبیہقی ، باب میراٹ اولا والا بن ، ج سادس جس ۳۷۷ نمبر ۱۲۳۱۳ / مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۸ فی رجل ترک ایتنیه وابسته ابنه وابن ابن اسفل منها، ج سادس ،ص ۲۴۶ نمبر ۳۱۰۷۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیٹی کے آدھے لینے کے بعد باقی آدھا پوتے اور پوتی کے درمیان تقسیم ہوگا۔ مسئلہ اس طرح بنے گا۔ میت 100 ایک بیٹی ہوتا ہوتی 50 16.66 + 33.33 50 اس مسئلے میں بیٹی کو آدھا یعنی سو میں سے 50 دیا۔ اور باقی آدھا یعنی 50 میں سے ایک تہائی یعنی 16.66 پوتی کو دیا۔ اور اس کا دو گنا 33.33 پوتے کو دیا۔ حاشیہ : (الف) پس اگر پوتی کے ساتھ ہوتا ہو اسی درجے میں تو پوتی کو چھٹا نہیں ملے گا اور نہ اس کا کوئی با ضابطہ حصہ ہوگا۔ لیکن اگر حصے داروں کے لینے بعد کچھ باقی رہ گیا تو یہ بقیہ پوتے کے لئے ہوگا۔ اور اس کے درجے میں جو ہوتی ہے اس کے لئے بھی ہو گا۔ مرد کے لئے عورت کے دو گنا کے اصول پر
The half and the remainder for the son's children and their sisters: for the male the share of two females. If there is a daughter, she takes half. And since with the granddaughter there is a grandson, the remaining half is taken by both as residuary heirs. There is an athar: 'If there is a male with the daughters of the son, he is in their position, so they get no sixth and no prescribed share; but if there is a surplus after the prescribed shares of the people of inheritance, that surplus is for that male and for those females in his position, with the male taking the share of two females.' From this athar it is known that after the daughter takes half, the remaining half is divided between the grandson and granddaughter. The case proceeds as follows: Estate 100, one daughter takes 50, remaining 50, one third (16.66) to granddaughter, double (33.33) to grandson. Footnote: If with the granddaughter there is one of her degree, then the granddaughter does not get a sixth nor any regular share. But if after the shares of the entitled ones something remains, that remainder is for the grandson and for those of his degree, with the male taking twice the female.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on inheritance when a deceased leaves a daughter and grandchildren from the son (both a grandson and a granddaughter). The daughter receives her Quranic share of half. The remaining half is not divided solely among the daughter or others but goes to the son's children as residuary heirs (asabah). The grandson and granddaughter inherit the remainder, with the grandson receiving twice the share of the granddaughter. The proof is an athar from the Prophet (peace be upon him) recorded in Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah. The example demonstrates the division: from an estate of 100, the daughter gets 50, the granddaughter gets 16.66, and the grandson gets 33.33, fulfilling the rule of male double female. The footnote clarifies that if the granddaughter was of the same degree as the grandson (i.e., no other heir), she does not get a prescribed sixth; rather, she and the grandson share the surplus as asabah.

Key Terms
عصبہ (asabah): Residuary heirs who take what remains after the Quranic shares.
بني الابن (bani al-ibn): The son's children, i.e., grandson and granddaughter from the son.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Daughter gets half, the rest goes to the grandson.
B) Daughter gets half, the grandson and granddaughter share the remaining half, with the son getting double the daughter.
C) Daughter gets one-third, the rest is divided equally among all three.
D) Daughter gets half, the grandson gets the rest, the granddaughter gets nothing.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi faraid, when a daughter and grandchildren from a predeceased son survive, the daughter takes half, and the remaining half is divided among the grandchildren as residuary heirs, with the male receiving double the female's share.

Inheritance of Full Sister and Consanguine Siblings
Ruling with proofs on full sister's half and consanguine siblings' residue

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the shares of a full sister and consanguine siblings when the deceased has no child or father, applying the Quranic rule and the principle of asabah.

Core Idea
Full sister gets half; consanguine siblings take the residue, male twice female.

This passage explains a key faraid scenario: a deceased leaves a full sister and consanguine siblings. The full sister's half is fixed by the Quran, while the consanguine siblings inherit the remainder as residuary heirs. Understanding the interaction between fixed shares (fard) and residuary shares (asabah) is crucial for correct distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs
List the heirs: a full sister (haqiqi), a consanguine brother, and a consanguine sister. Note any potential exclusions (here none).
Full sister is not excluded by consanguine siblings.
2
Apply the Quranic fixed share
The full sister receives half of the estate as per Qur'an 4:176 ('she gets half'). This is her fard share.
This applies when there is no child or father.
3
Determine residuary heirs
After the full sister takes her half, the remaining half goes to the consanguine siblings as asabah (residuary heirs). They inherit per the principle 'male takes double female'.
The athar (hadith) supports this: 'start with fixed shares, then the residue goes to the children of the father.'
4
Calculate the shares
Divide the remainder (half) in the ratio 2:1 for male:female. Example: estate 100, full sister gets 50; remainder 50 is split into 3 parts: consanguine brother gets 2/3 = 33.33, consanguine sister gets 1/3 = 16.66.
Always verify that the fixed share is given first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۲۲۶] (۵) ایسے ہی جو باقی بچے ایک حقیقی بہن کے حصے سے وہ سوتیلے بہن بھائی کے لئے ہے، مرد کے لئے عورت کا دو گناہ ایک ماں باپ شریک بہن ہو تو اس کو آدھا ملے گا اور باقی جو آدھار ہا وہ باپ شریک یعنی سوتیلے بھائی اور بہن کو لے گا ۔ مرد کو دو گنا اور عورت کو ایک گنا۔ ایک حقیقی بہن ہو تو اس کے لئے آدھا ہے اس کی دلیل کے لئے آیت گزر چکی ہے۔ یستفتونك قل الله يفتيكم في الكلالة ان امرؤ هلك ليس له ولد وله اخت فلها نصف ماترک (ب) ( آیت ۱۷۶، سورۃ النساء ۴ ) اس میں ہے کہ ایک حقیقی بہن ہو تو اس کو آدھا ملے گا ۔ اور باقی آدھا سوتیلے بھائی بہن کو ملے گا اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ فان كان مع بنات الاب اخ ذكر فلا فريضة لهم ويبدأ باهل الفرائض فيعطون فرائضهم فان فضل بعد ذلك فضل كان بين بنى الاب للذكر مثل حظ الانثيين حاشیہ : (ب) آپ سے فتوی مانگتے ہیں تو فرمادیجئے کہ اللہ کلالہ کے بارے میں فتوی دیتے ہیں کہ آدمی مرجائے اور اس کی بہن ہو تو اس کے لئے ترکے کا آدھا ہوگا۔ 100 حقیقی بہن علاقی بھائی 50 50 33.33 علاقی بہن 16.16 اس مسئلے میں حقیقی ایک بہن کو سو کا آدھا 50 دیا۔ باقی آدھے میں سے ایک تہائی 16.66 باپ شریک بہن کو دیا۔ اور اس کا دو گنا 33.33 باپ شریک بھائی کو دیا۔
Similarly, what remains from a full sister's share is for the consanguine brother and sister: for the male the share of two females. If there is a full sister, she takes half. The remainder is for the consanguine siblings: the male takes double the female. The evidence is the verse: 'They ask you for a ruling; say: Allah gives you a ruling concerning the kalalah: if a man dies and has no child, and he has a sister, she gets half of what he leaves.' (Qur'an 4:176). And the athar: 'If there is a male with the daughters of the father, they have no prescribed share; start with the people of fixed shares and give them their shares; if there remains a surplus, it is between the children of the father, with the male taking the share of two females.'  Example: Estate 100, full sister takes 50, consanguine brother takes 33.33, consanguine sister takes 16.66.

Commentary
This passage explains the division when the deceased leaves a full sister (uterine sister) and consanguine siblings (father's side). The full sister takes her fixed share of half (Quranic). The remaining half goes to the consanguine siblings as residuary heirs, with the consanguine brother taking twice the consanguine sister. The proof is from Qur'an 4:176 for the full sister, and an athar for the consanguine siblings' residue. The example distributes an estate of 100: full sister gets 50, consanguine sister gets 16.66, consanguine brother gets 33.33.

Inheritance of a Person with Dual Relationship as Paternal Cousin and Maternal Brother
Ruling with proof on dual inheritance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares when a paternal cousin is also a maternal brother, applying the principle that a person inherits through each of his relationships independently.

Core Idea
A person inherits through each relationship: first as a Quranic sharer, then as a residuary heir.

This case illustrates a unique scenario where one heir combines two distinct relationships to the deceased: he is both a paternal cousin (asabah) and a maternal brother (Quranic sharer). The Hanafi ruling gives him both shares sequentially. The evidence includes a Quranic verse and a narration from Ali and Zaid. Understanding this case is essential for correctly distributing estates when multiple relationships converge.

Guided Path
1
Identify all surviving heirs and their relationships
List the heirs: two paternal cousins. Note that one of them is also a maternal brother. Recognize that he has a dual relationship.
In Hanafi law, dual relationships allow separate inheritance from each.
2
Apply hajb (exclusion) if any
In this case, no heir is entirely excluded. The maternal brother is a Quranic sharer, and both paternal cousins are residuary heirs.
Hajb hirman does not apply because there is no heir who blocks another completely.
3
Assign Quranic shares (fard) first
The maternal brother is entitled to 1/6 of the estate. This is based on Quran 4:12 for siblings in kalalah. No other Quranic sharers exist.
The maternal brother's share is fard (fixed).
4
Distribute the remainder as asabah
After deducting the maternal brother's 1/6, the remaining 5/6 is divided equally between the two paternal cousins as residuary heirs. Both are at the same degree of relationship to the deceased.
The paternal cousins are asabah (agnatic heirs) and inherit by ta'sib.
5
Verify the shares and calculate the base number
Express shares with a common denominator: maternal brother = 2/12, each paternal cousin = 5/12. The sum is 12/12. The base number is 12.
No adjustment like awl or radd is needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۲۲۷] (۶) کسی نے چھوڑے دو چازاد بھائی، ان میں سے ایک ماں شریک بھائی ہے تو ان کے لئے چھٹا حصہ ہوگا۔ اور باقی دونوں کے درمیان آدھا آدھا ہوگا۔ یہ مسئلہ اس اصول ہر ہے کہ ایک آدمی کی دو قرابتیں ہوں تو دونوں قرابتوں کے الگ الگ حصے ملیں گے۔ ایک آدمی نے دو چازاد بھائی چھوڑے۔ ایک چازاد بھائی اس کا ماں شریک بھائی بھی ہوتا تھا، کیونکہ اس کی ماں نے چچا سے شادی کی تھی تو ماں شریک بھائی کو اخیافی بھائی کا چھٹا 16.66 حصہ پہلے ملے گا۔ پھر جو 83.33 باقی رہے گا اس کو دونوں بھائی بطور عصبہ کے آدھا آدھا تقسیم کریں گے۔ ماں شریک بھائی کو چھٹا حصہ ملنے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ وان كان رجل يورث كلالة او امرأة وله اخ او اخت فلكل واحد منهما السندس (الف) ( آیت ۱۲ سورۃ النساء۴) اس آیت میں ایک ماں شریک بھائی کو چھٹا حصہ دیا گیا ہے (۲) اور چچازاد بھائیوں کے در میان باقی مال طور عصبہ آدھا آدھا ہو گا اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ كـان عـلـی وزیـد يـقـولان في بني عم احدهم اخ لام يعطيانه السدس ومـا بـقـى بينه وبين بني عمه وكان عبد الله يعطيه المال كله (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شبیہ ، افی بنی عم احد هم اخ الام ، ج سادس ص ۲۴۶، نمبر۳۱۰۷۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ پہلے ماں شریک بھائی کو چھٹا حصہ دیا جائے گا۔ اس کے بعد دونوں میں آدھا آدھا تقسیم کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ دونوں برابر درجے کے عصبہ ہیں۔ مسئلہ اس طرح ہوگا۔ حاشیہ : (الف) اگر سوتیلی بہن کے ساتھ بھائی ہو تو ان کے لئے باضابطہ حصہ نہیں ہے۔ البتہ پہلے حصے والوں کو حصے دیئے جائیں۔ اگر اس سے بچ جائے تو بھائی بہن کے لئے ہوگا، مرد کو عورت کے دوگنے کے اصول پر (ب) اگر کوئی مرد یا عورت کلالہ ہو اور اس کے بھائی یا بہن ہو تو ہر ایک کے لئے چھٹا چھنا ہو گا (ج) حضرت علی اور زید فرماتے ہیں کہ چچا زاد بھائی ماں شریک بھائی بھی ہے تو اس کو چھٹا دیا جائے گا۔ اور جو باقی رہا تو اس کو اور دوسرے چچا زاد بھائی کے درمیان ہوگا ۔ اور حضرت عبد اللہ تو اس ماں شریک بھائی کو پورا ہی مال دیتے تھے۔
If someone leaves two paternal cousins, and one of them is a maternal brother, then that maternal brother gets one-sixth, and the remainder is divided equally between them. This case is based on the principle that when a person has two relationships, he receives shares from both. One man left two paternal cousins; one of them was also his maternal brother because his mother married his uncle. So the maternal brother first receives 1/6 as a maternal brother (16.66), then the remaining 83.33 is divided equally between both as residuary heirs. The evidence for the maternal brother's sixth is the verse: 'If a man or woman dies and has a brother or sister, each of them gets one-sixth' (Qur'an 4:12). The evidence for equal division between the two paternal cousins is the athar: 'Ali and Zaid used to say, regarding two paternal cousins, one of whom is a maternal brother, they give the maternal brother his sixth, and the remainder is between him and his cousin.' Abdullah used to give all the property to the maternal brother.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage addresses a unique case where one person combines two relationships: he is both a paternal cousin and a maternal brother of the deceased. The ruling is that he inherits in both capacities: first as a maternal brother, taking 1/6 (Quranic), and then as a paternal cousin, sharing the remainder as residuary heirs equally with the other cousin. The example illustrates: from 100, the maternal brother first takes 16.66 (1/6), then the remaining 83.33 is divided equally (41.665 each) between the two paternal cousins. The evidence includes Quran 4:12 for the maternal share and an athar from Ali and Zaid for the residuary division. The footnotes provide additional context, including a dissenting view from Abdullah who gave all property to the maternal brother.

Key Terms
چازاد بھائی (chazad bhai): Paternal cousin (son of paternal uncle).
ماں شریک بھائی (maan shareek bhai): Maternal brother (same mother, different father).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Quran 4:12
B) The athar of Ali and Zaid
C) Ijma of the Companions
D) Qiyas on full siblings

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi inheritance, a person who is both a maternal brother and a paternal cousin receives 1/6 as a Quranic sharer and then shares the remainder as a residuary heir.

The Musharrakah Case: Full Brothers Excluded as 'Asabah
Definition and Hanafi ruling of Musharrakah with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the Musharrakah case, derive it from Quranic verses, and explain the Shafi'i counter-argument and its practical consequence.

Core Idea
Fixed shares consume the entire estate, leaving nothing for 'asabah — full brothers are excluded.

In inheritance, some cases seem unfair at first glance. The Musharrakah case is one such: a woman leaves her husband, mother, several half-brothers from her mother, and her full brothers. Intuitively, full brothers should inherit something, but the Hanafi school rules they receive nothing. Why? Because the fixed shares assigned by the Quran add up to the whole estate, leaving no residue for the 'asabah (residuary heirs). The Shafi'i school disagrees, arguing that full brothers should share the one-third share of the uterine siblings. This lesson examines both positions and the evidence behind them.

Guided Path
1
Define the Musharrakah case
Identify the surviving heirs: husband, mother (or grandmother), several uterine half-brothers (ikhwa li-umm), and full brothers (ikhwa li-abb wa umm). Note that there is no child of the deceased.
The case is also called 'shared' because it involves different types of brothers.
2
List the Quranic fixed shares
Apply the Quranic verses: husband gets 1/2 (Surah al-Nisa 4:12), mother gets 1/6 (4:11, because there are brothers), and uterine siblings get 1/3 collectively if more than one (4:12). Calculate the total: 1/2 + 1/6 + 1/3 = 1 (the whole estate).
The shares are derived from clear Quranic texts, but the interpretation of which brothers are meant in 4:11 is disputed.
3
Analyze the status of full brothers
Full brothers are 'asabah bi-nafsih (residuaries by themselves). They inherit only if something remains after the fixed shares. Since the fixed shares total 1, there is no residue, so they are excluded (mahjub).
This is the Hanafi position. The full brothers are excluded not because they are distant, but because the estate is fully allocated.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that full brothers are closer to the deceased than uterine brothers (they share both parents), so when uterine brothers receive a share, full brothers should also participate in that share. He cites athar from Shuraih, Masruq, and 'Uthman who included them.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that under Shafi'i law, the one-third share is divided equally among uterine and full brothers.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the literal allocation of the Quranic shares leaving no residue, and on the athar from 'Ali that full brothers are excluded. The athar from 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud initially included them, but the Hanafi school follows 'Ali's view as more consistent with the Quranic sums.
The relied-upon fatwa in the Hanafi school is that full brothers get nothing in this case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

اس مسئلے میں سو میں سے پہلے اخیافی بھائی کو چھٹا یعنی 16.66 دیا۔ اور باقی 83.33 دونوں بھائیوں میں آدھا آدھا تقسیم کیا تو دونوں کو
41.66 ملا۔ اس لئے ماں شریک بھائی کو دونوں کا مجموعہ 58.33 ہوا۔
[۳۲۲۸) (۷) مشترکہ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ عورت شوہر، ماں یا دادی اور کئی ماں شریک بھائی اور حقیقی بھائی چھوڑے تو شوہر کے لئے آدھا ہوگا اور ماں کے لئے چھٹا اور ماں شریک اولاد کے لئے تہائی اور حقیقی بھائیوں کے لئے کچھ نہیں ہوگا۔
یہ مسئلہ مشترکہ ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں کئی قسم کے بھائی ہیں۔ اور ماں اور دادی کا مسئلہ بھی ہے۔ اس لئے اس مسئلے کو مشترکہ کہتے ہیں۔ مسئلے کی تشریح اس طرح ہے۔ عورت نے (۱) شوہر ، (۲) ماں (۳) ماں شریک کئی بھائی (۴) اور ماں باپ شریک بھائی چھوڑے۔ ایسی صورت میں آیت قرآن کے مطابق شوہر کو آدھا ملے گا۔ کیونکہ میت کی اولاد نہیں ہے۔ ولکم نصف ماترک ازواجكم ان لم يكن لهن ولد (الف) ( آیت ۱۲، سورۃ النساء ) اور ماں کے لئے چھٹا ہوگا ۔ آیت میں ہے۔ فان لم یکن له ولد وورثه ابواه فلامه الثلث فان كان له اخوة فلامه السدس (ب) ( آیت ا ،سورة النساء) یہاں کئی بھائی ہیں اس لئے ماں کو چھٹا حصہ دیا جائے گا۔ اور ماں شریک کئی بھائیوں کو تہائی ملے گی۔ کیونکہ آیت میں ہے۔ وان کان رجل يورث كلالة او امرأة وله اخ او اخت فلكل واحد منهما السدس فان كانوا أكثر من ذلك فهم شركاء في الثلث ( ج ) ( آیت ۱۲ ، سورۃ النساء ۴ ) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک سے زیادہ ماں شریک بھائی یا بہن ہوں تو ان کو پورے مال کی تہائی ملے گی۔ اس اعتبار سے سب حصے پورے ہو گئے اور حقیقی بھائیوں کو بطور عصبہ دینے کے لئے کچھ نہیں رہا اس لئے وہ محروم ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ شوہر کو آدھا 50 ملا۔ ماں کو چھٹا 16.66 ملا۔ اور ماں شریک بھائیوں کو تہائی 33.33 ملا۔ سب مل کر سو 100 ہو گیا۔
حاشیہ : (الف) تمہارے لئے آدھا ہے اس میں سے جو تمہاری بیویوں نے چھوڑا۔ اگر ان کی اولاد نہ ہو ( ب ) اگر لڑکے کو اولاد نہ ہو اور ماں باپ وارث ہوں تو اس کی ماں کے لئے تہائی ہے۔ اور اگرمیت کو بھائی ہو تو ماں کے لئے چھٹا ہے (ج) اگر مرد اور عورت کلالہ ہو اور ان کے بھائی بہن ہوں تو ان میں سے ہر ایک کو چھٹا ملے گا۔ اور ان سے زیادہ ہوں تو وہ تہائی میں شریک ہوں گے۔

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الرابع
وام فللزوج النصف وللام السدس ولاولاد الام الثلث ولا شيء للاخوة للاب والام یہاں ماں باپ شریک بھائی اگر چہ میت کے بہت قریب ہیں۔ لیکن وہ عصبہ ہیں اس لئے حصے داروں کے حصے کے بعد بچے گا تب لیں گے۔ اور یہاں کچھ بچا نہیں اس لئے ان کو کچھ نہیں ملے گا (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابراهيــم قــال كــان عبد اللـه وعـمـر يشر كان قال وكان على لا يشرك قال ابوبكر وهذه من سنة اسهم للزوج النصف ثلاثة اسهم وللام السدس وللاخوة من الام الثلث وهو سهمان (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی شيبه ، ۱۷ ، فی زوج وام واخوة واخوات لاب وابن واخوة لام من شرک ینهم ، ج سادس ،ص ۲۴۹ نمبر ۳۱۰۹۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ مسئلہ چھ سے بنائیں۔ اس میں سے آدھا تین حصے شوہر کو دیں۔ اور چھٹا حصہ یعنی چھ میں سے ایک حصہ ماں کو دیں۔ اور ایک تہائی یعنی چھ میں سے دو حصے ماں شریک بھائیوں کو دیں۔ اس سے چھ حصے پورے ہو گئے۔ اس لئے ماں باپ شریک بھائیوں کو کچھ نہیں ملے گا۔ مسئلہ اس طرح ہوگا۔

امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ ماں باپ شریک بھائی ماں شریک بھائی سے زیادہ قریب ہیں اس لئے جب ماں شریک بھائی کو حصہ ملا تو ان کو بھی اس کی تنہائی میں شریک کرنا چاہئے۔
اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن شريح و مسروق انهما شركا الاخوة من الاب والام مع الاخوة من الام. اور دوسرى روایت میں ہے۔ ان عثمان شرک بينهم (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبہ ۔ کافی زوج وام واخوة واخوات لاب وابن واخوة لام من شرک بینھم ، ج سادس ،ص ۲۴۹، نمبر ۳۱۰۹۲ /۳۱۰۹۱ ر سنن الدارمی ، باب فی مشرکة ، ج ثانی ، ص ۴۴۶ ، نمبر ۲۸۸۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ حقیقی بھائی ماں شریک بھائی کے حصے میں شریک ہوں گے۔ مسئلہ اس طرح بنے گا۔

Chapter of Exclusion [3228 (7)] The Musharrakah is that a woman leaves behind a husband, a mother or grandmother, a half-brother from the mother and a brother from the father. 
Deceased: 100
Half-brother (mother's side), Cousin brother (paternal uncle's son)
41.66
83.33
16.66
+
41.66
58.32
In this matter, out of 100, first the half-brother (maternal) was given one-sixth i.e. 16.66. And the remaining 83.33 was divided equally between the two brothers, so each got 41.66. Therefore the half-brother (maternal) gets a total of 58.33. [3228 (7)] The Musharrakah case is that a woman leaves behind a husband, a mother or grandmother, and several half-brothers from the mother and full brothers; then the husband gets half, the mother gets one-sixth, the half-brothers from the mother get one-third, and the full brothers get nothing. This case is called 'Musharrakah' because there are several types of brothers, and also the case of mother and grandmother. So it is called shared. The explanation of the case is as follows: The woman leaves (1) husband, (2) mother, (3) several half-brothers from the mother, and (4) full brothers (from both parents). In such a case, according to the Quranic verse, the husband gets half, because the deceased has no children: 'And for you half of what your wives leave if they have no child' (Surah al-Nisa, verse 12). And the mother gets one-sixth. The verse says: 'But if he has no child and his parents are his heirs, then to his mother is one-third. But if he has brothers, then to his mother is one-sixth' (Surah al-Nisa, verse 11). Here there are brothers, so the mother gets one-sixth. And the several half-brothers from the mother get one-third, because the verse says: 'If a man or a woman dies leaving no children but has a brother or sister, each of them gets one-sixth. But if they are more than that, they are sharers in the one-third' (Surah al-Nisa, verse 12). From this verse it is clear that if there are more than one half-brother or half-sister from the mother, they get one-third of the entire estate. Based on this, all shares are fulfilled, and nothing remains to give to the full brothers as residuaries, so they are excluded because the husband gets half (50), the mother gets one-sixth (16.66), and the half-brothers from the mother get one-third (33.33); together they make 100. Commentary notes: (a) 'For you half of what your wives leave if they have no child.' (b) 'If the deceased has no child and his parents are heirs, then for his mother one-third; but if he has brothers, then for his mother one-sixth.' (c) 'If a man or woman dies as kalala and has a brother or sister, each gets one-sixth; if there are more, they share in one-third.' 
Page 433: Chapter of Exclusion. Al-Sharh al-Thamiri vol. 4: 'And for the husband half, for the mother one-sixth, for the children of the mother one-third, and nothing for the full brothers.' Here, the full brothers, although they are very close to the deceased, are residuaries, so they take only after the shares of the sharers if something remains. And here nothing remains, so they get nothing. (2) There is proof in the athar: From Ibrahim: 'Abdullah and Umar used to include them (the full brothers with the maternal brothers), and Ali did not include them. Abu Bakr said: This is a sunnah. Assign to the husband half (3 shares), to the mother one-sixth, and to the half-brothers from the mother one-third (2 shares)' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 17, fi zawj wa umm wa ikhwa wa akhawat li-ab wa ibn wa ikhwa li-umm min shurak, vol. 6, p. 249, no. 31096). In this athar, the case is built on 6: give half (3 shares) to the husband, one-sixth (1 share) to the mother, and one-third (2 shares) to the half-brothers from the mother. This uses all 6 shares, so full brothers get nothing. The case becomes: Deceased 100 - Husband 50, Mother 16.66, Several half-brothers (maternal) 33.33, Full brothers X (0). Imam Shafi'i says that full brothers are closer than half-brothers from the mother, so when the half-brothers from the mother get a share, the full brothers should be included with them in that share. There is proof in the athar: From Shuraih and Masruq that they included the full brothers with the half-brothers from the mother. And in another narration: 'Uthman included them together' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, fi zawj wa umm wa ikhwa wa akhawat li-ab wa ibn wa ikhwa li-umm min shurak, vol. 6, p. 249, no. 31092/31091; Sunan al-Darimi, bab fi mushraka, vol. 2, p. 446, no. 2882). From this athar, it is established that full brothers share in the share of half-brothers from the mother. The case becomes: Deceased 100 - Husband 50, Grandmother 16.66, Several maternal half-brothers 16.66, Several full brothers 16.66.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage explains the Musharrakah (shared) case in inheritance law. The author first defines the scenario: a woman dies leaving a husband, a mother (or grandmother), several half-brothers from the mother (uterine brothers), and full brothers (german brothers). The Hanafi ruling is that the husband takes half, the mother takes one-sixth, the uterine brothers take one-third collectively, and the full brothers receive nothing because there is no residue left after these fixed shares. The author provides Quranic evidence for each share: the husband's half from Surah al-Nisa 4:12, the mother's sixth from 4:11 (since there are brothers, she gets one-sixth instead of one-third), and the uterine brothers' third from 4:12. The full brothers are 'asabah (residuaries), but as the fixed shares consume the entire estate, they are excluded (mahjub). The author then cites an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i reporting that 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and 'Umar ibn al-Khattab used to include the full brothers with the uterine brothers in the one-third, while 'Ali did not. Abu Bakr (likely al-Siddiq or another) said it is a sunnah to give the shares as described. This shows an early difference. The passage then presents the Shafi'i position: Imam al-Shafi'i argues that full brothers are closer to the deceased than uterine brothers, so when uterine brothers receive a share, full brothers should also participate in that one-third. He cites athar from Shuraih, Masruq, and 'Uthman where they included full brothers with uterine brothers. The Hanafi school, however, adheres to the ruling that full brothers are excluded because they are residuaries and no residue remains. The author includes a calculation showing how the shares add up to 100%, leaving nothing for the full brothers. This lesson illustrates how different proofs (Quranic verses, athar of Companions, and qiyas) lead to ikhtilaf between the schools. The operative Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is that full brothers are excluded in this case.

Key Terms
مشترکہ (musharrakah): A specific inheritance case where a woman leaves husband, mother/grandmother, uterine siblings, and full siblings; full siblings are excluded.
حجب (hajb): Exclusion from inheritance due to the presence of a stronger heir or because the estate is consumed by fixed shares.
عصبة (asabah): Residuary heirs who take whatever remains after the fixed shares (ashab al-faraid).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Musharrakah case, according to the Hanafi school, what is the share of the full brothers?
A) One-third divided equally with uterine brothers.
B) One-sixth each.
C) Nothing (excluded).
D) Half of the estate.

Key Takeaway
In the Musharrakah case, full brothers are excluded because the fixed shares from the Quran exhaust the estate, leaving no residue for 'asabah.

Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate
8 min
The Hanafi Ruling in the Musharrakah Case
Inheritance case with exclusions and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares in the Musharrakah case following the Hanafi school and identify the type of exclusion (hajb) that applies to full brothers.

Core Idea
Full brothers are totally excluded when prescribed shares consume the entire estate.

In this lesson, we examine the Musharrakah case, a classic inheritance scenario where full brothers unexpectedly receive nothing. We will work through the calculation step by step and understand why the Hanafi school rules this way, supported by athar from the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Heirs and Their Categories
List all surviving heirs: husband (fard), mother (fard), uterine brothers (fard), full brothers (asabah).
Asabah heirs only inherit after prescribed shares are paid.
2
Determine the Asabah's Condition
Full brothers are asabah; they take residue only if any remains after assigning prescribed shares.
3
Calculate the Prescribed Shares (Base 6)
Husband: 1/2 = 3/6. Mother: 1/6 = 1/6. Uterine brothers: 1/3 = 2/6.
LCM of denominators 2,6,3 is 6.
4
Sum the Shares
Total = 3+1+2 = 6/6. The estate is fully consumed.
5
Conclude on Full Brothers
Since no residue remains, full brothers are totally excluded (hajb hirman). They take nothing.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) ruling in the Hanafi school.

حاشیه : (الف) حضرت ابراہیم فرماتے ہیں کہ عبداللہ اور حضرت عمر حقیقی بھائی کو ماں شریک بھائی کے حصے میں شریک کرتے تھے۔ اور حضرت علی نشریک نہیں کرتے تھے۔ حضرت ابو بکڑ نے فرمایا یہ مسئلہ چھ حصوں سے ہوگا۔ شوہر کے لئے آدھا جو تین حصے ہوئے۔ اور ماں کے لئے چھٹا اور ماں شریک بھائیوں کے لئے تہائی جو چھ میں سے دو حصے ہوں گے ( اور حقیقی بھائیوں کے لئے کچھ نہیں بچے گا ) (ب) حضرت شریح اور مسروق حقیقی بھائیوں کو ماں شریک بھائیوں کے ساتھ (باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )
اس مسئلے میں اخیافی بھائیوں کو جو تہائی 33.33 ملی تھی اس میں سے آدھا حقیقی بھائی کو دیا۔ جس کی وجہ سے دونوں کو 16.66 اور اخیافی بھائیوں کو 16.66 مل گیا۔ المشتر کہ : اس مسئلے کو مشترکہ مسئلہ کہتے ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ حقیقی بھائی انکار کر دیئے جاتے ہیں اور کبھی شریک کئے جاتے ہیں۔ ایک عبارت میں المشرکہ ہے، اس کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ بعض حجرات نے حقیقی بھائی کو ماں شریک بھائی کے حصے میں شریک فرمایا اور بعض حضرات نے شریک نہیں فرمایا۔
( حجب نقصان ایک نظر میں اور حجب حرمان ایک نظر میں اگلے صفحات پر دیکھئے )
حاشیہ شریک کرتے تھے اور حضرت عثمان نے حقیقی بھائی کو ماں شریک بھائی کے ساتھ شریک کیا۔
Chapter of Exclusion. And the wife: for the husband half, for the mother one-sixth, for the children of the mother one-third, and nothing for the full brothers (through father and mother). Here, the full brothers, even if very close to the deceased, are asabah; therefore they take only after the shares of the share-holders, if anything remains. And here nothing remains, so they get nothing. (2) Proof of this in an athar: from Ibrahim, he said: Abdullah and Umar used to include (the full brothers), but Ali did not include. Abu Bakr said: This is a sunna: for the husband three shares (half), for the mother one-sixth, and for the uterine brothers one-third, which is two shares. (a) (Ibn Abi Shayba, Musannaf, 17, fi zawj wa amm wa ikhwa li ab...). In this athar, the case is built on six. Of that, half (three shares) to the husband, one-sixth (one share) to the mother, and one-third (two shares) to the uterine brothers. Thus all six shares are used. Therefore the full brothers get nothing. The calculation is as follows: Deceased 100; Husband; Mother; Several uterine brothers; Several full brothers: X – 33.33, 16.66, 50. Imam al-Shafi'i says: The full brothers are closer than the uterine brothers, so when uterine brothers receive a share, the full brothers should share with them in that portion. Proof in an athar: from Shuraih and Masruq that they included the full brothers with the uterine brothers. And in another narration: that Uthman included them together (b) (Ibn Abi Shayba, Musannaf...; Sunan al-Darimi). From this athar it appears that full brothers share in the uterine brothers' share. The calculation: Several full brothers: 16.66; 33.33; Deceased 100; Husband; Grandmother; Several uterine brothers: 16.66; 16.66; 50. Footnote: (a) Ibrahim said: Abdullah and Umar used to include the full brother with the uterine brother, and Ali did not. Abu Bakr said: This case will be from six shares: husband half (three), mother one-sixth, uterine brothers one-third (two), and nothing remains for full brothers. (b) Shuraih and Masruq included full brothers with uterine brothers (rest on next page). In this case, from the one-third (33.33) given to the uterine brothers, half was given to full brothers, so both get 16.66 each. Al-Musharrakah: This case is called the Musharrakah issue because full brothers are sometimes excluded and sometimes included. In one phrase 'al-musharrikah' means that some scholars included the full brother in the uterine brother's share and some did not. (See notes on hajb nuqsan and hajb hirman on following pages. Footnote: They used to include, and Uthman included full brother with uterine brother.)
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Samarqandi deals with the famous inheritance case known as 'al-Musharrakah' (also 'al-Musharikah'). The scenario: a deceased woman leaves a husband, a mother, several uterine brothers (same mother), and several full brothers (same father and mother). The passage first states the Hanafi ruling: the husband gets 1/2, the mother gets 1/6, the uterine brothers get 1/3 collectively, and the full brothers receive nothing. The justification is that full brothers are asabah (residuary heirs) and take only after the prescribed shares are distributed; but here the estate is fully consumed by the three fixed shares (1/2 + 1/6 + 1/3 = 1), so nothing remains for them. This ruling is supported by an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, who reports that Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and Umar used to include the full brothers (i.e., give them a share), but Ali did not, and Abu Bakr explained the calculation on the basis of six shares. The passage then presents the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues that full brothers are closer relatives than uterine brothers, so they should share in the uterine brothers' third. He supports this with athar from Shuraih, Masruq, and Caliph Uthman, who all included full brothers with uterine brothers. The passage then shows the Shafi'i calculation: the 1/3 share is divided equally between uterine and full brothers, resulting in 16.66 for each group (assuming one full brother and one uterine brother, or multiple brothers sharing equally). The term 'Musharrakah' is explained: it refers to the fact that full brothers are sometimes excluded (as in the Hanafi position) and sometimes included (as in the Shafi'i position). The passage concludes by noting that this is a well-known disputed issue, and the Hanafi school adheres to the exclusion of full brothers, which is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).

Key Terms
حجب (ḥajb): Exclusion from inheritance, either total (ḥirmān) or partial (nuqṣān).
مشرکہ (musharrakah): The inheritance case where full brothers are sometimes included with uterine brothers in the 1/3 share.
اخیافی (akhyāfī): Uterine brother (same mother, different father).
حقیقی (ḥaqīqī): Full brother (same father and mother).
عصبہ (ʿaṣabah): Residuary heir(s) who take the remainder after prescribed shares are distributed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what do full brothers inherit in the Musharrakah case (deceased leaving husband, mother, uterine brothers, and full brothers)?
A) They share equally with uterine brothers in the 1/3.
B) They receive 1/6 of the estate.
C) They receive nothing because the estate is fully consumed.
D) They receive the residue after all other shares.

Key Takeaway
Full brothers are totally excluded in the Musharrakah case when the estate is fully consumed by the shares of husband, mother, and uterine brothers.
